O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, dear children, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine, its fulfillment, and have finished it through its explanations and statements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with this treatise, which is the beginning of the work of hands, namely "surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work of hands is treated differently in our region and is strange to all, the science is lost and cut off, and there is nothing left from its roots except for small descriptions in books by the ancients about what the hands have done.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed, and knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	I believe I want to revive it by organizing this treatise according to the method of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will bring together the shapes of cautery instruments and other tools for the work with their appropriate adjustments, as needed.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has languished.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who wishes to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, must know the judgment of the members, their shapes and connections, and the separations of parts; he should have knowledge of bones, nerves, blood vessels, and the number of organs, and understand the functions of moving and resting veins.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And Hippocrates says that the name without meaning is empty, and the work with it is little.
et meismement en l’art de main.	and especially in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, will surely fall into error and harm others.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	since I have often seen many of those who undertake this science and abandon themselves without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I have seen a foolish craze that seizes the scrotum or neck of a woman and affects the arteries of the neck.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood comes out that the woman dies in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And see another wonder where a stone is treated from a man's eye, and the stone was large.
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	if it carries with it a piece of the bladder, and he was bitten inside three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him; I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and if it were not removed, he would surely die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And see another wonder where he took care of a duke from our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound.
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the ignorant doctors tighten the break on the wound as if by strong force, and leave no room for the wound to heal, and they leave it thus at the end.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commands that he does not dislocate it at all;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and waits until the leg is completely swollen and sore, and it comes to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I am called to come to him, and I hasten to go and dislocate the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I saw it dislocated, it was at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But any attempt to correct it was already confirmed as corrupted or the member could not be healed.
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and does not cease the corruption of pain through the member until the limb is completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I also saw another wonder: the abscess became worse, and then it was inflamed due to the evil nature of its mastery.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the chancre, when it is free of melancholic humor, one should not use iron to treat it unless it is in a part that can be entirely removed, so as to eliminate what is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this reason, gentle reader, it is necessary that you know that the art of healing is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, work where there is danger in many ways;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show, in each part of this book, where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For this reason, it is important for you to guard yourself, so that the foolish eye cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take up your weapons in courage, and approach your sick gently yet firmly, and use the best method, through the grace of God, you will come to salvation and be saved.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and let go of the fearful diseases of sorrow, healthily.
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and remove your weapons of doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other, gloriously.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen does not speak in any of his warnings:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take any ill disease too much to heart, unless you are called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are about fire cautery and the use of harsh medicines, and they are ordered from the head down to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and the shapes of instruments, the tools for cautery, and everything necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter deals with cutting and piercing, and the use of suckers and incisions, and treating wounds, and extracting arrows, and similar procedures.
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and it describes the chapters arranged and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar conditions.
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is ordered from the greatest pain down to minor discomfort, and describes the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, remembering the work, it is necessary that I mention the quality of the aid and the harm of each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of help, and its harmful effects, are the longest discourse and most subtle science, and secret answers.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and about these things, many of the wise spoke, and agreed upon this.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and I will be satisfied with few of my words, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that fire cautery universally helps every complexion where it has substance, whether it be of two complexes.
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	This is to know: a hot complexion with material cause, and a dry complexion with material cause.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry complexion, combining material causes, they devised something and said that fire treatment is great aid.
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the other ones said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that fire treatment is not useful for a disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	Because nature of fire is hot, and it should not be treated with heat for a disease caused by heat, nor by dryness.
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and he who does the opposite of cautery provides great help for hot and dry disease that comes upon the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and its moisture with the heat of fire, you perceive that the flesh is fresh.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in every case, no one should intervene unless they have tested it themselves, and who knows through long experience the chapter of cautery, and the diversity of the constitutions of men, and their dispositions and the causes of their illnesses, and the time and space.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	we have no fear, especially of cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all agreed and were convinced about the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, child, that cautery joins fire, which is a secret of healing, and indeed it is much gentler than burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and brings no harm but to the member that is afflicted, and does not affect any other member.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Burning medicines pass from one part to another by separation, and bring to the member painful diseases with no healing.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and perhaps the patient recovers.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	He does not waste it for its nobility and the goodness of its nature, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found by experience and through the length of service and study that I have devoted to the art, and it was about the truth of things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and therefore I excuse the length of my words, for I do not like to deprive you of the secret that is hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives diseases from the body, as the philosopher demonstrates.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	or consider it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know this, my son, that there is agreement among them as to when cauterization should be performed and the appropriate tools chosen.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harmful substances causing pain are removed by the help of cautery.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and indeed, cautery itself is necessary for pains that cannot wait for the time when greater harm does not come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think, dear child, as do the foolish people;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the illness that is cured by cautery has no recurrence;
et il le dient ensi;	and thus it is done;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not at all as they should take care, because cautery is only a remedy that alters the complexion, dries up the humors that cause pain, and acts more quickly than other medicines because of its virtue and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible for the illness to come, sometimes according to the temperament of the patient and the place where the illness resides and its nature.
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and in him are accumulated excesses through the acquisition of meats and similar things, unless cautery is administered to remove these excesses and moisture, as with cautery for pain and similar conditions, and such pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	but this rarely happens.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand at all why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and it is indeed so.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cautery is valid after medicine; their intentions are false, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we administer treatments in any disease and they do not work, then let us use cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it becomes clear that cautery is indeed the last of medicine, not according to the opinions of ignorant people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that gold cautery instruments are better than iron ones, and they did not consider fire to be hot enough except for the quality of gold and the high value of its substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the fire of cautery does not cause putrefaction, but this is not true, as I have tested it, and I have found that it is indeed harmful to no men.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and fire cautery is more valuable than metal, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	However, when you heat gold instruments, you are not sure if they are heated through due to the color of the gold, and once heated, they quickly cool down.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if they are heated too much;
si font au feu;	they turn black from the fire.
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus, there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cautery because we have made it suitable for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	You have ordered this chapter from the beginning to the end, so that the path may be lighter to follow.
dou cautere olivaire	Oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Fire cautery is useful for moisture and cold on the head, and it is effective in cases of disease called "soda", and due to many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for numerous dreams, toothaches, throat pains, and especially in all diseases caused by cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar ailments.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged by a solvent medicine that cleanses the third or fourth (nerve) channel, according to the virtue and age, and the habituation of the patient to pain.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make the patient's head comfortable.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	and then make the patient lie with their head between your hands, and place their hands on some weight.
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	after that, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes.
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and when your two tools have come, take the blood from the wound and heat the cautery called "olive" (olivare), of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	and place the sign (or mark) of ink on the dislocated joint, and move your hand down and pull it in, repeatedly disturbing it.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then gently release your hand, and if you see the bone move slightly,
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it move, repeat the cautery until you can see the bone as I have told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	After taking a little silk thread, wrap it around and make it soft cotton, place it on the wound, and leave it for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After that, place the moist cotton on it.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave it until the burning is gone.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterward, treat the wound with the dressing called "tetrarmation" as long as it remains healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purifies itself.
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason, help is sought.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one must not leave the cautery so long that the bone is burned, and then remove what is burned from the bone, and it will heal.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And he should be told to leave the cautery alone and press so hard against the bone that it opens as wide as women do when they give birth so that the humors can escape.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and the wound should remain open for a long time.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	After the operation, one must cure and dress.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in every way, except for those who have no other choice.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I must leave this;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the tissue is weakened by continuous solutions of moisture, as we testify in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and also when the joint of the patient is weak by nature, and the initial appearance of cautery is safer and more mobile for me, from which I derive great benefit.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When chronic pain persists for a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie", as well as purgatives for the head and eyes, and poultices.
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one performs the cautery as we have said above, it is ineffective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Beware that the patient's joint is of strong nature, and that it is not too sharp.
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Then cauterize deeply, as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After that, cauterize each corn of the shoulder just below the bone, as we have said above, and cauterize the one called "vasselz".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and hold the limbs where vents (suction cups) are placed.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and gently hold the hand so that you do not see the bone.
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	The sick person feels too much great pain in this cautery more than in others, and I will speak of that later.
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the cautery of the horns be more subtle than that which cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is its form:
dou cautere dou chief	For fire cautery, instruct the patient
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When there is sudden pain in a part of the head and the illness extends to the oil (or possibly referring to swelling or inflammation), and the condition is purged with various medications, and other treatments as I have mentioned in the division of illnesses, and none of these help:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Then he performs cauterization according to two manners, that is to say, with hot medicated herbs and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	He performs cauterization with hot medicated herbs if he presses a sweet almond, removes the skin and wraps it in cloth, then makes an incision at the site of the pain in such a way that you can reposition the almond under the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is repositioned, if he holds it well and tightens it, leaving it that way for twelve hours.
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then free it and treat with honey for the wound, leaving it thus for two or three days.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then place a cotton cloth soaked in butter over the wound until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment, as long as it is healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you find yourself in need of any of the burning medications that I have written about or the proper treatment of burning medications.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the fire cautery with this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because the head is shaped like a clasp where there is a little curve, and has a small appearance.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful joint, hold your hand and gently turn it, until half of the thickness of the heart is burned.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and let go of your hand so the artery does not burn, which is depleted, and allows abundant blood to flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After applying cotton wrapped in string, place it on the joint for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then I cover it with moistened butter, and then treat the wound of the limb until it is healed;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare" (scalpel), be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine that is not ancient.
de emigraine	migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migraine as we have previously said in the divisions of illnesses, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cautery mentioned above (scalpel) is dirty and does not serve its purpose, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and thus, by the joint that causes pain, draw a line half as long as a finger, and once your hand is in place, hold it so you do not touch the artery and do not go past the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and guard the jaw that stops when chewing, so the nerves are only focused on the quiet and no spasms come to the patient, and beware of blood flow from the artery once it is cut, as cutting it carries great fear and especially for one who does not know how, or has no experience.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the wound halfway healed;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to retain blood when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it clots in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery is not sufficient for the illness, and the patient suffers, cauterize both joints as we have said, and treat the wound until it is clean.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said in this chapter for the extraction of the artery, using a cauterization tool with two blades.
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this is the best cautery of them all and most helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	about the pain of ears due to cold.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ear due to cold, and various solutions and other remedies as we have mentioned in the previous section have been tried without relief, then apply this cautery called "point," which is shaped as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After puncturing around the painful ear or both ears, hold them slightly apart and tilt them upwards from the root of the ear, having marked the place of the joint.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and make X punctures around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterward, treat the joint while it is healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	Of mouth torture" translates roughly to "Du torture de la bouche" in
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	The torture that must be cured by cautery is limited to those that move with fluid, as we have said in the sections about illness.
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not perform cautery on conditions that resemble dryness and pain from nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this resemblance of torture that moves with fluid from dry spells and purging in the head and gargling, and it is not effective, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the base of the ear, another slightly above the temple, and the third in the adjustment of the two lips.
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery instrument on the part that opens up clean, and make a burn in the top of the ear just below the edge of the skull, and another one on the forehead at about the same distance;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery on until half of the heart is burned;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it resembles the knife that we have placed in front, but this one is a bit more subtle, and it is necessary for the knife to be slightly thicker.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing, reset it as I have previously said, while it remains healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is ancient and you cure it as we have said, but the patient does not benefit, and has no fever, then make four cauterizations.
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	On the two horns of the head, I apply heat to the head, and I treat the limb called "vessel" as we have previously said, and do no cauterization on the mouth of the stomach.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and so be healed as we have said before.
de litargie	The word "de litargie" appears to be related

de la froidor dou chief	from the cold at the top
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	The head should be cleaned with earth and water as we have said before.

de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should only use fire cautery for those who are phlegmatic; it is first necessary to purify the brain with years and other remedies as we have mentioned in the section on the treatment of great pain and suffering from medicinal errors.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a young child who cannot bear the pain, give them gargles and chewing, often cleansing the brain with good meats;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the king has entered the chamber, and we have done the cautery as we have said before, and cauterized on the vessel, and on each corn.

Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is afflicted, perform a delicate cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, there are excessive or corrupt moisture and a thick flux, then perform cauterization with hot irons as we have said for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, the excessive fluids decline into melancholy and the body of the afflicted patient is moist, then give him something to drink by which the brain is purified, as is appropriate according to the rules of division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After the king has entered with the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	After making the twist of the bandage well done, just as if you draw a circle, place it on the head.
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the patient should be crossed, held firmly from all sides.
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	after applying the poultice, rub it with butter from old bees.
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and heat it gently over fire, so that the patient can bear it.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after emptying the circle inside out around the head, and leaving it to cool down;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this for the patient each week once with another good method, as long as they are healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or, if you need to cauterize it, make several incisions across the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	this method of cautery moistens the brain increasingly;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then place a moist cotton ball in butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyes come first under the signs I mentioned in the previous section, then begin and give to the patient something to drink, a purifying medicine for the head, and protect from all moisture, and make him sweat or take a bath while fasting.

dou cors des larmes	two sides of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and flow in the veins, cut the arteries that are visible on the inner side of the eye.

Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil (maybe referring to skin or a wound) is softened by illness and moisture, then use this cautery which is called "olive.
de coi ci est li forme:	Due to which the shape is:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see that it is necessary to perform cautery on both sides of the wound, make them as long as the hairs;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not remove your hand until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that is not yet oil (i.e., unripe or not fully developed)
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Never does it happen that the hairs of the wound are turned to ash, and they prick the skin; and cautery is performed according to these two manners:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say, with fire or burning medicine.

et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of the work's healthiness are that you see the skin retracting and the hairs standing on end at the tip of the oil.

aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the healing treatment as long as it is clean.

puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take French soap and sharp knife, each one, and grind them together well;

Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	As you have done this for a long time, if medicine fails, resort to surgery.

et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is so, then it is good.

Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you have to take care of yourself, watch over your work carefully so that it does not stray from the medicine at all.

aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment, as long as it is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the form of the wound with great care:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the bones of humans vary in size and shape, and according to these constraints.
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and do not deviate from the correct path for him who has studied this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have explained in the sections on diseases, and your treatments are of no benefit, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to place his head in a healthy position.
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor do they wiggle their head.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	after moistening a cloth with wine or juice of parsley on oil;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	after heating the cautery instrument that is sharp:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it should be shaped like the head of a quill, assembling the tip to be the cautery.
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you look, it is pointed from one side to the other, and if you look, it is also like a tent.
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but nevertheless, this baldness is worth moving for your work.

de la dolor des dens	of the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When dental pain comes from coldness or frostbite, and medical remedies are ineffective, then cautery is required according to the following two methods:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and with butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	The butter cautery is such that you press butter into the wound, and then end it with a metal spoon, either of iron or gold.

Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	He uses fire cautery if it is such that you insert a iron or steel needle into it, and it is hot enough so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, from which the shape is formed, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down.

de ydropisie	The term "dydropisie" appears to be a
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not effective for edema, except in the manner known as "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you cure it according to the ways we have said in divisions, and your treatment is not beneficial, then you must make four cauterizations around the wound, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the heart, two behind the back on the spine, and one at the anus.
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	and so the cauterization should be close to the specific heart beat.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	After leaving the cauterization open for a long time to allow pus to drain, do not neglect the care of the patient after the cauterization.
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	and healing would be hastened, and the two intentions would be aligned with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	The form of the cauterization for the abdomen should be like the nail that we have shown before.
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	and if it is for the back to be olive-shaped, according to what it has been previously placed.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the stones
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the feet are swollen in a hydroptic patient, filled with yellow pus, it is necessary to cauterize on the back between the little finger and the ring finger.
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and hold your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, so as to close the citrus wound, and be the cautery according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	After that, make two cauterizations on each leg at the tip with the point of the knife;
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	and make the cautery long, one on either side of the knee and the other on the leg.
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	and leave the cauteries to grow long without dressing them, so that they heal from within.
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	after the dressing of the other wounds that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the injury
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When abdominal pain arises from cold and moisture, the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by any means.
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	and you see the patient in great pain and of strong virtue, so make a great cautery on the stomach according to what he has spoken beforehand or cautery of the stomach, to the circulating cautery;
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	and I cauterize around the anus gently with a subtle cautery, and I cauterize on the thighs.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each place, and three small cauteries on the stomach to lessen the great pain, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	On the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When hemorrhoids are at the foundation or in one or more places, and they are old and composed of corrupt cold and moist humors, and they are treated as we have said in the divisions, but it does not help, then make cauterization:
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	On the spine of the back, whoever is completely devoid of strength, gradually and carefully moves in a triangular motion, and with two incisions from the side, he should cauterize the wound.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	and if you think his stomach is chilled, and the meat does not cook, and you see the face swelling, then great cautery should be applied to the stomach, as it is said above, and another on the liver, and another across all the organs with cautery nails.
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, reset the joint while it is still healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	When you have finished everything, if you feel the heat of the cautery that seems too sharp, and then apply it thoroughly to that entire wound;
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	and let your hand be still so that the cautery reaches the vein's origin, from which comes health.
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	do this once or twice, and if there is much heat in the wound, cauterize each one as we have said.
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	after the beneficial treatment of wounds while they are clean;
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	and if you use a large hot cautery on it, it will have greater help.
de plaie mal curee	From the badly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, as we shall relate in its place, such a disease arises that can only be healed by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a vein becomes fistulated, and is inflamed, filled with putridity and corrupt moisture, you must try every subtle remedy, and ensure that you know the full strength of each attempt.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	After heating the cautery until it seems sharp, insert it into the fistula according to the amount that has entered, and repeat the cauterization as many times as necessary until the dead and corrupted tissue is completely burned, once or twice or three times, depending on the amount required.
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	and be careful not to burn the sensitive nerves and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	if the fistula is in the wall of the bladder and the intestine, be careful of these joints, and make no fires except on fat flesh, and consider that it is not permanent.
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	After healing the limb as long as it is healthy, and if the joints are loose, and the bones have been pulled apart for a long time, then know that the joint is completely healed.
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	and if the bones have not been pulled apart, know that the joint is broken and the bone is crushed at its base.
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	and thus, as one of these things we would say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	When sharp pain and great swelling come, and it does not respond to treatment for women, then you must perform a cauterization on the affected area on both sides, using the cautery iron that we have previously mentioned.
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	and so we cauterize it in the middle, if there are three cauterizations in a row, and they will bring greater aid.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then it should be cauterized in the upper part, where the urethra begins, and this on both the right and left sides, making each cauterization as long as our thumb.
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	and then cauterize behind the back, as needed.
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	and let the cautery be done according to the shape mentioned above.
de la marris	Of the pain
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	When the weather is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception, and the flowers are withered and their ends delay;
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	and when they come, great pain is felt;
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	then it is necessary to make three cauterizations around the anus, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauterizations on the back;
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	and let the cautery burn, as we have said.
de la hainche	de la hainche" translates to "of the spine
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	When sticky moisture descends to the chest cavity and for this reason it becomes mute in its place, and the sign is that the affected limb appears longer than the other when measured together.
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	and it is found that the internal organs move, so it is necessary to cauterize the patient on the chest at the cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the organ around the chest as it returns, so that the chest is within the circle.
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	and if they are cauterized like those with which the stomach is cauterized.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	And if this cautery is not present, make three cauterizations from the large olive tree, and let these cauterizations be just as effective as all the others.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it as long as it is healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain arises in the chest due to cold and moisture, and the patient suffers from great discomfort, treatment as described in the previous section is not effective, and the illness is chronic:
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	Then it is necessary for you to cleanse the patient of bad humours, such as foul pills or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere;	After that, he performs cautery;
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	and the method of cautery is according to two manners:
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	this is to say, burning medicines and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cautery is according to many manners, of which some are as follows:
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	that you cauterize on the wound of the hamstring in three places, cauterizing them triangularly according to this form, and make them deeply and widely, and allow between each cautery a distance equal to that of two fingers, and let them be olive-colored.
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	never should one cauterize in the middle of the hamstring, which is why there are three according to this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	and if you see that the cautery is like a circle as we have said before in the dislocation of the hamstring;
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	but make it in such a way that the circles hold all the hair, and every little part of the heart is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the method used for sciatica, when the pain persists in the hip and does not reach the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it extends to the thigh and leg, make two cauterizations here where the patient feels the most pain, and one cauterization on top of the ankle, slightly to the left side.
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	and it should be a cutting cauterization, and the thickness of the heart should be burned.
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	and if the patient feels the pain extending up to the two bones of the foot or near the ankle, cauterize that area in three spots or four, and this cauterization is called "point.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if it happens again, it must be done more carefully;
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the pain is in the knee towards the thigh, it is done with a sharp or circular cautery; and be very careful in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery too long, burning the nerves and large arteries, and causing the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	I myself have seen many who had cauterized the ankle of the foot, and left it until the leg was completely swollen, and the ankle as well, and it became pierced and corrupted throughout the entire foot.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After an abdominal solution, he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, apply cautery to one and to the other in this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the wise ones say about the cauterization of the spine: this is how it should be done, take a hot iron as thick as a finger and make incisions, either crossed or one after the other, with a distance between them equal to the thickness of a fingernail.
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	and intertwine them across both parts, and they should also be equal, and have one well-made iron;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	and heat it until it is entirely red and oozes pus, then place it on the diseased joint of the patient, and turn to the healthy side.
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	and cauterize it once the cautery is dry, and leave it for three days.
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	and then apply a paste of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of dressing, as long as it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	Albuscasim says that we use this cautery little because of the fear of its regard, and we see few who use it.
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	and yet these are good cauteries, which a strong person can endure, and the place where it is done.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	He uses the cautery of burning medicine if you make an instrument to intertwine with which you lower the edge of the door, and it is either of iron or steel on a long wall, and at the top there are two of us, and between each one has the quantity of thickness of a finger.
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	and they should be open above and below, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	After that, place the board of the chair on the sick person lying on their side, and quickly put your hand most over the board of the chair.
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After pouring between the two circles of hot awes (a type of iron) heated over fire, leave it for an hour, and let the patient endure the heat and burn from it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	Because it has the same effect as fire;
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	and when the burn has passed, take a clean hand with the instrument and raise the limb with the soft awes, leaving it thus for three days, and apply butter until the black from the burn is removed;
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	and let it remain three days in purification;
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and this would be the last aid after the treatment of wounds as long as it is healthy.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	And if the pain extends to the thigh or leg, apply the instrument as it has been done in the hip, accordingly.
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	and this is the way of hot water, and I have written it in treating for rectifying medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and hot ashes, as much of one as of the other, crush them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	if he has a small opening, deflect it so that the tip of a tool can enter.
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and place it in another well-sealed pot, and add alkali and salt, and gently heat it until there are two layers of powder on top, as you would carefully press it into your hand.
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and leave it until all the water and liquid have evaporated from the sealed pot, then take all that remains of the liquid, and pour it onto salt and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And thus, it will be a great aid and comforting in many works of medicine and other cauterizations on other parts of the body.
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	For it performs the same work as fire, and is useful in other medications where cauterization is applied well to the wound, such as honey, anacardium, and chalk with soap; all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure for which a nobleman was freed from the pain of chest and sciatic vein, and he said that no other cure was done, and he was completely healed once this treatment was carried out, and he bathed as he teaches below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And it is prepared in such a way that you press fresh and dry laurel leaves, grind them finely with some fat, and apply it to the wound and on the thigh and leg where the pain persists, and bind it.
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	and leave it for three hours, or as long as the patient no longer feels the pain.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	Then make the patient take a bath or a warm drink until the body is slightly warmed, and make them lie down, and the pain will disappear completely and they will be cured.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire treatments with such remedies, except after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it provides great relief.
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and the cautery must be performed in this way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take another cloth and grease it with old oil, and place it in the hollow between the big toe and the other one called the fossa.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After taking dried goat's dung, set it alight until it becomes charcoal, and place it on the wool, leaving it until it is stained.
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and repeat this process again, and do not stop doing so as long as you think the pain has ceased;
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	and this method of cauterization is called "keyhole cautery.
de la dolor dou dos	Of the great pain in the back.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When great pain comes to the back, whether from strain or impact, or due to excessive evacuation, or from some similar matter that appears expanded and cold, no cautery is valuable against these symptoms other than for those who suffer from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	After the patient has been voided of foul pills or other similar substances, one should apply this on the back, where the pain resides, three lines marked with a sign of a cross, and in each line, V cauterizations or more, according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure.
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	and the cauterization is done according to the cautery which is called "points";
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	and if you see, make three cauterizations or four at the middle of the bone according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	This illness often comes to young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a tight and painful throat when they swallow, and they feel weak.
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you feel the last, deep pain in the back and, appearing differently from the other pains.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this (condition) and you observe it being cured, cauterize it with a hot iron according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	The cauterization should penetrate each part of the pain equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, cauterize around the pain with a hot iron that pierces two or three lines, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treatment, keep the limb healthy according to what we have said, and be careful not to apply heat to any stiffness that is nerve-related.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When the pain of joints is caused by moisture that spreads through each member of the body, and when the pain comes suddenly, they call it "podagra" properly, and when it is due to cold and can't be cured with medicines, it is cured by cautery in this manner:
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	Make a burn around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary to press on the face with your foot, make a cautery all around with something called "point.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens often, make cautery on each knee with three or four cauteries from every side, making all cauteries olive-shaped.
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	and if you have more skill, do more, but don't hold your hand too tightly until the specific heat is burned in.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	and if the pains are in the hands, then do less around the bones, two lines at most.
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if no pain remains, do less on each joint and on the skin of the hand;
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	and if the pains come up to the waist or shoulders, cauterize each part and do good governance for the patient, taking medications.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you apply good care and purge the fluides, it will be healed by God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	from the rupture of the sinew
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When a rupture occurs in the legs, and the bows descend to the knees, it is new, so when you see it healing, do not interfere with that day.
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and it uses things that cause the stomach to relax, so that the intestines descend from the stomach.
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	after making it lie on its back between your hands, instruct it to hold its breath until the bowels are repaired, and arrange them in your palms, and sign with your fingers across the rupture on the bone of the wrist, and mark it at every joint as if it were half a circle above the body.
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then heat up the cautery with which is this form:
