tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and exudes tendrils.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	then reset the bones to their place;
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and the healers should place their hands on it so that they do not return to the previous state;
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and open well the thighs of the patient, and place beneath him cushions and supports on the thighs, and others on the bed which hold his hands;
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	then place the cautery iron on the affected area with your entire hand, and hold it straight until you reach the bone. If you do not touch the bone the first time, repeat this process several times until you do.
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and be careful that the boil does not burst when you apply the cautery.
que tu ne le brulasses;	so that you do not burn it.
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and so that the patient does not die or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is necessary that the cauterizer of children be subtle according to their size, and for grown people as great according to their measure;
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	after three days, cure the shoulder with butter until the burn is healed;
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	after the treatment with other remedies until it is healed, and lay the patient on his back for forty days until the wound is completely sealed;
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	and it is necessary that these movements be left for a long time, so that the boils do not appear when he goes to other rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, a well-made bandage should be applied to him and left for another forty days.
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and he should have good rest, work little, and guard against excessive drinking and eating, as well as too much noise.
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	and when he follows this teaching, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will now describe the treatment for cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When ruptures occur in other parts of the body and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow any more, apply cautery to them from cautery according to their quantity, and burn one-third of the depth.
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the cure according to what we have said;
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the ancients said that one should cauterize with a three-angled iron according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the site of the hernia with a sign, and make a line across the width above the rupture; then another from below, and hold your hand firm over all the cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cautery is lighter and easier.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain arises in any limb, whether from falling or injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and the medicinal cure is ineffective, then it should be cauterized with the cautery known as "the point," and the cauterization must be done according to the length of the limb and its smallness and fragility, and its twist, and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	if it is healthy from the first cauterization, that is good;
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	if that does not work, repeat the cauterization on another part, because such is the custom that it should move to the neighboring limb, so you must perform the cauterizations until the patient is healthy.
de meselerie	From illness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The wounds are aided in no way by cautery, especially the illness that arises from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	You should cauterize the wound, be careful if the illness is in its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, without delay or staying, and you doubt that the corruption may spread throughout the patient, then make cautery on the head.
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I apply the heat to the head at noon, and to the other side towards the forehead at the end of the hair.
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and then on both sides, and behind on the scalp.
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and leave it long enough for the cautery to reach the bone, and until the scabs come off so that the vapor of the thick humors can escape.
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and cauterize the mouse according to what is before it.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	and if the infection is scattered everywhere;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and it is clearly evident, so you must cauterize these wounds with the cautery we have mentioned above, and cauterize them deeply, and cauterize on the spine of the neck, and cauterize on the spine of the back, and greatly on the groin and another delicate place, and on both shoulders.
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and on the sides, and on the tendons of the legs, and on each joint of the hands and feet, and in the pits of the hands.
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and guard the nerves that are on the bottom of the foot from burning.
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and never perform cauterization on the bones of the hand or other bones, such as those of the stomach or liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And know that the more cauterization is performed, the greater the help it provides and the better the outcome.
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	and know that the patient feels no pain from cauterization, as the healthy one does, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be great and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the ways of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, apply wheat flour with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When swelling appears in any member and is cured by medicines, oils, and bandages, but there is no improvement, then the doctor should perform cautery on the affected member according to its size.
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	and the cautery should be performed slightly inside the heart's chamber.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound as long as it is not healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And never should cautery be performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the point where the nerve controls the member, and thus if the swelling is removed.
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	and nevertheless, no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the passages of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of albars (or albaras, a medical term
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the disease called "albaras" is raging, and the medical arts are of no avail, then cauterize with a hot iron a little bit, according to the amount of danger present, until the white is removed, and it changes color.
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	then apply a cure of meal and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and collick sap and alder sap, each in its own portion.
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and mix all together, bind them with a cloth, and keep them elevated until they are healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of a cancer (chancre) by cauterization.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a wound appears at the beginning, and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that seems to form a circle, around the entire wound.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	Nevertheless, the wise say that one should also perform cautery in the middle of the chancre;
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	However, this does not seem good to me, as I fear it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never had any success with it before;
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	and the more appropriate thing is that it be cauterized around, in the cautery called a "circle," as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	from the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When anyone has a disease called "adubelati," and it does not end in death or because of the excess it creates, or due to the severe pain of the illness when the patient is aged (i.e., too much), and there is little blood, or because of time.
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you see it hasten to death:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then cauterize around with small cauterizations by pricking:
aprés le laisse ensi.	afterward leave it thus:
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	Because it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through all the cautery, make the cautery so hot that this is its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this illness called "adubelati" until the cauterization has reached the heart, and it is done in such a way that the patient feels relief in this manner so that the flow of putrefaction is stopped.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment, until it is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	Heal the fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another type of illness is called "corrodens," which is nothing other than a corruption of the member, as it attacks the members just as fire does the dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this disease in a limb that can be treated with fire cautery, then heat the cautery nails slightly and greatly, according to what is suitable for the limb or the disease.
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	After cauterizing all parts until you eliminate all corruption, and nothing remains of it, everything that is corrupted must be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and apply oil to the cauterized limb suffering from broiling due to fire until all burns from the fire are eliminated, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of wounds that cause pain.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if after three days, healthy hair does not grow, that is good.
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	and if that is not the case, then repeat the cautery on what is remaining of the corrupted limb.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this mixture is sometimes treated with a hot liquid instead of fire cautery.
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	but fire cautery is nevertheless of greater help, and I have already described the treatment for the hot liquid mixture in the previous section.
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the vessels that come as pieces
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that a pain arises from a defect which we call "close" according to our intention, and it is a great fault which wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	For fire cautery, heat the instrument like a shear, as hot as it can go, made of good iron to hold the nail from all sides, and have sharp edges.
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	After heating everything hot on the nail, and turn your hand completely around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail.
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and leave it thus for three days until it begins to fester.
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	then make a poultice of wild sage leaves ground with rope, leave it on all night, and the nail will come out and be pulled from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the shoulder with a warm compress until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are burned by fire, and many times it happens on hands and feet, then you must apply hot water cautery.
et est en teil maniere:	and it is in this way:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	Take a needle of iron or gold, or a quill from a raven's wing, and place the nail and the thread on it, that is, the pliers for warts.
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	and place the needle around it so that it surrounds everything, then apply a little hot wax, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the needle reaches the root of the nail, and can find the hot water channel all the way to the root.
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	and the patient suffers a little the biting of hot water for an hour;
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	then leave it thus, and it will pull out at the root entirely.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	First, do one after another, until you have eased all those that are in the body, then treat the injuries which cause pain.
li cure dou trembler	It cures the trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When anyone shivers from cold or has a fever, it is necessary to make four cauterizations on the spine at the back, or three cauterizations between each spine.
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and make one cauterization on the foot, and another on the stomach with an olive cautery.
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	if he lets it shake, and hastens the health of the cold illness.
des pustules puans	from pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never is it apparent through external defects or pus-filled blisters that come from highly corruptive matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	it is necessary at first, when they appear, to perform cautery on each head of the pustule:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	a subtle cautery with a stick of myrtle, whereby the point is seized by fire, or with the root of an aromatic plant distant, or with lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And never should one cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow worse in advance, but are healed of the excesses from which they come.
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times, severe consequences arise from the blood of an artery that is cut at the wound, or during the incision of an abscess, or the cauterization of a member, and similar things.
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	and it is a very serious matter to stink.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And yet if this happens to anyone, hasten to place your finger on the wound of the vein, and pull very strongly until the pain subsides completely under your finger, and no more blood flows.
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	then place over the fire various olive oil cautery, small and large, until they are all red;
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	then take, according to the size of the wound and the place where the artery is visible, a great or small amount of salt, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery there until the blood stops flowing.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a sudden burning occurs while you are lying with your arm above the vein and the cauterization is complete, quickly take another cautery from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	and do not stop doing this one after the other until the blood stops flowing;
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	and be careful not to burn the nerve that is nearby, and do not let any further harm come to the patient;
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	and know that when there is no bleeding from the artery, one cannot properly feel it, especially when the artery is large, unless by one of the three ways we have said:
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	or by cauterization, or by extraction when it is not properly treated, or by a strong thread, or by medications placed on it that have the power to stop bleeding.
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	and it becomes locked and stretched.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers relief tightly binding them with cloth or placing hot things on them, or similar, will not benefit unless he does it properly.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to none and he has no medication at hand, he should place his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it well until it is felt over the wound and the vein.
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and do not move it, but apply cold moisture often as it is very cold until the flesh is frozen and swollen and numb.
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	and prepare remedies in advance for those who need cauterization and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	We begin the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have told you in the first chapter all about diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicines, and we have explained their purposes, causes, instruments, and forms of cauterization.
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and I have placed this chapter on the most common diseases, and I will follow the same path in this chapter so that those who wish to find it more easily may do so.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, before we begin, it is important for you to know that this chapter involves greater risk and fear than the first one on cauterization, and therefore requires more caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things.
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	Because many ways of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	if they come from those who were so afflicted by their illness that they died gently due to the severity of their condition and the great torment of their suffering.
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And from these one must be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And of these there are some who give up hope, and say:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am weak.
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the illness is cruel.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	You should not consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more great care in your honor than in your greed. Do not act rashly but wisely regarding what is certain and what you can safely acquire.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	and use divination and indication for the cure of your sick patients so that health may be restored.
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	and this will help you gain good reputation, glory, and long-lasting fame.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear child, our lords give you good understanding and rectitude, and if you desire the holy inspiration from his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter for you, in considering by chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery that I have devised from the head down to the foot, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	dou chief plein d'aigue" translates to "a head filled with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	Know that this illness often comes to children at birth, and when the head is squeezed too tightly.
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and it never comes from a known cause that one cannot explain.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and to all those that I have seen, death has hastened.
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	and for this reason, it seems to me that I must give up the work in part, in some treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw children whose joints were filled with water, and the head swelled each day until it could not be supported.
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and the moisture was so great that it became a wound, and this moisture is gathered underneath the bone near the lymphatic vessel between the heart and the bone.
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and if the work is such that moisture is between the heart and bone, and the abscess is small, you must make a wide cut in the middle of the head.
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and it should be as long as the moisture runs.
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and here, the form of the sharp instrument:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the openings of the skull comming apart in each part, and there is a sharp, strong pain when you press your hand inside, and it does not return to its place.
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If it is necessary for you to cut into the head, make three cuts according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	After making the cuts, tighten them with bandages and powders, and then apply wine and oil, leaving it thus for up to five days.
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	then untie it and dress the wound with bandages and compresses, leaving the head equally tightened, and provide the patient with dry meat from a pouch of moisture until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another method of incision is to observe the size of the abscess and the collection of pus.
car aucune fois est elle devant;	because never is it before;
aucune fois derrier;	never behind
aucune fois en destre;	never on the right
et aucune fois en senestre.	and never on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Then cut open the abscess deeply, and drain the pus, and make an incision according to your ability.
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and be sure not to cover the artery;
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and draw out the blood flow, so that the patients die from the rapid onset of bloodletting and moisture evacuation.
de reume	Of the root
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens to anyone a disease called "cataract" as some call it or worse, and the illness is ancient, and the cure of medicine does not help, then the last remedy is the cautery with which one severs both arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	Therefore, when you see them cover their eyes, the patient must turn his head back.
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	after rubbing the shoulder with a rough cloth until the arteries open, then gently pull the patient's collar to its full extent.
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	then look at where the vein is located, and the joints on both sides are behind the ears, and they are properly positioned.
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	then mark the joints with a signet ring, and cut one and both with a sharp scalpel, reaching as close to the bone as possible, and do this from the wide end upwards.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, remove the spatule from beneath the artery and cut above it, also cutting as it should go through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it bleeds continuously unless something holds it shut from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	and if the artery does not open when pressed, it is necessary to measure the distance of three fingers, then mark with a signet ring and cut through to the bone.
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	and that one should apply heat to the wound if it is necessary, perhaps 6 parts, or possibly a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the filling of the artery.
puis regarde la plaie:	then examine the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	if it remains on the bone with a sharp tip without pus forming, and if no abscesses appear, then strain the wound and bind it, and apply treatment as necessary until it is healthy.
de emigrainne	from migraine headache
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old migraine headaches come with catarrh due to moisture in the eyes and sockets, and cold perspiration, and other similar symptoms, and all medical treatments are ineffective, then we should drain the arteries of the eyes and apply cautery, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the method of extracting them is that the patient pulls out the hairs from their temples, and locates the artery which opens in the temple, as it opens well due to its pulsation, and is hardly closed outside, for there is no man too strong.
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and if it is reduced, pull the collar tightly from any rough fabrics, then rub the limb with a coarse cloth and immerse it in hot water until the artery appears clearly visible.
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	then take the spatula with its curved shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	then gently scrape the skin until you feel the artery, then hold it with pincers and carefully remove the strings that adhere to each part.
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	and if the artery is thin, return it to the tip of the hook and cut off that part according to the quantity of the two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it does not heal without great pain throughout.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And draw out blood from the vein of six parts, just to three.
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you bind it in two parts with a strong double thread of silk, so that putrefaction does not come before the healing of the wound and prevents complications from blood.
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	then cut off the excess between the two threads at that very moment, and then, if you see fit, cauterize with a cutting cautery tool just to the bone, as long as the chips are removed.
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and this is the mother task, if the patient has fever and is of hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	Because cautery is helpful in ending moisture:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	for this is of greater help with moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Or, for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the wound with dry cotton and apply tightly fitted bandages.
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when they are unbound, it is necessary to use dry medicines that produce heat and tightly fitted bandages until the wound is healed.
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and without any delay from the artery as you do it, if you hasten to cover with cautery, or employ the juice of vitriol and press it in your hand so that the wound is immediately cleansed;
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	and if you do not have this at hand, place a cold compress on the wound until it is frozen, and then apply hot water as needed to ensure proper healing.
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	and the one that is more mobile and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this sharp cautery from both sides, but the cuts should be well-spaced to preserve their heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	Because when the instruments are too tight, they hold back their heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And it must have between the two knives a space of sufficient width, and then when you have marked with the tongue both sides, and put the hot iron upon it until it reaches the bone, cut the vein in two places.
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and they must be separated between the two parts, for this cautery is not fully fused from one end to the other.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears from the eyes flow into the veins that are on top of the head, and no benefit comes from the medicines used, and you see the face of the patient becoming round, and feel their forehead trembling as if from chills.
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and its oil is hot and moist so that the hairs of the skin fall out, and the skin is scorched by the heat of the tears, for this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And they called it the "contused cure," and this is what you do for the patient who has this illness: he lets his hairs grow on his forehead, then you make three cuts on his forehead equally according to its length.
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and one of the cuts should be also deep as two others across the forehead, extending down to the nose, and the other two should be made along the sides over the skin, and beware of incising the arteries that are on the sides over the skin.
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	And move your hand away from the continuity of the two jaws, and each wound should have the quantity of three fingers in width across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and take a piece of sponge and cloth to wipe the blood, then use the sharp spatula with two parts from which this shape is:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision that is made on the forehead, just below the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape all the flesh that is between the two cuts to the entire satisfaction that is on the bone, then make another cut from this one until the other second, and then extract this spatula forcefully.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you insert the instrument called "cultellaire" (a type of scalpel) into the first incision, it should be very sharp on one side and soft on the other; its shape is as follows:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	and place the sharp side of the instrument towards the opposite edge at the center, and the soft side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to their roots until the incision is continuous up to where it opens the heart, and then make another slit in the middle until it reaches the other side.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then extract the blood equally, and press the wound to express the blood taken.
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then place a strip of fine cotton in each slit, and cover it with damp cloths soaked in wine and oil and wool, and ensure that no pus comes out.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and apply a strong infusion of sage in olive oil, then use a basic dressing with rose oil, and other remedies to heal wounds, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	your joints.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When a person has acute catarrh habitually, and you see the eyes become cloudy and small, weakening vision, and the eyelids burnt,
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and the head becomes painfully hot, and the patient sneezes;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Then understand these accidents that these matters and this cleansing come only from many veins, and the moving cure that is, it is thus.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to press their forehead, then make a deep cut across the forehead, and another one very wide.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin from the split in the left temple to the right temple, and make the cut up to the bone.
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and move your hand away from the nails of the temples that move when squeezed.
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then separate the two edges of the split and place old cotton and linen on it.
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then lay him on a blanket moistened with wine and oil, and guard against hot pus.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	When it is removed, it is necessary to rub the bone until it begins to heal, then apply drying remedies that help healing.
En teil maniere:	In the same manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of wheat flower and three parts of cologne, mix them to make an emberment.
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and administer these remedies to heal the wounds thoroughly.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From ear discomfort
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	Everything that breaks off inside the ears is one of the four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or seeds, or animals, or stone from the mine, or similar things as to make:
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seeds, such as beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or things that flow away like water, smooth and clear, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	If anything, such as a stone or any other object that does not fit properly in the ear, causes pain or does not grow inside the ear, place the affected ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see a stone, and it exudes a little drop of dark or yellow oil, then proceed to extract it.
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and it causes sneezing from congestion, and it stops up the nostrils when sneezing occurs, and place pieces of cloth or wool inside the ear.
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and stretch the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Often, this treatment brings about fever.
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come out, apply gentle extracts with small pincers, which is its form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it jumps out with the pincers, that is good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if it does not, apply an extract with a delicate, small-toothed instrument;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it still does not come out, make a wire hook and bend the tip of the hook towards the ear canal, and stuff the area around the hook with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the hook.
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then mold it to its proper form, for often it comes out as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come out in that way, take a sharp instrument and carefully make an incision, and insert some cotton inside.
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	then press the lump against the stone or anything else, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if none of the things we have said work, hurry to split the ear so that the abscess hardens and does not move.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the method of the cut is that you first make the patient safe from the pain in the head, and extract blood according to its strength, then place the patient between your hands and restore the ear to its original position, and make a small cut at the base of the ear where the fat or tissue is attached.
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and make the cut as thin as a moon, until you reach the bone, then remove it according to your skill, and suck on it gently with your mouth.
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it while it is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is a grain that is embedded and swollen, then administer extraction.
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot be extracted, then administer the delicate scraping according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and perform an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not attempt this if you think the grain is moist from earwax, as long as you have made many attempts.
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract it gently with pincers and suck, as we have said, so that the extraction is light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case where something breaks off in the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use sneezing to expel the foreign object, and to open the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lay something on that same ear, whether there is a foreign body or water.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps through fire, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If this is not done, take many pins according to the length of your thumb and fingers, and warm them slightly in the fire.
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and insert a plug into the patient's ear, and try from another side, and place another stone on top of the stone in the ear.
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and continue this process of stone against stone until the pain completely subsides, and thus it will completely disappear.
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see, take a thin wire, and insert one end into the ear, and heat the other end with fire until the thinner wire is burned.
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Then make other adjustments of other joints until the pain completely disappears, as we have said before.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	When extracting a small foreign body, such as a tiny bug or similar object, treat it as we have described in the previous section.
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is large and can be felt, use tweezers for its careful extraction.
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and it is the easiest thing to remove, which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	When extracting worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the section and how to deal with distensions, the treatment is not effective; it is therefore necessary that you examine the ear in sunlight.
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If no worms are opened, but they are treated with fine pliers, and if they do not open, take the cane from which their form is as follows:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be tightened from below and widened from above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And insert the most subtle instrument into the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient, then suction along the entire cane.
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Make sure often until all the veins are open.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, then cauterize around the cotton thread as I said before;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not protrude as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have tried in incision of worms, and you will find them or treat distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if distill your oils and medications into the ear with all these instruments, in such a way as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And whether it is of silver or golden threads, remove them from small incisions and above others to distill;
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press from below the distillation with a well-made silver instrument, and if you see it, take a razor and wrap cotton around the tip carefully.
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you see of your medications in the cauldron, and the cauldron be in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then put the razor completely into the cotton and press your damp hand firmly until the oil is distilled or slightly from the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and it makes the patient feel deep pain, and so the distillations are heated in the fire just as they are in the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and ensure it is not too cold, for the medicine would then be ineffective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From ear discomfort
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born with any perforation of the eardrum.
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and the same thing happens to adults due to sudden injury or a foreign object in the ear, and this blockage never fully clears in the ear unless one can see it.
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and never let the wound become infected, and the sight be good.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	When this happens, and it cannot be seen, the lack of proper treatment leads to more harm. In such a case, it is necessary to place the patient's ear in the sun.
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the swelling clearly, where this tissue has formed:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And make cuts both before and behind, all around, so that it does not damage the ear.
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the operation is on a new or old part of the ear, and you have fine pincers, hold it gently and cut slightly until that part is completely severed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	If the inflammation is deep in the ear, take a fine, sharp razor, warm it slightly over the fire, and insert it into the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the operation is causing great pain in the ear, pierce gently, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear.
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then place in the ear a band according to the size of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Make sure no day passes until the wound is clean, or take a tent and moisten it with rosewater, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on it.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear swollen, it is necessary that you take the tent and move another tent moistened in cerate made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then dress it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the occurrence of blood comes, soak a sponge and drape it with cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that remove the flow of blood, which are treated through distillation.
de la char des papieres	Of the work of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	Make sure that when they come off in papers, the roots are moist and dry, it is necessary that you extend them with pliers and tongs, and cut the top with a spatula from its roots.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then place the hot glass on the affected area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if, after removing the outer skin with a delicate lenticular cauterization, the cauterizer makes another incision, he must be moved.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and often they heal, but nothing remains of their roots.
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized with fire, their roots are burned and do not grow back.
de la gresle	from the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times come to paper certain things that appear twisted in their form and hardness, and for this reason, this disease is called "grapes," and it is a gathering of great moisture on the paper above and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	The work is as follows:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	take care so that the grapes do not move from one side to the other, and this is a light thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	make the incision deeply, then carefully peel from each part slightly, then take it with pincers and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	if you cannot cover it without piercing the paper slightly, so as not to disturb the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the fracture is large, and it has a joint, treat it until it heals.
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, do not use excessive force, because the joints will soon restore it and cause harm.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the pain descends within the ear towards the top, turn the paper against it, and grasp the pain with tweezers, then cut and press from both sides.
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is separated by the incision, it does not matter.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the ice is broken, leave the salt water oil to heal the vein of the one who has been wounded until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Xerophtalmia is a fat that is deposited on the surfaces of paper, and this occurs more often in children than in adults, causing them great distress, leading to morning cataracts, and preventing them from looking at the light of the sun because tears flow to their eyes.
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and for this reason they close their eyes again, and sleep upon them, and their cheeks become moist beneath the hair that has grown out of the skin and appears covered with the oil from within.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the limb with your hands and feel the extreme pain between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	and the manner of the procedure is that the patient places their head in the hands of the healthy person.
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take the linen cloth, and prepare a tent in such a way that it forms a circle according to the quantity of the discharge from each part, and then place it over them.
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press your hands on both sides so that the bones meet within the circle.
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then make a groove in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula, not wider than the wound made in the vein.
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and cut the skin perfectly until you reach the bones.
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in different positions, pull out from the groove, according to the shape of a white fatty piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Take then from there a whole piece of cloth torn between your fingers over the fire, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is even.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and ensure that you do not adjust the gap, that you reach all the space up to the oil, and do not blow on it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the gap does not open at the beginning, gently widen the gap a little bit if it starts to open.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then extract it as we have said, then moisten the cloth with oil and water, apply it to the limb, and gently stretch it.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if with such people who grind and apply something to corrupt the moisture that is stuck.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it as long as it is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the hot abscess, treat it with external soothing as long as it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When papers (skin) grow hairs that are not natural, they become inflamed, causing just as much harm, and lead to types of illnesses such as rashes and softening of the papers, and scaling, due to the destruction of the hairs.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and the cure is according to four manners:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by cauterization with fire, or by using medicines according to what is presented in this chapter of cauterization, and it is done through incision and stitching, or by using bands, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient with the illness in your healthy hand, then turn the paper from the oil to your left hand.
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	if it turns out well
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if it does not turn out well, then pierce it with a needle through all the threads above it.
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and be sure to remove the edge of the paper where the hairs grow, and pull out the threads above all the paper, and turn it over to the razor.
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	Then, making an incision in the skin, they remove the hairs, adjusting them from root to tip, cleaning all the mucus, from the large tear to the small.
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	Then, extract the thread and place beneath the paper a small piece of cotton and cloth, then mark on the paper a shape like a mitre, but it must be according to the amount that you see the paper rise, which is measured in all directions.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if, at the part where one has to cut, they need to use a great deal of paper, according to how soft the paper is.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then making a cut across the entire surface of the two lines that you have marked, begin with a large tear from the outside to a small one.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let one of the cracks be near the natural hairs, in thickness like a root, then bend the knife into one of the two angles towards the heart, and then peel it all off.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then bring the two lips together with a stitch from a fine needle and all of the blood, and dry the excess of the fabrics on both edges without any sticky substances, if you are able to do this.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if this does not help, then after some time, leave the stitches and threads for three or four days.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then dress the wound without stitches or constricting things, for the paper becomes loosened at the healing of the wound and the gathering of it, but stitches are moved (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	and if in another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you sign the paper with a figure which is also like the shape of mint leaves, as we have described, at three points according to the form below:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take hold of what overcomes the small muscles equally according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you cannot hold the pincers firmly, and the matter is not even, take a needle where there is thread, and tie it around the shape.
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and twist another thread through the large tear, and the second thread through the small one, and gather the threads equally between your fingers.
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then gently hold your hand equally, and press all the skin where you have marked it, as we have said, then sew together the two edges of the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess forms at your incision, apply wax and similar medicaments to soothe it;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and never should the hairs of the paper (skin) be cut:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	it is necessary that you use what we have said about incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but stitching one to the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of dogs is as follows:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and you should convert the paper and make it inside according to what I have said, then make two chains by art, and two fine liens as long as the paper and wide with the spatule.
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut as the parts of the thread where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then carefully join each other over the top of the paper from the oil, and pull the two chains from the two parts formed.
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave it thus for no days, and the skin that is pulled will die and wither and heal, as long as it remains like this.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it is delayed, if the fever takes hold with great strength, then cure it as soon as possible while it is healthy.
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is deeply infected, and if it opens up and the pus comes out, and the hair cannot grow back.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and this is the shape of the two threads that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the work involves piercing the skin with a fine needle, threading a soft and thin silk thread through it.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then join the bones together subtly, and make sure the length of the fils is a palm's breadth.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then arrange in the wound another thin thread of silk briefly, and tie the ends tightly with the main thread.
