puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then place the patient's head in a healthy position.
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and make sure the sun is removed so that the work is revealed, for it is a delicate and small task. Then insert the needle into the entire wound at the root of the hair gently, piercing it into the paper slowly as you draw it along the natural hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then extract the hair up to the root, and push the hair back into the root if there is one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then extend your hand until the hairs grow fully out through all the root in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the root is treated and the hair does not grow out with it, then pull the root from the inside out along the entire thread that you had ordered, until the root comes out completely through the opening above and you see it with your eye's vision.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	So then, if you remove the chase and the thread, and close the wound and leave it for two or three days, until the hair grows back into its place and the scar heals.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	and if the hairs are small, then accompany them with the long hairs of natural growth, and raise it along with that or leave it, as long as it elongates and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	regarding the inflammation of the wound
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease called "aleacrati" or putrefaction comes to the wound, it has two manners:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one is natural, and the other is unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs suddenly from a wound, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the method of working in it is that you split open the wound, separate the lips of it, and put linen strips inside, binding it until it is healed.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not advisable that you use drying and constricting things in the treatment of it.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but I work with softening things, such as fennel.
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the rose water or other and flax seed are cooked, and the diluted vinegar in neither of the eyes, and it wraps a bandage, and treats this one.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the true treasure of your remedy is that you take care not to let it harden according to its former shape.
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these works that we have spoken are not only remedies for this illness, but also to prevent it from returning according to its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the matter that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is a dislocation, truly called "fracture," is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident arises from wounds, cuts, cauterization, and similar things.
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the way of the procedure is such that if you pierce a needle with a double thread, and insert it into the wound, and make it enter from the left side near the right eye, so that the thread comes out in two parts on both sides of the wound.
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then the wound is covered with cloth, and the patch is large enough to cover it.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the paper returns to what is appropriate, it is good.
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If this is not done, take a razor and place it in the fissure, turn the paper, and make two cuts on either side inside the paper.
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and the cuts of the two fissures at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make them form one angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter "I Greek".
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then cut that one, according to the thickness of its edges, from the paper, then adjust the two parts carefully, and sew them with a thread of wool.
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the remedy we have mentioned about soothing and softening medications, as long as he is healthy.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the disease comes from a cut or stitch or cauterization, it is necessary that you make a clean split beneath the skin and flesh, according to what is mentioned above.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then separate between the two parts of a tent, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the skilled masters have devised many devices from all sorts of means to restore the natural shape.
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient himself, according to what is necessary for the work and the use of various instruments in many arrangements.
dou soudement de la papiere	The phrase "dou soudement de la papiere" appears to be a fragment of the
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this sewing is done by inexperienced hands in such a way that the paper on top is smooth with white oil and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the tip of a razor under the paper and lift it slightly from below.

et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and is healthy the entire affected area, and never immerse it in dirty water, but rather use clear, clean water, and raise it with sweet water and a collar.

de l’ungle de l’oil	from the nail of the finger
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	You know that the fingernail grows according to two manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	It is nerve-related and appears hard and satisfying to touch, while another type is not nerve-related but seems like white, frozen moisture that, when touched with iron and treated like pincers, cannot be moved by anyone.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and both appearances begin towards the large tear duct, growing smaller and smaller until they cover all sight and all light and the movements of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the method of incision is such that the patient places his head on a healthy surface, then opens the eyes.
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and hold the paper in your hand, then curl the finger like a small pair of pincers, and stretch it upwards.
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and insert a horsehair, or a hen's feather, or cow hair, and tie a strong thread to it.
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle slightly and insert it through the nail, piercing the entire length of the needle, and tie the nail with thread, stretching it upwards, and scrape all the hair around the edge of the nail with a thin blade, immediately after applying the prune and silk to the hair root up to the head, then cut the remaining part at the base of the nail with a delicate spatula, leaving the nail in its natural state without any cuts.
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and never extend the nails to the bone, only with the file, as we have said.

et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and they grow as I have described in the dissection; and if you see it covered, open gently the wound of the sick person, and take a light spatula according to this form.

puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then recommence the other work according to this same operation, until it is entirely healed.

If nothing contradicts you in the oil, such as a hot abscess, then apply it, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then continue the work as before, until it is completely cured.

de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	on the flesh that is born on the iris
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	Some men's eyes never turn red, they cover the pupil and rest on paper, twisting them into a blackness that resembles a balm rose.

des voines des eulz	veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These are red veins that are covered over the eye, they steal from the sight their work and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	The first task is to observe which part is affected, whether it is a bone, muscle, or joint, and there is no other disease outside the swelling.

de la fistule de l’oil	from the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	It considers those as "fistules" named:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	As you treat it with cautery and medicine for the burning pain as I have previously said, and it remains unhealthy, there is a danger within it if you pierce the abscess, leaving him to die there, and remove all the moisture until the bone is exposed.

si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is a lighter matter for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the opening of the vein

puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then dislocate it after the day and night have passed, and if you see the oil repairing, that is good.
se ce non;	if not, then
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the splint, cloth, bandage, and leeches are reapplied while he is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	disruption of the woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When the veil or cloth covering is torn, it should be opened up and filled with papers as if with resin grains, which is encouraging to see.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	So if you see it, the work is such that you push a needle into the root of the part as far up as this, then push another needle where it has a double thread from the part of the arm.
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and pierce it, leaving the first needle according to the position.
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cut the thread with the double thread and tie a part of the wound around it, and tighten it well, then pull out the needle and apply the other moist lint in abundance.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and let it grow until the hair is long with the root, then treat the wound with comforting things until it is healed.
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and never should the wound be restrained with any part of a cloth circle until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the pain is greatly apparent, if you pierce it with a thin spatula that comes from oil, and draw out the albugineous moisture and straighten the joint, and enter again soon.
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the oil's fat
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease called "alcunnati" is only due to a gathering in the blood, resembling swift water flowing down, but it is not true water.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of performing the operation is that you place the patient in a sitting position with the affected part elevated and straight, then take the head in both hands, and move it until you see the gathering of blood rising towards your fingers.
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then it should be completely sealed, and the light should not descend or recede, so the patient can see things as they normally would.
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend on its own, know that it is acute, and the descent from the bowel is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	if you delay the patient in your hands, then take the delicate spatula and make incisions on the corny tissue following the continuity of the conjunctive with the corny tissue and the crown, as long as the bowel persists.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is removed, distill it in hot acute oil mixed with honey, or boil fennel and honey, then apply another remedy until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	des aigues de l’oil" translates to "water from oil" in English
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have experienced the forms of cuts in division, and what is necessary to pierce;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if in work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you place the patient between your hands crossed, away from the light for the sun, and tie the healthy oil tightly.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then place the paper of the oil in your left hand if the limbs are on the left, or in your right hand if the limbs are on the right.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if the joints are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the joints are on the right.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	then take the tip of the instrument and cut through the crown with a single, swift movement, starting from the thickest part towards the smaller end of the canal, then twist the instrument called "almagda" vigorously, and turn your hand as it pierces the inner layer of oil, and feel that the "almagda" reaches the empty space.
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is necessary that the length of the "almagda" be precisely equal to the distance from the tip of the prune to the end of the darkness.
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the crown of oil;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	if you see the bone on this paper due to the clarity of the cornea, then place the instrument directly on it or in the water, and express it from one side to the other.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he feels a sharp descent now, if he sees the patient before him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After resting for a little while, and if the water has risen through the second passage, place force with the instrument, and when it is firmly inserted and does not rise, gently extract it by turning your hand back and forth.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put back in sharp a little piece of silk thread, and remove from these oils inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply hot oil or any other moist oil, rosin, and an abundance of wax, and wrap with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, put a fine cloth over with much heat.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the mixture cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are many people with too hard eyes, it is necessary that you press the instrument called "alberit", which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then pierce only the joint tightly, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then apply almagda as we have said.
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and upon completion of the work, prepare for the patient a comfortable bed, so that he sleeps on his back in a dark place.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and he must be careful with all movements, consume light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his condition for three days.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then release it in the same dark place, test its sight, and make it see nothing, and then put back the bandage for seven days.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not advisable that you do this during the treatment or after the incision now, but it is necessary to lighten it, because acute pain rises suddenly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	if an abscess forms after seven days, then release the oil in front of the seventh day and follow the treatment for those who soothe the abscess.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when he is calmed, if he loses vision and puts on his face an eyelid to cover any light, and is thus in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	Then he goes out of the house little by little, and returns to his own affairs.
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and he knows that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from Iran, who told us that in their peaceful lands they make an instrument that extracts water, but I never saw anyone like it in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients.
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps it's a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the appearances of the forms of magic, for those who do not know them will see them as different.
et soient d’arain proprement:	and they should be properly arranged:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the center of this same subtlety be in one place, and the rear in three corners acute.
de la char sor le neis	Of the pain near the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	No creature ever born or formed with diverse joints will seem to be a scorpion made of pieces.
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if it has such as he has charmed with fox-like coloring, and if the charm is of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In this case, where the wound is sore and not yet healed, you should make the patient rest their afflicted part between your hands, facing the sun.
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open the patient's nostrils, and apply the warmth to those wounds, and treat them fiercely.
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then hold what you can bear of the thin, sharp spatula on one side, as long as you know that wound is entirely healed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there remains anything that cannot be covered, open it with all the delicate, light instruments until nothing remains.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and without worrying, or an abscess forming, if it is cut as necessary;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if these are malignant abscesses, act quickly and cauterize until the pus is drained and all openings are healed, then apply new ash and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the wound opens again and moisture reaches the mouth, knowing that it is clean;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if the moisture does not pierce as necessary, knowing that there is an obstruction in the bone above, which prevents the tools from cutting.
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Then you must insert a thread slightly thick, and be careful with your hands, and leave enough space between each one, either more or less.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and place the patient's teeth with the thread in their mouth, drawing gently until it comes out through the breath.
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and often children learn this practice, and it is easy for whoever wishes to do so.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head with one hand coming through the breath at one side, and the other hand holding the opposite side of the head coming through the mouth, alternating between them as we do with thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do as much as you know to purify the wound, then treat the child, wipe away the blood, and moisten the wound with Egyptian ointment, and put it back on the body as before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Apply the ointment for three days or more, until the ointments have penetrated all that is still stuck to the wound.
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put on a clean bandage for no more than a few days until it is healed, and if it needs further treatment with medicated ointments, do so.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the shape of the instrument to purge the head, from which the oils and medicines are distilled:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	and it should be of silver or gold, resembling an open lamp, like a candle, and lead it thither.
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you make a closed candle, and it is the instrument full of medicine for purging the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and it has many parts on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the pain near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a pain appears in the head due to a sickness called "telis," which swells and grows worse, as long as it is a visible thing to look at.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this reason, it is necessary that you grasp it firmly at the beginning, and remove all bones, then apply the burning cautery or medicinal fire.
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if it is delayed in grasping it as it swells, take care if it becomes hard, of a poor color, or lacks sensation.
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	do not touch it with iron, as it is an enhanced abscess, for when you grasp it, great harm comes to the patient.
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of a soft consistency, not filled with pus, and you can completely drain it without pain, then dry the wound thoroughly and treat it with things that heal and soothe.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and wounded
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when the flow of continuity comes to one of these powerful cartilages, it benefits little, indeed, for no man.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary to pay attention when this occurs, so that if the wound is fresh and filled with blood,
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then tighten the two lips with a stitch, and treat it until it is healed.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are separated on both sides, it is necessary that you cut away all parts of their core while they are healing, then sew together the two lips with a stitch and tighten it, and apply powdered dragon's blood and crushed incense.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and place a piece of plaster, strong or other plaster that binds, on it and leave until it falls off by itself, then treat the wound as long as it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The method of stitching is as follows: you assemble the parts together.
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the stomach;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	At first, the abscesses in the veins appear hard, similar to grains of various sizes, both small and large.
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then you must turn the abscesses and cut into each one, taking them with pliers and cutting into each part.
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply the leu (a healing agent) after the cut with vitriole (a caustic substance), until the wound is cleansed.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then apply the living oil of asil, and heal the wound with dry things until it is clean.
de la char des gencives	from the treatment of gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times a growth appears on the gums, tightly attached, which the ancients call "albus".
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	it is necessary that you hold it with pincers, cut off at the base, and let flow the pus or blood;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then place on it vitriol powder, or other restrictive and desiccant powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if it returns after the incision, this happens many times, if the wound is opened a second time, and cauterized.
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after the cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the shapes of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	from obstructions
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Never should they be assembled at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, the edges of which are ugly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and never should the tooth be black and yellow and rotten, as long as the corruption comes to the gums, and it stinks.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	If it is necessary that you hold the patient in your hands, and his feet be in yours, and you remove any bones or scars visible, until nothing remains.
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and thus do with blackness and greenness, and jaundice and other hues, as long as they are fresh.
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes what is at the first cause, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then read again the second time and the third, until everything is removed.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the tooth requires diverse tools to extract, according as the work shows, for the saw used to cut out the teeth has different shapes from those used between them.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these shapes and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is important when treating a tooth causing pain to take your time and apply gentle pressure as much as possible, for one should never do otherwise.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a hot substance, so one should have no excuse for applying too much pressure.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is constrained from drawing out the pain, it is necessary that you be certain about the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the patient suffers great pain, and believes it to be from a tooth or gum infection, and has the good tooth pulled.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and yet the pain does not leave them for this reason, until the evil is completely extracted, as we have already tried on these patients.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are certain of the tooth's pain, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth very strongly with a tool to protect the gums from all sides.
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then move your hands or the subtle pliers bit by bit, as long as they are well positioned, and then firmly tighten the pliers.
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and place the patient's dislocated joint in your hands between his knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth properly without breaking it, if it does not come out, take none of these instruments and push it gently from each side, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	and if the bone is broken and disintegrated, it is necessary that you fill the space with cloth, either at the wound or the opening.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if it is squeezed gently with pincers, so that it does not break when squeezed.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to carefully cut around the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Be very careful not to break it, and if a part breaks off, return the fragment to the patient; due to the evil of the root, he will experience greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And be wary that you do not act like the ignorant healers who, through their haste and boldness, break the body's balance, and do not heed what we have said.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but they bring about this great illness due to the roots that remain, or because of the imbalances that they create, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the swelling is severe, wash the affected area with wine or vinegar and salt.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and the bleeding that ensues, which often occurs, can be alleviated by applying the juice of crushed vitriol.
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize him.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shape of the instruments, with which you will first mute the teeth, should be long and sharp with thick handles, so that they do not bend when pulling the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let the tools be of good quality, so that they do not bend when pulling, and made of iron well-forged, and toothed for secure grip.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root persists when pulling, it is necessary to place a moistened cotton ball or butter (on the day or the second day), until the swelling subsides, then apply pliers called "algefri," which give the tooth the appearance of being cared for.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and they should be made inside as if with a chisel, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out of these claws, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put the instrument called "althali", which is a plier, whose form is as follows:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	and it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out, that is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if not, with all the tools, the shapes come as follows:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument with two prongs, its form is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are used in the treatment of teeth, and this instrument that resembles large pincers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	and this tool should be strong so that it does not break, and remember that many tools are inside.
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not mentioned;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the most skilled surgeons create their own instruments, according to what their works and the illness show them, for there are certain diseases that the ancients did not teach any instruments for, and if one breaks a bone or other part, and it becomes stuck, and he seeks the instruments that I told you about, with gestures that help form this:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	and they should be large and well-fitting to hold the bone, so it does not escape, but can be held and removed;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the limb to suitable medicine for this, and if there is decay in the bone, even if it is small, use all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth does not appear according to the body's natural course, and its shape is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the other teeth, and is not in the correct position, and cannot be filed or polished.
adonques lou raie;	then the tooth should be extracted;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is attached to the tooth, take this instrument whose form resembles a small beak, and make sure it is very sharp.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And take a small knife and hold it in your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it from one side as the shape allows.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the limb from which they make arrows;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and the tooth, little by little, gently in his hand, so that it does not move until it is completely healed;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then at the end, there is no cutting, and the teeth are too sharp and damage the tongue, so it must be leveled until it is even, so that it does not damage or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth hurts
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the teeth loosen, either through hammering or pulling, and the patient cannot chew what they want to eat, they should be treated with restrictive medications, but that is not effective.
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	If they need to restrain it with a thread of gold, for the silver's thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the amount of space between the bones.
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you need to align the bones, take the thread and loop it twice between the two healthy bones, then place the dislocated parts between the healthier bone, as many times as there are (dislocated) parts, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side firmly.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then recommence the covering up to the part where you instruct, hold your hand gently and firmly, until it does not move.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your finger be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	then cut the pieces of thread with pliers, assemble them, and insert them between the healthy tooth and the one with the abscess, so that it does not damage the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it so tight as it can stay, and if it loosens, the threads will come out, if released from another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it were to stay still and serve thus all its time, and that's the shape of the teeth and the figure of the correct arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two muscles, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth is dislodged, it must be gently put back in its place, one by one, as we have said.
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and do not allow anyone inexperienced and frightened to intervene; never should the shape of a tooth from a dead animal be used, and it is placed in the missing position, and held tight as we have said, and stays still and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Cut the skin around the tongue's surface.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	No illness is this one that comes from beneath the tongue or its origin, except thus.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or due to a deep wound.
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient with difficulty, place his head in your hands, and extract his tongue.
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the large nerve, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is stiffness or pain, and it's a sudden wound, pull the hook and cut through that ligament.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and ensure that the cut is not too deep, for the artery below.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done this, lift the arm with the red and swollen liquid, or cold water, and then place a cloth under the limb.
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and cover it each night so that the limbs cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if blood poisoning occurs, then apply a poultice of crushed vitriol to the limb.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if it hurts him, if he is cauterized with slow fire, which is good for him.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then apply other remedies as long as he is healthy,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see it is red or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it turns pale and there is moisture, then dip the spike in, and with a thin spatula, remove it from both sides.
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if it does not give way under your work, pour vinegar ground into a paste until it is stained, then return to your work until you have treated everything thoroughly.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift the limb from rest and relax it, and treat other treatments as long as it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	From the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Never does a hole open up inside the throat called "godath", and these are properly called "laryngitis", and when you treat them, as we have said in the previous section, and they remain unhealthy, be careful.
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If it is an abscess hard with a small, dark colour, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the prevention of pus.
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but leave it until it turns black, and then remove it, or it would break on its own.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of white colour with thin roots, then have ready the instrument to cut it, but first ensure that the abscess is cool and at ease.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and stretch his legs to their full extent, opening his mouth wide and gripping the lower jaw between his hands, pressing the tongue down with all the instrument's force, from which comes its shape.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and be of silver or subtle gold, just like fine knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Cannot you press the tongue down with all this instrument, and see the abscess, take the awl and screw it into the gum, pulling it upwards as much as possible.
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and do not try anything with threads, then cut it with the instrument, from which there arises a form resembling strength;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	but nevertheless the instrument is curved in one place and another, very sharp, made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, if it is like pliers, then this is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	and it has notches on one side and is smooth on the other.
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have cut one of the strings, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, rinse the patient's wound with hot water, cold water, and clean air. The discharge of pus occurs if the wound is rinsed with hot water, or cooked pomegranate skins, or mint leaves, or similar things, until the infection has been washed away.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it as long as it is sound;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and never does it produce other abscesses in the throat than the two mandibles, so treat them accordingly as the two teeth are attached.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was new inside her throat, that is to say, a small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and had a great deal of swelling closed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained in that state for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed two ribs through the two openings in the throat.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hastened to do so, and inserted one needle, then drove it through with force, and extracted a great portion of bowel.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then repeated the process on the other side through the opening with another needle, and opened the mouth and pressed the tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	after inserting the needle into these abscesses, and extracting a portion, only a little blood came out.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the airway of the woman was opened from the throat, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting into that abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and it made the abscess reopen again, and filled back up the vein I had drained, as long as it was very large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I secured it and cauterized it inside the throat.
ensi demora sens croistre;	so it took time without growth.
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I withdrew from these parts, and only God be the judge after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the eye returns to its socket, and it is swollen and distant, it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is removed from a large and round object, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the previous section, but the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscess has subsided, and it is subtle, then it is necessary to drain it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and the one that is round and compact is not too distant.
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is red or of a dark color, then it is necessary to carefully make the incision on it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the ill patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary, when you see this, according to the manner I have said, of cleansing and lengthening, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we spoke earlier.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the hook into the eye, remove it from inside, and cut with the first of the two instruments I spoke of during the incision of the two stones.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cut off more than the excess beyond the natural limit.
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	because if you do not handle it well, it will cause pain to the voice and speech.
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use the same method we described for incising the second mandible, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient feels great pain, it is necessary that you use a tool for cauterizing the sensitive parts.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of cauterization is very hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient places his head in a healthy position, and then presses his tongue with the instrument described in the chapter on cautery (fire treatment), using sharp live coals, so that they are neither too thick nor too thin.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and in using this instrument, by which there is formed:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And let the patient have a mirror or some object to apply the medicine, as if it were the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should lie on their side, so that the saliva and mucus from their mouth can drain the medicine, without it going down to the throat, and it remains clean.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then take your hand, holding all the medicine, and press it onto the eye for a quarter of an hour, until you see it relax and the pain from the medicine is soothed.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and insert the instrument entirely into the wound over the cotton until the cotton is saturated with the fluid.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, as long as the cauterization is perfect, then leave it to dry, and after three or four days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to redo the cauterization with the medicine, when you redo it, after the cauterization, wipe around the eye with cotton soaked in butter and change anything around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let him be raised from cold water, and cure him with gargles until he is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This cure is safer than incision, rather than cauterization.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take plenty of calament and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and similar herbs, and combine them all or some of them in a pot, add water, and boil.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and into the pot put a shovel-like instrument according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And whether it is of silver or gold, and if one of the joints is squeezed in the mouth of the patient until the vapour rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye becomes numb.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	after the swelling often recurs, while the eye is dry, and be sure not to do this at the beginning of the formation of the abscess, as many complications can arise.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not make any movements except during the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not available, take a straw and insert it into the patient's mouth with a piece of cold cloth, so that the mouth does not get too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	Because the heat of fire does not allow moisture to accumulate in the mouth, it is a good cure that brings overall healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Often, it causes a burning sensation in the throat from bone or fish spine, or any other thing.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	So it is necessary that you treat what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you may observe the thing moving.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And if it does not open and is withdrawn into the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit so that the food may be cooked in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	in case the thing goes the other way through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patients swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of cauliflower, or a lettuce root, or a crumb of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and it passes through the sponge, and then it is regurgitated;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it reaches its place, if it is stuck, then it should be pulled forcefully;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come from what we have said, take a plunger tool according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	and the tool should be curved at the tip so that it can more easily enter the throat, and hold the head slightly elevated.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, so that all parts do not come together, and do not push any bones inside.
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is important that the patient pushes on the tool, because if he does not, the object inside will be stuck.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If the bottle is swallowed, pull it out with all the instruments equally as far as possible.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the mucus in the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Never should medicine be given without examining it, as I said in the previous section, through the treatment of medicines.
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and if it does not help, then look in the throat of the sick person towards the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, pull it with all the small hooks or subtle pincers that are suitable for it.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if these are not suitable, take a horsehair and insert it into the throat of the patient, then pull or gently tug on the hair; do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has fever all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in slowly, moving the tongue with your hand frequently.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if he feels a sudden cold, then it is certain.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not give way as we have said, then the patient should be given the instrument used in fumigating the eye.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will become easier without targeting.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of fumigation is that you heat a pot with hot coals, place a perforated cover over it, and in this opening, insert the instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then he applies the fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes it, so that no smoke comes out, but only the steam.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the steam will now separate, and if it does not, the fumigation should be repeated many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient will suffer from thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, but not drink water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it is better for him/her not to speak against this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which the blood is treated, if it can be seen, resembles curved pliers for entering the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and it resembles the beak of a bird of prey, and has the hardness of lime, so that whatever it takes hold of, it cannot let go.
et vez ci la forme:	and consider the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many signs of an abscess are, as the memory comes to us from one side or the other in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and this is in two ways; one is by its own likeness, and from that which holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the upper part is different from that of the lower, and the abscess of the fleshy part of the limb is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if at abscesses one must not pierce while the bowel is still alive according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if of such (abscesses) it is necessary to pierce when they are hardened and do not die according to their completion, as with abscesses that are in delicate joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	Because when an abscess comes from damaged joints, and it is left as long as it is rotten around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Or, if the abscess is in the principal member, and you delay piercing until it is dead, it will harm the principal member.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	if you remove the foundation, so that it is pierced in such a way that it dies.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not advisable that you pierce an abscess without completing the healing process, otherwise, if the one who removes the foundation does not heal completely and remains inside, a fistula will develop.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and it will not heal completely.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you know the right time for piercing an abscess when it has healed completely; this is when the pain is relieved, and the fever departs, and the pain and redness diminish, and there is a smooth recovery, and other signs.
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you make the incision sit more dependent on the abscess, and there where it opens movement.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the incision should be deep into the flesh, and if the abscess is near the surface or in the joints and tendons and arteries, and everywhere it is even, without any curvature.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And for abscesses that are in soft flesh, it is better to leave the incision until it is completely healed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it in front of that, the flesh around the vein will become stretched and filled with a lot of filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance, the edges may harden and become deeply embedded within it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if at any abscess that is pierced according to the thickness of the flesh, as needed by the member.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And you must treat them with small incisions, small openings.
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large incisions, large openings, and many cracks according to the size of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if with such abscesses it is necessary to pierce the heart, then cover it.
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become dry like the skin, and is stiffened, then it must be treated like the buboes:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if they are of such a nature that they are cut in three angles, and if they are of such as are also cured with myrrh, like abscesses from attacks;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if they are of such as require a large incision, or other sized cuts and similar treatments.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those that have no head, like a superficial sore, it is necessary that you pierce it deeply;
