et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large and has great tension, and you pierce it, if you do not draw out all the tension at once, but only a part;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop the abscess until the other day, then draw something from it;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times gradually until the bowel releases entirely;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	most often the patients are of weak spirit, or pregnant women, or small children, or old, frail people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For sometimes the spirit jumps at the outcome of the bow, which might cause the patient to die, and you should not be alarmed by this.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	therefore avoid this chapter with great care, and when you have perceived your abscess, if the wound is clean, and check if the abscess wound is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a clean cut, apply these attempts of linen or old cotton;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess with many openings, you should insert a tent into each one so that they come together.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have managed to remove a part of the abscessed skin and close it, you should fill it with old cotton or dried linen rags without moisture and bind it for three days.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the bone, and the treatment of healing as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the infection spreads to your work, then apply cold water and ice, moisten the bandage, and lay it on the affected area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the bleeding persists, apply government and cure, and the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter or the veins and abscesses are very nervous, then you should place these moistened cloths of wine and hot oil upon them.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in such a state, and the vein is fleshy, then you should place moistened cloths of water and oil, or wine and fresh oil, up to the third day, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then release the abscess and wipe it clean and treat it as necessary, so long as it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And it is necessary to know this universally in the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	for it has been said to you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and now let us consider this chapter.
des soros	from blood
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or there are many small abscesses that come from the heat of the head, and they are like threads, as well as the sinew of a chicken, and they have many similar appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are thick and such, where there is also moisture as well as pulsation;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if it is of such that are hard and difficult to cut, and there is no doubt that the artery does not act contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the thigh is such that you should test all instruments called "intrusive" with which the following form is obtained, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they make a hole from above down long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is drained, if nothing remains in the skin that contains the moisture, because it repeatedly returns when nothing is left.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then immerse cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, with water and rope, and apply to the wound, and leave until the other day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and they will correct those who are delayed in healing.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then begin the bandage again, as before, on the second day, and third, as long as you know that it does not delay healing.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound with healing remedies as appropriate, as long as it is clean.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess remains firm, as per this form, for a long time;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and immerse them in water, and scrape them from all sides, and put all your effort into drawing out the pus from the wound where it lies.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if it causes him pain, do as I have told you.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Also, treat an abscess that is painful, and cut it and cure it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut the abscess first and moisten it if necessary; for it is filled with little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if none of these abscesses or joints have moisture, and it is one of these deep abscesses that I found on the shoulder of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess as hard, sharp, and white stone that cannot be broken.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if none of these helps, one should also make a wound as if from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other cases of abscesses occurring in the head or neck, those who come as leaders of children and affect the roots of the ears, the opening should be kept completely open for as long as possible to allow the pus to drain.
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat it as appropriate.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess appears in the neck, and it discharges pus, and causes pain, and never comes elsewhere on the body, and it is full, and twisted together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each ulcer is properly within its cavity, just as the neck and abscess in the head, as we have said.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others of a malicious nature that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that one which you see of good disposition when touched, and resembles the color of healthy flesh, is quiet from every side and has no signs of inflammation in the collarbone or in the artery or in the duct, and is not too deep.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	it is necessary that you cover it from above, and strip off the skin from every part, and the two lips of the heart be opened at the same time, if you need to, as we have said in the chapters on the head.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	And move it little by little, and be sure not to touch the nerve or vein, and do not cut with the spatula or saw, so that the hand does not slip, and do not look too far ahead, lest you touch something you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you touch the vein or artery and it does not allow you to act, then apply vitriole (a caustic substance) ground into a powder that stops blood, or any other powders that prevent clotting, and close the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscess is calmed down, and the wound is softened, and begin to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the patient is stained with blood, he returns to your work, as long as you complete it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then seek your finger's sign if there remain no small bumps, if they are clean and smooth.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein at the root of the bump, it is not enough that you only remove this bump at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and leave it to fall without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then apply the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then dress it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you clean the entire scab, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them now, so that there is no delay due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you need to understand how to deal with the root of it, and pull it out, and cut it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofulas that hold an excess, cut there where it appears to die.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and the cutting should be done as previously mentioned, depending on the situation, then it is administered with bandaging and similar things, so that it corrupts none of what remains from the corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is clean and free of infection, if the healing bandage causes pain, as long as it remains healthy.
de squinance	squinance (n.) - squint or astigmat
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients spoke and discussed about the incision of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen it done in our land, and it is written in their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those with a squint, it is necessary that the fold in the throat, called the epiglottis, be avoided.
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and no help is done through them, because all the veins and the pores of the sick are hot in those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both jaws.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the urethra's channel, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss caused by strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it in three or four small slits diagonally, between the two circles, or according to the size of the slit, not into the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and if these muscles are suitable for cutting the epiglottis, so that there is no scar, and the vessels are long and thin.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is timid, it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to the entire bone, and then cuts the heart until it reaches the chain.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the tissue as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the cutting of the throat's blood vessel that jumps out from the place which is broken, and by the loss of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and keep the wound open for a time.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed and there is doubt about the strangulation, gather the two edges of the wound together with care, and cut through just beyond the cartilage.
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that promote healing as long as they are clean.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says: One should not proceed with this until the throat is completely closed, and the patient is considered dead, lacking all breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he will breathe through the wound, thus preventing death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and for this reason, the ancients instruct to keep the wound open until the ill will of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they command to sew up the wound and treat, as long as it was cured.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a damsel took a knife, and inserted it into her throat, cutting part of the tongue from the side of the mouth.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and I found her also as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was coming from it, and realized that it had no power or passage to the outside other than through the throat, and the veins were emerging from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and stitched the wound, and treated it until it was clean.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and having no further use for the damsel until her voice had returned, she later resumed her proper position.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	because I say that in the operation of the epiglottis, one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	from the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	A cystic abscess is called a "neck hernia," and it is a large abscess with the color of an arrow, and it occurs mostly in women.
et est selonc II manieres:	and it is according to two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	naturally, it has no engine.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two manners: one is similar to a tumor, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that arises from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and fear is present, and one should not attempt to make fire outside in the open, but rather in a small space, testing and examining every opening.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you let it grow out as much as a new grass, and it does not give way to any force, if the bone breaks, just as we break bones of others, and treat it with all care, if there is no pain.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	surround it closely, and treat it as appropriate, as long as it is completely healed.
des nous	From us.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of doing this, which I will describe in detail.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary that I explain the distinction between our methods and those that come from elsewhere.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that it is caused by heat and fever as long as the ebullition has not passed and the putrefaction is complete.
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then rest the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With no new heat, fever, or pain, and it retains satisfaction, which is its own sac and is according to the condition of the body, and begins also like a wound, and becomes large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to their appearances, whether fat, moist, or of a certain color, as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You should, when you approach the treatment of a new patient, that you test and inquire first about all the instrument called "entangling" (entromissoire), according to its form as it appears in this chapter or the following one.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of inquiring into abscesses is that you press more or less moistly on the abscess, and move your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the center, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the instrument, and be careful that no part remains inside.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture is running across the wound, what color it is, then do as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and after the insertion of the probe, no moisture enters, knowing that it is full, so make it cross-shaped, and take it as pincers, and gently scrape each side and protect the wound where it lies so that you heal it sound with new tissue.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot heal it sound, then take it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	Because if nothing remains, it will return to the body many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a little remains and does not cause you harm, then apply some corrosive powders to the wound, tighten it, place hot soothing poultices on top, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if it happens to us, when we cut both lips of the wound, and the treatment of those who cause harm.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the pain is intense and other remedies fail, use the juice of vitriol ground, leave it on for two or three days until the wound pus forms, and let the fever of the blood subside.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to cover what has been exposed from the wound.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the shapes of the instruments used, which are of three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	great and strong and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three quarters which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three ways:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	great, strong, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistulas;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like needles used to pierce sorceries, made of gold, or iron, or silver, and the ones that are yellow are more effective at encircling fistula abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the opening's size.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the incisions are very similar, as you can see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	great, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if the incisions have two curves in three ways as well;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if there are those who have three curves, and they are also of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if there are others who have two curves, and some with only one curve, and they are of three kinds;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all of this is necessary for their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The leader of these, which are made to be sharp, and there are some that do not cut well from both sides, which scrape the skin, so that one cannot cut into the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and from these intrusions, the stitches are removed in several places, so that the patient does not lose them when opening the abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	great, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and do not use them on any part of the body that is not muscular, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar areas.
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and never does one use another small instrument, resembling the soles of hands, according to this form, to stop the blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it never rests in its place which is beneficial for veins, arteries, and always returns according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Never do the breasts of any man swell when they begin to be corrupt, as long as they appear like a woman's breasts.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain idle and weak, and anyone who wants to cure them should be careful according to this form in this line b until g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and apply medicinal fire, then bring together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healthy;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and hold the eyes steady, relaxing them due to their great weight, as it happens with women, making a kind of split in two ribs, through these similar openings;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one holds the other at the end of each, ensuring the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to line .g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape off the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have mentioned about stitching and powders, as well as anything necessary for the treatment, while it is still healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if he is not healthy, or the incision is not completely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood flow, it is necessary that you fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive dressing.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it absorbs the moisture and fat, then treat it as soon as it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	from the abscesses of armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are hard scrofula or have nodules, and if they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line B to line G.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, apply old cotton to the wound and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with suitable dressing until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, then do as we have said for cutting out scrofula, and if the wound sinks in, apply cautery as we have mentioned before.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is bloated and the skin above it is closed, this often leads to abscesses, and likewise occurs in the swollen vein with an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if you recognize it thus, as it is for an artery, then cut the abscess long enough to open it;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your hands, if it feels strange;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is for the vein, there will be red swelling visible;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cover this abscess, especially when it is deep in the flesh and full of anger and other parts, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is necessary to avoid iron treatment, and he who has a strong pain should also avoid it, and for him whose artery bursts open through the skin from above, cut deep into the flesh.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then operate on the chest as one does with wounds, and carefully remove the artery from the tissues while it is still exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle from beneath and pierce it through to the other side, gripping the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you regarding the extraction of the two arteries located in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then point to the place between the two links of an instrument until there is no pain remaining in it, and loosen the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the treatment with caution, as long as the wound is open.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply this treatment with care, as long as it is clean.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is the size of a vein, it is necessary to hold your hand over it, from the abscess to all the skin, then insert the needle through the flesh and pierce it, and use a double thread so that you can pull it out from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then, as I have told you, take the abscess, or one of the parts of the bone to the joint;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the thread is not strong enough, if it rebounds another needle into all the parts of the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tightens the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then, cut the abscess until the surplus part comes out, then cut off the surplus from the center and leave what is bound.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place on it a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, then administer treatments of bandages and poultices until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	Of the abscesses of nails
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, so too do they appear in nails when they are damaged or subjected to excessive strain, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this occurs more often in joints and limbs where there are displacements, which are abscesses, and their appearance seems to be the color of the flesh, and they are in various positions with pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when they tighten it, the patient feels pain, and is not completely healthy in that part, but the pain radiates from the heart.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and it must remain still from all sides, neither moving forward nor backward, up nor down, and the one that is in joints should not be covered with iron.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	in case they contract
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and whoever is on the head or forehead, makes the skin split with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	if the abscess is small, if you have pliers, cut it at its base;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, if he suspends it at the corner and scrapes off the skin, then cuts out the bone and reassembles the wound with stitches, and treats it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	Des grosses boces pendans" translates directly to "pendant large mouths
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	It never appears in the stomach or anywhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its similarity to roots, and it has thin, large droppings.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and it has small and large droplets.
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I have seen at home those who had them in their bellies that were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, had a delicate root, and were constantly moist.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I collected them and found in one eighteen ounces heavy, and in the other six ounces, and the work of the incision is such that if you watch, the patients are moist, and the colour of the articulations is white and moist and of delicate root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if it is collected with a wide spatula, and they are in your presence, perform the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For cutting often brings too great consequences of blood loss, and if it without your notice, then hasten to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient afraid and filled with fear of the incision, take a well-made thread, tie it as we have said, and leave it for a day.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	then restrain it, and do not stop pulling the thread until it dislocates the joint, and thereby achieve relief.
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are thick, be afraid to dislocate them especially for the stomach, but you can still dislocate half of it, then cauterize it so that it does not return.
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then treat the wound, and ensure you do not cover the part that is red, painful, and full of pus.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess magnified, and I will come to the treatment of this ulcer afterward.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the bowel is blocked.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the lump arises from cauterization of a wound or an incision on the soft tissues, and it is located on the belly and not in any of the bowels, as happens in other openings, or due to blood clotting in veins or arteries as described previously, or from abscesses;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is through the opening of the soft tissues and through the discharge of the bowels, then the abscess has the color of the flesh, and it is slightly painful without much discomfort, and it opens up in various ways.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to an intestinal issue, then it is more diverse, and when pressed by the fingers at its opening, it returns, and sometimes becomes constricted, greatly expanding at the bath entrance or through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a minor thing, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, it does not constrain.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it is due to blood, it opens up in these signs: abscesses large and hard, and are fixed according to quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work involves observing whether the appearance is due to blood from an artery, a vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary, you must leave the cure.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter about abscesses, both for the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or the bowels, you should instruct the patient to raise his leg and keep it straight, then tie a cord around all around the abdomen.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then command him to twist slowly between your hands, then enter the joint that you have marked throughout its entire range of motion, then pull half of the abscess above all the great hook.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread or firm silk string tightly, and make sure the bandage is securely in place.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open half of the abscess extended over the bandage, and insert your finger index, pressing inward to explore.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you feel it is firmly stuck to the bandage, loosen it gently, and press outward on the intestines away from the abdominal wall.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you feel the boil, if it is taken at the right time, and cut off the surplus.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the arteries or veins run counter to your work, then return to your task and take two needles, and force them through the flesh, and push both needles back in the same way you made the incision;
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then strain the abscess in four directions over the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the flesh until it heals, and draw out the dead flesh by yourself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	You apply the knife when the swelling is gone and manageable, then treat it as we have said, and heal the abscess.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the area as appropriate, and bandage the wound.
dou chancre	The first sentence translated from Old French to English is
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have spoken in the previous section about the appearances of ulcers, and how they must be treated with medicine, and how one should avoid iron treatments.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and let us speak of the ulcer spreading in a dangerous manner, and exercise great caution in its treatment, and advise the patient that when an ulcer is in the flesh or can be cut out like an ulcer in the mammary region, or in the foot, or similar places, it must all be removed as soon as possible.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, you should not even approach it, for I can never make it whole.
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	no one can ever make it whole before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And for the works when it is in the air or can be removed, as we have said, do not at any time purge the patient of black bile.
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make it healthier if there is evident fullness, then perform the work on the patient's good limb to carry out the task.

de ydropisie	The term "dydropisie" appears to be a
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have previously discussed the similarities of hydrops and described how the assembly of fluid is formed in each case, the signs of each condition, and the treatments that are effective through medicine or iron.
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only slightly dislocated;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one must not use iron in these two instances:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	that is to say, tympanitis and ypopharacy, for it is a deadly thing;

Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And make incisions from both parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	with a point, but not so deeply that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and cannot tear:

et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is due to mucus, then it should be on the right side, and it is not advisable that the patient lies on top of the cut so that excess fluid does not flow into that weak joint.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and pour it out, and lift your hand from all the slime between the skin and the flesh as if you were scraping with the size of a fingernail or in any other way.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the flesh until the slime is completely removed and dry, which is when the pain ceases, then pull out this instrument and it should look like this.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	and it is similar to a small silver chain, made of fine gold or light bronze, and has a small hole at its base.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and from one side, three openings;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and from the other side, two; and another from another.
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and it is cut like a feather, and this is the form of the incision in which the scribes cut the feather.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at the top of it is the groove, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it now sinks onto the instrument.
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	Empty the body then, half or a third, for if you empty more than is necessary at that hour, perhaps the patient dies due to the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls into a coma, or draws near to death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the disposition of the virtue in the patient signifies, and his pulse.
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then take the instrument and hold the water, which is now retained by the cauterizing iron that seals the opening on the affected part, of which I have spoken, and pierce according to this manner.
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then continue with the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering from this, and take a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do this every day, and be careful not to force it until it heals but with a little water.

et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and apply drying medicines as long as he is healthy, and cauterize the stomach and liver and spleen after draining the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	from the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born who does not have an opening in the penis, or if the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary for him not to pierce through all the very subtle spatium according to this form,
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	Then take a subtle hole in the bladder and close it and hold for three or four days when he wants to urinate, then open the closure, let him urinate, and then close it again.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and if by chance he does not remember, because the strong flow of urine does not allow the closure to be kept closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening is small, it is a sign of a weak bladder closure, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the hole in their bladder are cursed, because no one is born with a hole at the top of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they close their penis.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot move because the material cannot reach the joint, and it is a great illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the method of performing this procedure is that the patient lies on their back, then the doctor makes an incision at the base of the spine and also cuts across the chest as if it were the size of a quill, so that the opening reaches the depth required.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be careful of the bloodletting that occurs frequently, and if it happens, apply pressure to stop the bleeding and treat the wound until it heals.
