de la circoncision	On circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not a complete healing process like other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	however, when we perform this operation of our own will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best and lightest work for their salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they do not practice it in their laws, and we have acquired knowledge of it only through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have sought out most of the masters and wise ones who perform circumcision around the anus, and have learned from them all, a new technique.
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	if the veins were different because there are two layers, and perhaps one is cut above and the other below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	or if he re-covers it, the pain is doubled, and the cleansing of the wound around the anus is not assured for the point of the member.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and to the cleansing of the nail, perhaps the fire escapes and corrupts the work, causing the wound to heal, and often they grow back in such a way that no further cleansing is needed, which I have witnessed.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the cleaning that is done with force on every link of thread, I have found the benefit of experience, because the forces cut exactly as well from above as from below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, cut it evenly through all its parts;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but make sure the thread is well twisted around the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and let it be the gentle manner of the first operation, so that the child, if he hears, believes that you are only tightening the thread around the stick very gently, and then make him forget in all possible ways.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then make it stand straight between your hands, and restore the strength between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see any of the tools.
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	then take your hand to the staff and blow on it with your breath, and hold it up until the end of the staff is in place.
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	then thoroughly clean it from the dirt that is gathered on it, then tie the joint with a doubled thread, and bind it to another limb with a new ligature.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it in both hands at the second tie, with the little finger and index finger, and cut between the two threads, then gently lift the end of the staff.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow little by little, for it is the cause.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and sprinkle it with a powder made from a mixture of cooked egg whites tempered with rose water, preserved with good rosined oil and fresh herbs, and leave it until the next day, and treat it with another remedy as long as it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The method for purification is as follows:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	both feet should be clean and cut, and the toes should also be as long as the rest equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The mistake of purification is when the veins are cut open;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Then it is necessary that you extend it with your finger, so that the veins do not form an abscess.
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and hold it even, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then use tweezers to hold it and cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they remain for three days, and what is under the stick is swollen, leave it until the abscess is calmed down, and gently peel off the skin.
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	if the cup is as you can see, and you keep it from the part of the stick, it will not harm him in any way.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Treat therefore the sudden wound from gunpowder, which we have spoken of in dealing with powders, and if the cup is made of hard material, and it goes above beyond measure, it will do no harm.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure it therefore, as we have said, while it is whole and healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is a sign of stone or frozen blood, or bowels, or a blocked duct, or similar conditions, as we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine cannot be passed, it is because of a stone in the bladder or at the neck of the bladder, so it is necessary for the patient to bend over on their knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and they should place the feet on a chair behind them and extend their stomach from above the back, and restrain the patient sideways as much as possible.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then it is necessary to constrict the bladder neck at the level of the stone above, so that the urine can be passed.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer the extraction of all the instrument called "syringe", whose form is:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it should be made of fine, light silver, like the feathers of a bird;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and the length of the handle should be one palm and a half, and it should be thin at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the method of urination is as follows: you take a double thread, attach it to a small ball of wool or cotton at the end, and insert the threaded end into the syringe.
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut off the excess of the line and the flesh just above the chief of the vein, then anoint the vein with oil or butter and egg yolk, and place the patient in a reclining position, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis downwards towards the buttocks.
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	then squeeze the syringe before reaching the bladder, and let the patient feel the flow until it reaches the empty space, and this is not done correctly if you do not follow these orders, for the direction in which it flows is twisted.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then take a thread and pass it through the wool little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out forcefully, and let the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and repeat the process until the bladder is empty and the patient is comfortable.
des maladies de la vessie	From the diseases of the bladder.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or inflammation come to the bladder, due to an accumulation of putrefaction, you should draw out water and medicines using a device called a "clepsydra", and it is shaped as follows:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	it is closed, and if it opens again:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	from one side, and from the other, as you can see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the hair that is used for cutting the medicine should be such that it effectively numbs the pain without addition, if we can extract the moisture and apply as needed.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see your medications in the bladder, place the head of the knife into the moisture and extract with gentle pressure from the one who is inside.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	if you extract the moisture with the knife, then press firmly on the one inside.
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	if the moisture enters inside and comes into the bladder now, so that the patient feels it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of a delicate enema by which the bladder is enemased:
si est ci:	if this is so:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	and it is of silver or gold, and is the highest part;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and take it from the heart where the veins burst;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture you intend to use for the enema, then wrap it between the two breasts formed by a good double thread, and heat the mixture over the fire.
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then soak the head in a cleansing bath on the thigh, then press your hand against the bladder to all the moisture coming out, until the patient feels that moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle of it, and punch a round hole through it.
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then insert a strong thread into these openings, reassemble the circle as you would a nut and bolt, and place inside what you see fit (oil and moisture and water), and secure it with the instrument.
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do as you did with the bladder, pressing it with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have previously discussed the methods of cutting and extraction, together with all the medicinal remedies;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and I have said the distinction between surgical cutting at the joints and all the signs, and in what kind of cutting we must perform carefully.
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder occurs more often in children, and this is a sign of acute bladder infection, similar to the sharpness of water.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and I open her widely, greatly alleviating the patient's pain, and repeating this process many times until it becomes harder.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and it attacks the foundations of these stones.
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and it is gentle healing for children until they are four years old, and it is much more painful in the elderly, and it is halfway between those who are young and old.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and the cure is lighter for those who have a large stone, than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient through a cleanse, in order to draw out all impurities from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often obstructs the effort to cut into stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and straighten them, and move them to the side, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and it never moves up again.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	then make him sit between your hands, with his hands resting on his thighs, so that the bladder is tilted downwards.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	then take it (the bladder) and feel inside;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel the stone in the passage, then hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not yield to pressure from the fingers, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is weak, or your middle finger, if the patient is younger and fully grown.
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and press it into its base, hold the stone, and when you feel it in your hand, if it's at the neck of the bladder.
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press with your hand, and the stone will move away from where you feel it, or where you see it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the patient to press the bladder with their hand, and command them to extend their right hand upwards, and with their left hand, remove the skin that lies beneath the stones in the area where the cut is made.
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	then I squeeze the sponge thoroughly, which gives it its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	and make an incision between what is between the buttocks and the base, not in the middle but on the side of the left thigh.
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and be straight on the stone, and your fingers should be together at the base or on the thigh, and cut across with a sharp blade so that it is wide enough to accommodate the stone without being too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	in case the pressure on the fingers at the base causes it to move suddenly without effort;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and he knows there is stone or it has edges and corners.
si est griés a issir;	if it is caught while emerging;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if it comes out of a sore, resembling a gland, and red, with a thin discharge.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	At such time when it has edges and corners, make the size larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not yield, you must use pincers that are also like a file at the tip to extract the stone so that it does not escape.
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	you must remove the sharp instrument from its place on the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot do it thus, if the wound becomes large and very painful, and if there is no discharge of pus, but only a straining of vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there are more than one stones, you must first remove the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut it out, and afterwards deal with the smaller ones if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, they want to pull it out, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things often happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	if he dies, or urine comes again through the place where the bones cannot join;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but nevertheless, make every effort to extract it or clear it out with pincers, as long as you treat it piece by piece;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bandage it, and place on top a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess;
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Then resolve the patient's complaint on their collarbone, and do not loosen the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, if a lot of warm oil and water comes out, then apply healing ointment and basilic treatment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if abscesses appear in the wound and cause corrosion, and blood clots form in the bladder, and due to this, urination is blocked, known in such a manner that without warning with the urine.
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	so then press your thumb on the wound and extract the blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and it will decay.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then open the wound with heat and vinegar and salt, and aid it in every way that you can, as long as it remains healthy.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and it is necessary that all the wounds you treat, tie both legs to him, and apply the medicines on the joint.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	and if the stone is small, and it is located in the urethra, deeply embedded, and urine cannot pass through.
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if you treat it as I say, cutting him many times, then the size [of the stone] is excused due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have tested this myself.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take the iron at the front according to this form, and fix it at three angles in one stick.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	then take a thread and tie it around the urethra behind the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder.
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then gently turn the drill into the stick until it reaches the stone.
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the drill back to your hand in the stone little by little, as you can pierce the stone from another side.
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	if the urinus (urine) comes, then press your hand against the part that is stuck from the stone inside the stick.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	if it is broken and jumps out with the urine, it cuts the patient;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do this for any reason, then remove the stone from inside and place it outside on top of it, then cut the stick across the stone between the two edges, then pull it out forcefully, and loosen the ligament, and cleanse the frozen blood in the wound.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it while it is clean.
de la piere des femmes	of the women's stone" (referring to kidney stones)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	Very rarely do stones occur in women, and if they do, the treatment is difficult, and it is hindered by three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	One reason is that perhaps the woman is a virgin.
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second reason is that one cannot find a woman well-versed who exposes herself to men, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third way is that, perhaps, one cannot find a woman well-versed in this art of healing.
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	And the fourth way is that the skill of the woman is often more excellent than that of the man, so it requires deeper incisions and great care. If need be, one must appeal to a well-versed mistress, and if she cannot be found, then any skilled but chaste seamstress will suffice.
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and it presents a wise dance in the life of women, where a woman who knows a part of the art, and commands her to do what you command her from the examination of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and carefully consider if this woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then she must remove her hand or finger and seek the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, despite the constraint of her finger, she recommends that she remove her finger or hand with the patient, and press her left hand on the swollen bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If it is cut, it is necessary to move it little by little from the entrance of the bladder down to the thigh, until it reaches the root of the thigh.
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then cut into the stone at the root of the thigh, finding the soft center where it is most movable, and feel the pain in that part.
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move it far from the stone, either up or down, but make the first cut small.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then push the blade into the cut, feeling the pain as deeply as possible, and know that there are many ways stones can be removed.
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	This is to know, both small and large and sharp, and smooth, long and round, and which have roots.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	knowing these similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the wound does not heal, mix powdered vitriol and apply it to the place, holding it for an hour until the pain is relieved.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, as long as the stone is hard, and have the tools I told you for extracting stones from people to assist you in your task.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if the wound is from an artery that has been cut, apply powder to the place and press with tenes and bands, and do not repeat this, leaving the stone and not pulling it unless the patient might die.
puis cure la plaie.	then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the eyes open, return to your work while the stone is still hard.
de hernie carnouse	herniated cartilage
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Rameal water is nothing other than the assembly of moisture or white of egg, which is beneath the skin, containing the heat.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and it is called "syfac", and it is never properly in the membrane of the egg, if one considers that it is another egg.
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and this is the skin around the egg, between the white of egg that we have mentioned.
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and this happens no more.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is due to weakness in the organs, and this material expands.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And it never happens from striking against the bones, and this moisture appears in many forms.
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it changes to jaundice, or lacks red, or becomes black, or clear white, and this occurs more often.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to recognize this collection, for if it appears entirely white as we have said, then the abscesses are red, deep like an eye, and do not open the bones, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the wound bed, the abscesses are red with a portion of the flesh, and because of this, one thinks it is another wound.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white part, it smells good to him.
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	then when you see to know the color of the moisture, try to test all the inside thoroughly, from which the form will be as it is now.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what follows then, after the introduction, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to his ability and the replenishment of his body;
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then place him on his back, on one thing slightly elevated, and cover him with many sheets.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit him on his left side, and instruct the attendant to sit on his right, and extend the staff towards one of the two ribs on the heart's side.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the scalpel, and cut through the skin of the ribs from top to bottom at the elbow, and make your incision entirely straight by cutting through the ribcage until it turns a satisfying white, carefully removing the flesh according to its natural inclination.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	then pierce the swelling with a sharp instrument through a large opening, and drain all the fluid, then apply your bandages, and the swelling will subside.
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the heart of the swelling, but only the swelling itself.
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	cut it all or in pieces, carefully along its side, for if you do not cut it cleanly and precisely, the fluid will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the foam jumps out of your control, make sure it stays in its place as you complete the work with the swelling.
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then join the two books of the skin at the seam, then treat it as other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the fever corrupted by another illness, it is necessary that you bind the vessels that are suspended, in doubt of the flow of blood.
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	then cut the skin from all that is suspended, extract the fever, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the arrow is assembled into two parts, together forming two branches;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	if you treat the other part just as you did with the first, then wipe off the blood, and apply a clean moistened cloth with rose oil to the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and apply another moistened cloth with wine and oil, and place two bandages over it, and cover it with double-layered cloths, and tie it tightly according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths, make them of sheep's wool according to this appearance and sew them together at the neck of the pants, one on each leg, close to the crotch and at the wrist.
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other side of the head, on both temples, it should be entirely compressed in the bowstring's loop.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and under no circumstances should this cautery branch be applied with a hot iron, but rather use a delicate surgical knife to make incisions into the skin, and warm it as we have mentioned before, so that the white part containing the blood becomes exposed.

met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	With your two index fingers together, place the woman on her back, spreading her legs.
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	Then form the two leaves, as long as the subtle pain is gone, and be aware of the stupor.
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	Then take wool and dampen it in oil, and place it on the wound, and lay the woman flat each day, so that she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the substance is hard and thick, it is necessary that you cut it with a scalpel resembling a sprig of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the dislocation is from a fracture, then suspend it at the joint and the bone.
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and use the blood-stopping medications, such as oak bark, dragon's blood, incense, and plenty of egg yolk.
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	then apply a wide bandage, so that the wound cannot heal.
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and so do this for a long time, and apply a dry linen compress.
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then he should be treated with other remedies until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when fever comes from heat, it should be treated in this manner, especially if there are abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For abscesses that are aggravated during fever, they should not be prodded or touched to drain them.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that, without proper care, can become enlarged. When hemorrhoids have been present for a long time, they tend to get worse.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	and we have spoken about the divisions, similarities, and signs, and I will now describe those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and their complications, when they are completely in the anus, and they do not appear to be felt, can only be cured properly with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the anus can be felt; these are the ones that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is therefore advisable to place the woman in a cold house, then apply hot compresses to the affected areas, and use poultices with herbs that constrict blood flow, such as aloe vera and dragon's blood, and similar remedies.
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	then immerse his feet in the wall for an hour, then place them in cold water;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if the bleeding continues, one should apply a poultice of sumac and bark from pomegranate and gallnuts and similar things, then take oats flour and mix it with honey and oil, and make an emollient to place on their back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if she is tired, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If that does not help, one should apply cupping glasses on the back without harming the mammary glands;
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	then take flax and moisten it in the juice of plantain or olive with old wine, and apply to the dislocated joint.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess has healed, apply a clean dressing to the wound as long as it is healed;
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a sharp point, so it should be covered as I have said in the previous text.
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then apply the cure as long as it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	about abscesses in childbirth
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the body, such as chancres and previous abscesses, herpes, boils, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	Therefore, I should tell in this treatise about the hot abscess that appears in the thigh, which is not a true abscess but one that bows its joints.
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you want to know the work of iron, look if the abscesses are active at the beginning of their appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red, then you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	then do not hasten to pierce, but make it die while the pain is soothed;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then make the patient lie on his back, and have him sit up with small cushions, supporting himself on his elbows, crossing his legs away from the affected part;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let his legs be spread apart, and place his arms beneath his knees, and bind them firmly with a good bandage.
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then push the bail towards the right side, and insert the instrument used to open the wound's mouth, from which comes the shape.
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you insert this instrument, you first feel the depth of the wound, so that when the instrument enters, it does not go too deep and harm the patient.
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instrument is larger, it needs to cover the entire depth of the bandage, so that the instrument does not hurt.
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary that he places the horn of the instrument above and turns on the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscess opens and it is done gently with the hand, if it needs to be covered, it should be done at the top, with the spatule lead.
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	and when the bowel is emptied, it is necessary that you put into the wound moist tents, either in rose oil or in dry green oil;
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and take the tent of the wound completely over the margin, and place it firmly over the margin and on the inner side of the arm with clean moistened lint made from herbs or wool.
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it after two days of healing has come to it, as long as it is healed;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and never lift the margin and the wound with a cleansing of water and honey, and then water or cooked roots of lily and aristologe (herbs) long.
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then return to the healing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed in the inflammation, it is necessary that you be careful about applying heat, but treat it as we have said in the previous section.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	Skill is most important in midwifery that she knows the signs of natural childbirth, and these are when you see the woman hasten below, and desires to smell the ar (spice/herbs).
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	then the child hastens to be born.
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	so know that these children are according to the natural figure, and their issue (i.e., limbs) come out with them.
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press the abdomen so that the child is born quickly.
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	because as it descends onto its head, if it is attached to it, then it tightens the hair roots with proper purification.
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and this is what comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it never comes upon its feet, but rather penetrates the body or affects parts like hands or strikes the belly or back, and sometimes turns about by chance onto its neck, or in other harmful shapes.
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	so it requires skill in the art that it be wise and subtle in these matters, clearing itself of error and disappointment, and I will show you all the shapes how one must aid it.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If a fever comes upon the head due to natural causes, and a woman gives birth severely, her strength is weak, if she lies on a saddle, or women hold her that way;
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and if one's natural oil or fennel seed is cooked, then take a small spatula in the shape of which...
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and split the second layer, and cut into her fingernail as much as the moisture that is deeply embedded;
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and press the woman's belly as the child descends, and if it does not descend, it is necessary to enema the woman with fennel seed mush mixed with licorice oil;
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then make him breathe deeply and sneeze from the condition, and hold his mouth and nose for an hour.
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	if now the child is born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if both hands come out, it is necessary that you reset them gently, little by little;
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a chair and raise her feet up.
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then lift up the seat from the ground, and tie down the woman so she does not try to stand up.
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if her hands cannot enter, the child dies, if she cuts them with a knife placed before her, and extracts the child, then reset them both equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the birth of the child on his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes onto its feet, it is necessary to push them up.
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then make it even smaller and smaller, until it is level.
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then press upon it with your hands and stretch it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	can he jump up to his toes, if commanded to press, and makes him sneeze from the condition;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if he jumps up, God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not happen as we have said, he should turn him little by little according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes slightly lighter.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not come out as we have said, take a small amount of musk, and oil from the eyes, and melted gum, and grind everything in a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and place it on the nature of a woman within and without this treatment, then make her lie in warm water reaching down to her ribs.
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is dampened from below, make her wear a collar of myrrh and place it around her, and leave it for an hour.
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her lie on a seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose tight, and press gently on her belly, for the baby is now ready to be born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the passage of the child through its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the fever comes in this form, he should raise his hands little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then he should rest on his collarbone, with the weight hanging down below, and lie down on his side.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and he should bend his hands little by little, then take his hands and place them on his belly, removing the pillows from below until it is flat.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the fever does not subside, he should take his feet and move them forward, then raise his belly upwards, and then press his hands.
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and let the child grow and grow;
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and instruct the woman to conceive while the child is still inside.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the birth of the child who comes with a large hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	I know how to bring the hand back:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if it cannot be brought back, then one must raise the woman and move her along.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot move, then have her lie on the bed with her legs straight.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then remove the mucus I have described;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, but the fetus remains in the womb, then study how to bring it down by pulling on the hand.
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and pull the child out according to its natural position, make it sneeze, and command that it strain until the baby comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on its chest, with its hands spread and its face turned away from its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	I know that the pulse has its hand, then it presses little by little, and turns it slightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when they are even, he should place a mucilaginous and oily substance on them, as we have said, then he commands that they move little by little.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, if the fire is on a seat, command it to burn intensely.
et la fai esternuer.	and it causes sneezing.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner, throughout all of this.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it manifests in this way at regular intervals, take a cotton swab and remove the moisture with your fingernail.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and it ties itself to its face and neck, if the cap of the wound is not held, it will die.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then bring the child inside, as long as you have placed it properly, and tell the woman not to move at all.
adonques si istra legierement.	then gently straighten it.
de l’issue des gemelz	From the emergence of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	Know that many times twins are born, and never more than three or four at once;
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and this is by no means a strange thing, and often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	These are strange things, and do not live, but have no name.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they multiply, and are devoured by the satisfaction of him who devises them, who is bound to the bow.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and they never appear as naturally as all of us, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they are severely stuck, if the treatment is as we have said, and it is a cunning surgeon, then make it tight and gently do what it does.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do so as it deserves for health.
de plusors enfans	from many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	Never are they formed in the joints I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and they are all formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of their noble wisdom, and it is necessary that the skilled surgeon knows all this, for by chance, something similar might happen.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	if it is done according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman with a dead or pregnant child, as I said in the previous section, and there is no discharge, and you are compelled to use forceps;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is necessary that you know if the woman is of healthy virtue, and has no risk or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is necessary that the woman be supine on her back, and that her legs be inclined downwards, and raised;
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and treat the wound of its second part, where it is attached to the bed so that it does not heal until after the birth of the child.
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the mother with moist oils mixed with fennel and fenugreek seeds, then apply this mixture to her hands.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	then gently squeeze the mother, and check if she releases any pus, making sure that it does not descend onto her head.
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	If the thorns become stuck in its own joints or in the neck or mouth or inside the throat or beneath the beard or on the forceps or near the ribs, and this penetration is on the surface, stick or press it gently against the bones.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he holds the thorn with his right hand, and places the claw between the fingers of his left hand, and presses gently with his entire hand, and sticks the thorn into any of the joints we have mentioned, as long as it reaches the empty space.
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the thorn:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then find another joint, where you need it most, so that extraction is even;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch it evenly from side to side, so that it can be moved and the joints become sharp, as is the shape:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if part of it remains, and if you cannot move any of its joints with oil, press the oil into that part and pull on the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if nothing remains, then move this joint higher up and do until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes forward before the other and cannot return due to tightness, it is necessary that you wrap it up in a cloth until it heals completely.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	then cut it at the joint of the foot or the knee, and so it is necessary that you do with the other hand, and have both feet bound.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the child's head is large and stuck in the birth canal, or it has a sharp point assembled, it is necessary that you press the spiny forceps between your fingers, and do the head and extract the blood.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	You cut it with the instrument called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the tools or chapter that follows this one.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus, I myself make it attach firmly at the great natural strength.
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then pull the bones with pliers, and the joint jumps out and is seized by force, so that it may be split, until all moisture that was causing trouble has left.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot be extracted, then break it into pieces until you can move it.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if he is bloated in the stomach or has fluid in his ribs, then you should pierce it until the moisture is drained.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the fever is on its feet, it has a light pull, and the direction to the opening of the wound is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	If he is constipated in the stomach or has a stone, then it is necessary to pull it out with a grip on the enveloped drape around the hand.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and making the stomach or intestines empty, until the moisture within is drained.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if any other part of the body is broken and the stool remains, apply pressure with your hand from the outside of the anus, and pull it towards the mouth of the anus.
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	Then he heats the fire and plunges it in (the affected area), and pulls it out.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the wound is constricted due to hot inflammation that has come upon it, it is not suitable to work on it, but instead moist and greasy things should be applied.
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and apply it with moist plasters, and immerse it in warm, softening and lubricating water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on his side, and you can make it even, then apply what we have said for the living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one cannot, if it is broken into pieces, do not leave anything of the ligament.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when this is done, apply what we have said about the incisions that come to the wound;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if the inflammation comes, it should be treated with severe restraint, and other remedies should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had been cut open, and I consulted another on that wound, who healed the other wounds.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there comes a abscess in the cheek, it swells until it opens, and begins to cause severe pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called upon to treat it, and I thought for a long time, but I could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong poultice, and an bone came out, and after a few days, others followed.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought this was a bone from a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I examined the wound, and pulled out the bones with my hands, until the woman was in better condition;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and he should examine the woman long times thus, and then let go a little bit of pressure from the blue.
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I remember this chapter only because, when the master encounters a strange thing, he knows how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the woman back to her place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	After this comes the form of pressure, with which one binds the books.
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and at the second turn, as the second joint of the limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle in their tightening, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth should be wide enough for two fingers, with a margin of wood, about one and a half palm lengths in length;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and also both limbs should be equally adjusted with this same wood, firmly fastened together, about half a palm length or slightly longer;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and this double adjustment is tied at the opening of the wound to open it when you turn both horns.

et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and it should have two adjustments, as you see, of one palm length, and two fingers width;

puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then use your hand to handle all the tools, just as you have done with the pincers evenly, according to the amount that you see open the mouth of the wound, until the pain ceases to do what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	All these tools are skillfully crafted, and they are numerous in their varieties;
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when you see them properly equipped, the work becomes more rapid, and the results better for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disregard the instrument if you have not prepared it, for the need for it is not an excuse for negligence.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine (a tool or technique) is used during childbirth, it is important to instruct the patient to hold her breath and then make her sneeze gently, while pressing your hands on her mouth and nose.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she jumps through this, it's fine.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If the vein is not accessible, I take a small pot, make an opening or cover, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as calamine, fennel, chamomile, cassia, and centaury.
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all of these herbs, or none of them, should be cooked or put in water over the fire.
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then place a cane or small pot over the opening and put the other end in the mouth of the wound, and hold it until the vapor goes inside the wound.
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	then make the patient sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second treatment does not help.

si venra et se desaerdra.	If it comes and goes away.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the wound is tight and painful, we have said the remedy of sneezing and fumigating herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not of all that we have said, be careful not to follow the treatment incorrectly.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is important that one who has the wound in the mouth, you bind it to the thigh of a woman, and then enema with four-ingredient medicine.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if the wound becomes infected and is treated, and comes back again;
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but nevertheless, if it stinks badly in the stomach and head, and causes the patient to become ill.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	Then it is necessary to use suitable fumigants:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	no one of the ancients has tried fumigation with parsley and dried figs.

Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is like a glass vessel, and one places the head gently in its natural form, and the base wide over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let there be fumigations over the coals, and the scabies until it is completely healed, and then repeat another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who have not yet had their foundations pierced, but nature has sealed them with a subtle satisfaction.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	so it is necessary at the bath to pierce that satisfaction with a sharp instrument, and do not let it touch anything;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place it on a moist cloth with wine and oil, and apply the dressing until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not return, insert or open a plug of cloth, and leave it for several days, and it will be removed when the swelling goes down.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And at no time does this stoppage of the wound or abscess occur suddenly;
si covient coper celui soudement:	it is necessary to cover this stoppage:
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	if it is cured, as we have said of the pain of plunging.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from its origin
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that originate from beneath the foundation are called nodations, and those that come from above the foundation are larger, or in the space between the two parts, if there is a fistula or several.
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when this nodulation is old, if it becomes inflamed again due to moisture, causing white or subtle pain, and these fistulas do not persist.
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and they (the fistulas) are known by those who observe the patient's excretion or venting when the patient passes wind, and sometimes one jumps out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if the fistulas penetrate just below the bladder, and just halfway up the penis;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and reach just below the knee joint, and almost to the top of the thigh.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus you recognize the present fistula in the fundament, and it is not present.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you push your index finger or fundament, and push a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is curvature, if you push a slight blow or a horsehair, as long as you feel the tent or hair with your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come out with extraction or venting or movement, as we have said;
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	says that she does not feel any pain;
si te haste dou curer.	if you are in a hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists up to the bladder or up to the urine conduit, if it lets go of the urine, and cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is felt just at the joint of the thigh, then there is a strong tendency for veins to form close to the place.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no curvature or pain around it, and if it bows slightly, but does not suddenly improve with dressing, then medication is of no use.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these persistent fissures, there is no certain cure but effort and the vain efforts of those who interfere with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In those that are neither persistent nor old, there is hope of healing through fire, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies on their back between your hands.
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and extends the legs up to the thighs, bending the thighs towards the stomach.
