Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels pain throughout their entire body, it is necessary that you press your index finger into their side, and they will then feel the point penetrating.
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and if you feel the heat or cold between your thumb and index finger, then know that it is present.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if it is not treated with care, it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	Nevertheless, it is possible to heal no one at all, but this happens rarely.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and with the help of this, if it is made with a delicate cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said above.

et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this twice or three times, as long as you know that these charred marks must be burned, which resemble the feathers of an eye.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then apply hot, moist compresses until the charred marks disappear, and then treat with a soothing ointment that seals and soothes.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is in this state, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If this, in no other way, can be healed;

si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut from the beginning of the fistula and pull away before attempting to cauterize it, then after a while apply the heat to where the tenting begins.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and he will be freed from pain, and cut.

Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	Because fire cautery requires two good things:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	namely, the burning of these adjusted parts, and the irritation of blood and the dryness of moisture;

puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then treat the wound with hot, burning coals and dry medications.

Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way through to the very bottom of the body, and it is distant from the flesh, if you press it into its origin, and feel it there.

ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it deep, or if you can remove the itch and treat it as first.

et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and it is when you press the tent into the fistula, and it is on the side of the deep foundation through the skin above, then take a precise tent at the top in this shape:

Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, try to open it in every way you can, but if it is too closed.

Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	It has a form of very sharp, spiky spine from which one makes the fistula if it is much swollen and hard, cutting through one side.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand no, because one cannot copy what one must not copy, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	There are two types of memories:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are within the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are both small and large ones, and sometimes blood, and sometimes many, and they are pushed out from the fundament and towards the top of the fundament.
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are too dry have little moisture, and still, now or a little of citrus water or a little of blood, and have the colour of fresh flesh;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those who have them deep within the foundation, so you instruct the patient to stretch himself to move around in rooms, until the foundations are strong and the children appear.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you act quickly, and have a pen with claws, or hold it with your finger nail, then cut it at the roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if they cannot hold them for their moisture, if they take them in a drape or cotton or a piece of chamois;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and extract them at the right time, then cut them and sprinkle hot powders on them, which are suitable for cauterizing.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, and apply other remedies until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot come out, if you give the patient a harsh and biting enema to wash what is in the foundation, so that it can come out firmly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	Let the patients hold their breath and keep their eyes closed, so the hair can grow long and even; if they wiggle or move, it will cause pain.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and if you press them with your finger or pliers, cut them, and then treat them as we have said, while they are still healthy, and they do not fear the incision with a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	It is necessary that you perform the stitching in this manner:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	take a thin thread, twist it into a needle, and then pass the thread over the top of the needle, and pierce it from the other side, and bring both ends of the thread under the needle, making sure it's not too tight;
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and hold the thread taut, then tie it off, and extract the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave some for draining the excess blood.
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place a moist cloth or oil-soaked rag on the affected area and lay it down, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it until they heal, and when the wounds have healed, apply treatment and other remedies until they are cured.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Carefully consider the sources or foundations.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often, there is a drying up of sources (or causes) in the intestine, due to constraints of nature, and when the illness is old and no medicine avails.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you scrape off the skin with a spatula or your fingernail, which will prevent it from getting moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat it as long as it is sound, as it should be;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be healed, begin the operation again with greater force than before, as long as it is still fresh and there is bleeding.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal it as long as it is fresh.
dou fremit	He trembles.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	a flea is a small, hairy creature that burrows into the skin, causing much harm.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and it never cools down, and he feels as if he is dead from the tremor, spreading throughout the body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a feather from an goose or a strong falcon's feather, and place that feather on the tremor until the red circles cover the tremor entirely.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand over the entire feather until you cover all around the tremor, and press it firmly, and extract the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make this of a steel or iron wire according to this form, and be subtle and draw them from below and above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	I do not perceive, so as to keep the hand steady, and it moves with pressure.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see, cauterize the tremor as it is before or at the beginning of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a douching
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Never use silver or gold enema, or molten lead or alloy.
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and never use these small and large instruments, according to those who administer them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	He who is thus entrusted with the care of children, especially those who are weak and in pain, should be small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the bladder should be small and narrow at the top, wide at the bottom; the belly is bound according to this manner.
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and I say there is a desire or the belly should be restrained, as you see, and the excretion of feces should be felt inside.
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and it has two openings on one side and one on the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and the belly should be filled with medicines from a bladder of good leather or parchment, and it should be pricked all around in small openings, and there should be a space between each opening, then thread through these openings with strong thread twisted cruelly in X shape or similarly around, and tighten the belly as if it were a bow.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is applied, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread, then enema.
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and it takes the form of a soft circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and apply to the enema head oil or yolk of an egg, or a similar substance, then gently bottle it.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then the healers should press with both hands together until it is entirely full, then remove the enema and have the patient lie down against the wall, and let the medicine come out as much as possible.
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps through the night entirely, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the enema for a stomach disorder and the medicine quickly escapes, then it should repeat itself until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoid is at the anus or abscess, it should be treated with just as much subtlety as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle cleansing where the skin is tightened.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already discussed the treatment of wounds.
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or I will tell you the treatments of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to where they are located, and according to the type of wound, and from what they are caused.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the use of stone, and sword or knife, or spear or staff or arrow, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or according to the laws of the body, such as a wound that breaks through the skin, or on the head, or the leg, or the belly, or the liver, and similar parts;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and begin with simple head wounds, because the remembrance of them will come in their chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head, and the bone is not broken, be cautious if it's due to a sharp object or similar things, for the skin is still torn and the wound is deep, and you slightly doubt an abscess forming.
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if it quickly becomes healthier on its own, especially if the wound exudes little blood, and the healing is on the contrary of the affected part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and the patient should abstain from wine and rich meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to heal, his flesh should be reduced, and he should not drink wine, nor eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and apply this to the wound; if there is an abscess, take it out, using either oil mixed with rosewater or wine that is astringent.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, apply to the fresh wound while it still has all its blood, and do not move it with air or any powder, which I will mention later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it moves again, even if any sparks are present, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like the size of a sword or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by tenting, they should be sewed shut, as I will explain for abdominal wounds, using stitches.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and it bleeds heavily, but only for a short time, then it should be treated.
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then treat the wound with medicine, and replace the skin with hard flesh, and instruct the patient to eat substantial meats, such as tests (offal) and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	If you find putrefied flesh or skin that has not reached the bone, but is rotten throughout, cut it off and treat the wound.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if it has an artery in the wound or vein, which without cut, cannot be stopped by medications, if you sever the artery, and if you dislocate it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and it is that you apply this powder which heals so that the burn moves.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the method of the powder is thus:
pren encens une partie;	take a portion of incense
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood in two parts
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	take live charcoal in three parts, mix it finely with the wound and form a compress, until it spreads well and joins all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then bind it well, and leave it unbound if it does not swell.
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	because one cannot take medicine as long as it is fresh.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never should charcoal be used alone, unless you have incense or dragon's blood, but the fire must move the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the wound has changed or moved, especially when it is fresh, unless someone applies this powder to it.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply no poultices or compresses made of ground oats mixed with water and honey while it is still fresh.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply other remedies as long as it is fresh.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a bone fracture occurs with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with delicate pincers.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you below about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the collar (or neck).
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the neck and it is simple, then it has no distinction from that at the top, but if there is damage to the nerves or arteries in the neck.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nails, then there is no other tool but to let the cure happen and do not put anything restraining, for it harms the nails and makes them retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not apply anything sharp to the wound, for the substance of the nails is cold, and continuing treatment from outside affects the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be prepared, as if washing with soft water, mixed with rose oil, and also washed in soft water, and other herbs according to this method, and moist plasters.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cutting it open and binding it with bands, then heal it until it is cured.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	and if the wounds are deep and infected, and filled with pus, then pierce them or deeper still;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and pus flows, then follow these steps, and apply the proper law, and cauterize accordingly.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spine in the throat is cut, or the colors, and the flow is preserved, so that the flesh goes, as much as the color touches the bone in the throat, and do not touch the throat but return it according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then the gradual improvement occurs, and do not let it for any days, then cure the wounds afterwards until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, so be it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are pieces of bone, if you can remove them all, and those that you cannot get, if you leave it until the wound putrefies, and becomes gangrenous, then let it heal itself;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle it with the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones or a fistula in the wound, treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a blow from a lance or a sword, and the wound is deep, then pay attention to the direction of the flow of blood as the patient himself indicates.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	then know that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep, and the blood flow is fresh, do not apply the powder immediately, nor bind it for the blood to stop completely, lest it return to the body and further harm the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but I apply an attractive remedy, and bind it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you have no remedy, place much cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient lie on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no coming of spasm, no bad shaking of the body, or disarrangement of the limbs alone.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good disposition, then you know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Cure the wound with various remedies and others, as long as it is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, operate, then know that there is a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	if the cure is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is shallow or deep, on the front or back, then treat as follows;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is great, of stitching;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, of powder, and if it is tightly packed in the bone, and has cut through pieces, so that the wound is exposed, and treats them fiercely if they are infected.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not infected, then leave the wound to heal, and lighten the extraction.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds in other parts, the judgments are as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	disorder of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures in the belly are great, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the great wound, never let the intestines spill, or the inner lining of the intestines, so as not to allow foreign objects in;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the stitching is more delicate, and never as good as the small wound as compared to the large one, because we do not apply enough pressure to the intestines when stitching them up;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines quickly become swollen and feel painful if not stitched properly, making the smaller wound easier to manage, because we must first reset the position of the intestine in its place before stitching it up compared to others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common stitches are used in stitching the belly, and the stitch for other wounds of the body, and there are two other specific stitches that are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	However, they are more specific with the stitch for the belly, and I will describe each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no leakage of the intestines, and the thing to be stitched is easy to manage, then this is one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	For the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the injury.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	Moisten a sponge or take a soft cloth in hot water only, or cook in water with ginger, cinnamon and cloves, and soak the intestine until the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and never make this wine constricting, but it should be moved to reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestines are filled with water or blood, and bad humors are cooked, for this is lightens the entrance to some degree.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a slight wound with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is to move the limb, so we must not cut without great need.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for dividing:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if he cuts deep into the flesh and does not divert it, then see the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestine protrudes, return it to its natural position in its proper place, if you are able, for this is movement.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is large and located in the lower abdomen, it is necessary to have the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the lower part of the belly, then put the head and feet higher than the affected parts, and also turn the patient to one side so that the painful area is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And so we must administer what I say to great wounds and minor injuries.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	Treat small wounds by preparing what you have at hand, then take in your hands a gentle ointment that will heal all the cuts to its tip, and bring together the lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	This is the common method of stitching: you pierce a needle or more than one, according to the amount of space in the wound, then leave two spaces at the top of the wound, and insert a needle or strong thread where it feels right.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce both joints through the leather with both joints of the knife, which is to cut through the leather from inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part, and bring together the two joints of the knife in three parts.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then stretch a double thread around the needle from both parts, then bring together the two joints of the wound properly, and then leave two spaces, and insert another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then tie the thread just as you did with the first needle, and continue this work according to your need for needles, until all the wound is secured.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and they should be needles of medium size, between subtle and thick, for the subtle needles take up all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot enter properly.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	because they need to be medium.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and one should not push the needles too deep into the flesh and through the skin, as they can open the wound before the suture.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then remove the needles, so they do not cause the patient to bleed while sleeping, and place bands or cloth under the needle marks to prevent movement, leaving them until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this stitching method with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it requires only one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitch is common, and it consists of assembling the two pieces of skin and the two pieces of soft tissue together with a needle using a strong, thin thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have secured all these pieces together, return the needle to the beginning part where you started, in the manner one sews clothes.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and place enough space between each stitch, about the thickness of a smaller needle.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch opens the wound, and I sewed a wound with one of my hands on the belly, which had been cut by a knife; the wound was more than one palm wide, and it extended from the intestines two palms wide, and the wound was in the stomach.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its proper place after it had remained thus for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed completely within fifteen days, and it was cured, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they had all given up hope that he would die, and it was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with any treatment, for I was in a place where none could be found, neither medicine nor help.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and apply a clean cloth over the wound twice a day, and wash it with honey water until it is healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and dip it into the blood from the affected part up to this point;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the center in a straight line, if the point is lifted or the stitching or where you dipped the needle, and pierces from the inside of the affected part up to this point again;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as a tailor sews the fur, leaving once satisfied on one side and taking up again on the other, until the stitch is entirely completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second way of stitching, which Galen rightly calls, is like no other, assembling the two parts together naturally, and applying one of the ends satisfied to the other end in this manner.
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	take a needle or a piece of thread close to a mirror, and pierce only the left side, leaving both ends of the thread satisfied.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the distant part until it reaches inside, as far as the affected part.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce both parts from the distant side until they reach inside, in two other places where there is miracle on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most effective method of stitching, and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Many dispute these words, and no one testifies to them, so one must sew the belly with needles, or thread each one.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and you should push one needle from one side, and the other from another, in the manner of those who sew corsets.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, it is the most difficult to sew than other rips in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you pierce the fresh wound and all its blood, so that the arrow has moved it, then it should be pressed to stop the flow of blood and the pain.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then apply the enchanting powder over the burned area, and if the wound still burns, use any available dressing until it heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and then sew the wound closed with thread, ensuring the stitches are secure and tight;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you have no medicine, apply this instead: repeatedly change a clean cloth on the wound every day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need other medicines in various arrangements when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound affects the principal members, it is necessary to apply a light bandage in warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the wounds, and between the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if it feels pain or discomfort in the bowels, and this often happens, they should enema with red wine, especially when the corruption reaches the intestine.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it from within, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestinal tissue called "jeun" cannot heal when it is weary, and this is due to the condition of the veins, and the subtlety of the entire body, and the nearness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the plug jumps out of the wound, put it back as it was in the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and has turned black, you should leave the part that is black, so that blood does not come from venoms, because there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut off what is between the links and hang the two parts from the opposite side of the wound until they come out, so that the removal of the plug is easier, and the wound bends.
de la routure dou boueil	From the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in no man, for I saw a nobleman wounded by a spear in his belly;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became infected and developed into a fistula, and from there came expulsion and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to be subtle until it was healthy and the wound healed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it heal, I doubted that the patient would not have pain in his stomach;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there is no harm, but it waits for better dispositions, and foods and drinks.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and they should not attempt any experiments when there is a small wound in the intestine, but it must be treated in this way.
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take a large needle, then gather the edges of the wound, and when the needle has opened the mouth, place it between the two lips, so that it pulls the mouth apart.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cut off the head of the needle, and this should hold so that it cannot be released, then insert another needle in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed.
et cout la plaie.	and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the pain is sharp in the intestine and causes no harm to the patient, it is possible to bind the intestine with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the end of this intestine thread, which is well spun, and then tie it to the end of this fine linen thread twisted, then thread the thread through the needle, and sew the intestine, and rearrange it in the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of stitching with foreign matter is not useful except according to the path of promise and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it affects one of the vital organs, there is no remedy but subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	or whether it is a fistula, wherever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	You know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is generally called a "fistula", especially when it is covered with hair and deeply seated.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula appears as a hard and white nodule, without pain, and is also smooth like the quill of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and it never appears clear or thin, sometimes thick, other times sparse.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	never too little, and never too much;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of wound divisions, that any wound which is not clean, and there is no char, it is only out of one of the nine causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, because of the smallness of blood or pus;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its evil nature;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard matter inside, and on the lips, which does not allow any discharge to form;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	as there is too much bowel movement;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or their bowels are filled, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or such medicine is not good for healing;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	because this corruption is the manner of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	because due to the proprieties of the region, digestion is slow, health is delayed, and it is weak in nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	There are veins or bones here.
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already described all these causes, signs, and the cure of medications in detail.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I inform you about the treatment of a fistula which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	You should know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body.
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that affect large veins, arteries, and nerves, in the stomach, or intestines, or bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spine in the back, or any joint in the hands or feet.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it occurs at the property of the main member, and has similar joints.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this nature are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but hard work and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is no fistula that does not come to the place I mentioned, and you have confidence in the treatment, and you see it take effect, take a piece of iron or steel, if the fistula is deep, as you wish.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is twisted, try a thin piece of lead or iron, because the plunger will bend and follow the curvature.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and it cuts the hands deeply and you cannot properly search for them with your fingers if you clean them through one of the openings, because moisture passes from one opening to another, cleansing them.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then cut it deeply with your knife, so you know if there are bones or nerves, and remove the blood completely, pressing it firmly, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press, and the location where they feel it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know the location, and it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or any of the places I mentioned earlier, then cut according to what I told you, and remove the foulness and corrupt flesh that is within.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the treatment as long as it is healthy, and if the fistula is deeply placed in the right direction, it is necessary that you remove it completely, as much as you can, then apply moist bandages with astringent medicine, and keep them pressed to the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then apply hot compresses with healthy charcoal, as long as it remains healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	if it is not healthy, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, remove it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not affect your principal limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackening, remove it until the corruption is entirely gone, then apply remedies to heal the wound as long as it remains healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it remains unhealthy and turns bow-shaped as before, know that you are not yet allowed to proceed.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if it becomes exposed and you wish to go deep, remove all the corruption, then restore the joint;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if they are thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If that is not the case, know that the corruption is too great, and you cannot overcome it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other force but to surrender to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small, corrupt bone that you can pull out with tweezers, and if it is removed with a suitable instrument, and if there are many bones, they should be pulled apart without leaving any behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if moisture makes it contrary, there is no doubt or fear, if it is hot and moist and hard, and releases the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, apply something to the wound that promotes putrefaction, and leave it until the bones are softened around them, and then they will be more easily removed.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh bone, apply the putrefaction treatment so thoroughly that all the blackness is removed, and then dress the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a great deal of decay in the heart, it reaches almost to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is necessary, cover it with cloth and protect it until the decay is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurs in a man's leg, so that you can take an example from it and receive help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	It was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something inside the body, causing matter to accumulate in the leg, and he had a large abscess that would not open.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but because of their madness, they pricked the abscesses so deeply that they caused much damage to the body, and it became a fistula, and many holes appeared throughout the body oozing with pus and moisture.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many people spent more than two years without cure, and there was no wise man in the art of healing, until I was called to it, and I saw his leg and the medicines used to heal him, and what healed through the holes in the body.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man turned red, and it had the color of amber.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these gaps, and then I examined all the gaps, and I found that some came into contact with each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I quickly prepared a tool, and inserted it into one of the openings until I discovered a piece of bone, which I found corrupt and broken, and the corruption reached right down to the bone.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I realized what I was seeing in the corrupt bone, and thought that there could be no further damage beyond what I had seen.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to treat the wound with strong remedies for a long time, but they could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I tried again, and discovered the bone just as before, and found that the corruption continued within it, so I treated it and then reset it, and focused on securing the joint.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I cannot do it until I have completely healed one side of the bone, and pulled it out from its socket, then treated it with medicine.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it became healthy and whole again, and did not wish to repeat the treatment unless due to the weakness of the patient who could not endure, or for the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because for the complete evacuation of blood, it often happens, but it was completely healed, and a hard callous grew in its place on the bone, and it was of good disposition and caused no harm or discomfort at all, neither from going away nor from coming back.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it should be treated in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take a ligature, and pull it at the end of the bone that is open, and command anyone to extend it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and tie I another thread of a thicker nature to the first one, and attach it to the flesh that is beneath the bone, and focus on the joint, so that you pull the corrupted flesh from below, and expose the flesh on the bone where you wish to heal, so that the wound does not become infected.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and insert splints or a table beneath the bone to cover the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is important to observe and feel the corruption, and do this several times.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if a bone is corrupted, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then it exposes all the flesh.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then place hot coals from beneath, and then gently from one part to the other, spread the corruption, and so the healing is long from the corruption as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and either extract the bone or repair it from the other part.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuity of two joints, then there is no other choice but to cut them.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in the hand or foot, it is very strong, but you must inquire about this corruption how it opens.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it in any way you can, but ensure the vein or nerve does not oppose you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the saw and the threads to join these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and fineness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this, it is necessary to have a suitable instrument for each type of work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you the instrument you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so consider the instrument you need, according to what is suitable.
dou feu	Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The dislocation may occur due to internal or external causes.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have treated that corruption with remedies, and they do not help, then it is necessary to cover that limb up to the joint where the corruption has occurred, so that the patient might escape from death or from the greater evil of a fault in the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs of this are that the limb turns black, as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackening, then that corruption spreads from member to member, and takes over the whole body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if you hurry in covering it, and if it is due to the bite of some venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion or snake or similar, then that corruption is at the top of the limb, if you cover it, do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, so that the joint is dislocated, preventing the corruption from reaching the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it extends to the arm, so that the dislocation is at the elbow;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it goes beyond the elbow, it is fatal, and there is no cure except to measure the quantity of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and thus do the same when corruption or pus appears.
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	If it affects the first joint, then cut after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it affects the foot, then cut through the entire foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises up the leg, then cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the manner of cutting or sawing off the limb is as follows: you tie it down from above and below, extending one minister (cutter) on the lower joint, and another on the upper joint, and you sever the flesh that is between the two joints with a large spatula, until the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Then apply the poultice or linen, placing each layer of lint so that it does not touch the healthy skin, and bring about further injury and abscess for the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if the blood flow continues when you work, cauterizing the vein too quickly or applying any restraining powders.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your treatment until it is complete, then bind the limb with a strong bandage, and dress it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you if it turns out as expected at home after some time.
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	He had a blackening that seemed to be a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his right foot, spreading over the entire foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when he saw the corruption, he would cover his foot and it would heal.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and after a long time, the corruption returned to his other hand, and it came to me, and I put upon it things that rebound after purification of the body, but he cannot stop the corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he told me to cover his hand, but I did not want to, as I had hope of rebound the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also doubt if he cuts off his hand, he will not die, for the strength of man was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he became desperate, returned to his land, bandaged his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have no objection to this, if one knows how to do it differently, as needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No abscess can form in fatty tissue, and it lingers so long that it causes a great gathering of bowels.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they will pull and pierce, and jump into the bow, and hold the bones still, just like a vase.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin that is above is as delicate as fine cloth, and will not tear all the way to the bone or nerve, and such a condition is called "healthy," and not "fistula.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so stretched that it reaches the bone, it is called a "fistula.
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure is that you cut the skin all around, especially when it is thin, as if with a cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not be afraid of its decay.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you think that the skin is about to decay and the corruption is not yet complete, and the skin is dry and tough, then apply a cleansing bath thusly:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	check if the breasts are swollen and the bowels emit a bad odor, then cleanse them with Egyptian medicine made thusly:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take ease (or caution), and oil, and litharge, in equal amounts, and place them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take according to your need, and make it into water and honey, and enema the breast, and tighten the opening.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in for two hours, then extract it by straining.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this several times until the breast is clean and free from impurity.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and never should be rinsed with water from ashes when this medicine is not present, and you press ashes into vine bark, pour water over it, then strain it and use the water for enema, as long as you know that the intestines are well cleansed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot endure it, neither Egyptian medicine nor water from ashes will help, if they are enema with water and honey, or have a bit of litharge ground in it.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you should enema them with honey and sweet wine, that the honey has purifying properties to cleanse and wash, and the wine provides air to the health.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this and are sure that the wound is well cleansed, then administer a purge from what causes the fever to rise in him, and make certain you apply a plaster carefully, and do it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you administer certain medications and remedies, of which I have spoken about their properties or treatment of wounds.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the wound is very small and the purge cannot enter, open it slightly with a needle, and apply a bandage of the Egyptian or basilicon remedy, as long as it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too wide, so that the cut and it leave so much pain in place or the wound cannot be entered, and if the opening that sags is above, then the leg or below the knee must be treated.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is entirely blocked, it does not allow any passage.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot close the abdomen as you see fit, then arrange it in such a way that the bowel moves to the lowest part of the leg where it can be passed, for when the bowel is entirely blocked, it does not allow any passage and if you cannot close the abdomen as you see fit, then arrange it accordingly.
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the bowel moves slightly downwards, and leave nothing of the bowel;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidating medicines to promote healing, and lay them on the wound covered with linen cloth that covers all the wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then apply pressure with your hands to the opening near the chest, making it wider from inside than outside, since there is more wound on one side, and put a softer dressing on the other cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it on the healthy opening to align the bowel, and do not remove the large cloth beforehand for many days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and he who is sorely afflicted with a chest wound, often needs to have the bowel opened, and knows that comes from the bowel, whether it is poison or food, or properly digested or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been applied in this manner, and you see the effect that it has on the chest wound, then know that the bowel has already opened, and bring the patient closer to health.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then remove the bandage in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change it for a new one, and renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast becomes bowed and distended after many days, knowing that it will not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons appear after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are some people who slowly heal their wounds, and others who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and they bend over, feeling pain in their sides after many days, knowing that the pain will not subside.
