et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if their pain does not subside, then use medications with moist substances and dry virtues as an ointment, for there is a great deal of vitriol, and this is the last medication.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take the final ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and add aged wine of equal substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then apply it and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and it itself makes the honey thick and rich, when onions are not available, take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them, and sprinkle them onto the honey while it is still warm from the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then I wrap it in cloth and place it over the wound, and never apply aromatic herbs or roots of the celestial plant, which is also like flour from oats and chamomile;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and use simple or composite remedies;
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	Break them, and make them into powder, and add the honey I mentioned, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the cure is prolonged, and this cure does not heal it, then know that the corruption is complete, and it makes an impression on the bone, or the hard members, or the limbs.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure for the fistula, as we have said above.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	A gangrene is an abscess that forms under a nail of the hand, or the foot, or may occur elsewhere.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it becomes infected and no attention is paid, it leads to an abscess, and the pain and swelling increase until the root of the nail is reached, and perhaps even the entire nail.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and it brings corrosion close to the bone, causing intense and putrid pain, with the skin turning dark and swollen.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the previous section, and the treatment does not benefit, then you must remove all the dead tissue remaining under the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cautery is very helpful when the bone is healthy and the nail is intact.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail is quickly heated and begins to hurt, and the blister forms, then you must place a hot iron under the nail that has blistered, and raise it up, and gently and lightly cut off the blister, and apply burning and corroding medicinal remedies to remove all of it.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wounds as long as they are clean.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and treat it, for as long as the bone is corrupt, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see both bones corrupt, cut them as described above, and then treat them as long as they are clean.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is broken, twisted, and causes great pain, then you must first heal it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the nail with a sharp instrument at an angle from above, and ensure that the cut does not go all the way through to the quick of the nail, as the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, apply something that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain excruciates the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	He who is born without the hands in anyone's care is entirely flesh, and perhaps he has parts where there should be bones, and never an fingernail, and none of them are born at the root of a joint, or birth takes place in no way for any of them.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	He who is born with no new pain should not be mute, and he who is born at the joint of the bone may, perhaps, be mute.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut for that which is fleshy should be light, in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	The one that is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	if it keeps you covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	As for him who is born with or develops a deformity in the last (joint), it is necessary that you first cover the joint properly up to the bone, then dislocate the bone to a suitable position, and then treat it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The deformities that come as one must assemble themselves come either from birth, or from the healing of a wound, or from a burn by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must ensure that you cover the closed one, so it should be repaired according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two moistened cloths or sheets soaked in rosin oil, so they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You insert between two pieces of fine cloth, as long as the wound is closed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If adhesion occurs at any of its edges with the palm, close this wound as appropriate.
des vils	The word "des vils" translates to
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	They are veins thickly wrapped, filled with melancholic excess, which come to many parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more often occurs in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry things, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer purgative remedies no more often than once, and then cleanse the bowel.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The cure for this is according to two manners:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One is with cups, and they drain the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is that you open the vein and drain it completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The incision is as follows:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	first, raise the leg with hot water, making it as warm as possible, so that the pain becomes subtle, then stretch the sick leg from above the knee down to the ankle.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then open the vein in one, two, or three places with a large knife, then carefully and gently draw out the black blood in your hand from one end to the other, as much as the patient's weakness allows.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then lay it [the wound] open, and command him to eat foods that produce black blood.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are filled and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The treatment of this is according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Lift the leg of the sick person, if there is any hair, then immerse it in hot water, and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, then heat it over the fire, and then apply it to the vein from the top of the thigh down to the ankle or in the area around the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the joint, and scrape the vein from each side until it appears when touched.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it appears red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems like a white thread.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then stretch the skin from below, as long as it is lifted from the flesh, and then bend it gently at the joint, and then cut across in another place above and thirdly below.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then peel the skin over the vein while it is still open, then lift the raised edge, as you did before, and bend it at another joint, as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then cut another size, or more if needed, then lift and cut at the second joint from the top, then pull and lift until the second size is reached.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then extract it gradually, bit by bit, until it comes out completely, then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	if you cannot pull it out and lift it, push an needle through the entire thread twice as thick, tie and pull it, push down the bone with your finger from one side to another until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and ensure it does not break, because if it breaks, you cannot pull it out or lift it, and it will cause harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and once it is completely pulled out, place warm woolen bandages on the wound soaked in wine and rose oil;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat him as long as he is healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vision is contracted, twisted, and rolled up together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	One must carefully cut the vision if it is curved, without severing, until it reaches the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is a great burden, for if it were thin, it would cover the vein, but since it is thick as we have said, this is its form:
de la voinne civile	from the vein (in the limb)
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in the legs, in hot regions where there are no herbs or trees, and on land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it may appear in other places than the legs, and this leads to putridity that comes from beneath the skin, as if it were a serpent or worm winding and writhing within the flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein appear, it is that there is a very great swelling in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to emerge forcefully, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the joint is open, you must wrap it tightly with a piece of cloth from one and a half to two fingers thick, and compress it, leaving the cloth on the leg, and whenever there is no discharge, wrap it around the cloth and compress it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it and wrap the remaining part, but do not cover its root again until all the discharge has stopped.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it off, it will return to the root and cause an abscess, putrefaction, or a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For every small thing, it is necessary that it be treated little by little until it reaches its end, and nothing should remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and it is never this vein when it is treated with V palms of length, or X, and a man came to me, from whom it emerged X palms in length, and when you cut it, if it bulges or becomes narrow, and pierce it through to the bottom, so that everything comes out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and the material inside should be evacuated, and then the place should be treated with medicinal poultices for several days, and after that, the cure should be applied as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And never should this vein be cut again, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or the leg, and much rupture occurs, and from which much blood flows.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that are born between skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This illness is called the "beef disease" in our land because it often affects cattle, and it is a small worm that develops between the hide and the flesh, spreading throughout the body upwards and downwards, and it feels very hot from one limb to another, as far as the skin where it has taken hold, and it grows fiercely.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is caused by putrefaction of certain humours, as they accumulate and wind their way through the stomach, serpents, worms, and ascarids.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and doubt arises about the nature of his illness, for when it moves through the body, it rises to the head, and reaches the eye, perhaps re-enters, and destroys the eye.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it healing and drawing (out), one cannot be sure unless it has completely gone.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If it is necessary, then you must place the limb above and below with a strong bandage tightly, then cut and pull it until it comes out completely in the char, and you do not remove it, if you cauterize it with fire, until it heals.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is when it bleeds, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or the edge close to the oil, quickly remove the eyebrow-shaped mass by cutting and pulling it out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary for the patient to cleanse his body with solvent medicines to remove harmful humors, and to purify the flesh through hot baths to prevent putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in no particular member, but can move from one member to another.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I have shown you what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to tend to a sick woman, and upon examining her, I discovered a small swelling in the vein of her arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and then I see, the vision arise on the shoulder, more distinct than anything else, as vivid as silver when it cuts through flesh.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departs from its place and settles into the shoulder, and then shortly after, it spreads throughout the body, until it reaches the other breast.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then it told me that it twisted around the body again, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled much at how she moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	nevertheless, I wanted to see if the pain could move from one place to another, but I didn't observe it, as I saw in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought it was because the woman had dry skin, her veins exposed, and this stiffness appeared constrained.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and did not appear at all to those who are delicate, with moist skin and veins covered.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see this disease heal, and the patient feels the pain, if it opens as we have said, press it gently from above and below until this constrained stiffness in the joint leaves.
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the joint;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it for yourself, if the treatment of these impediments repels winds as if through foul pills, and pills of serpentary, and similar ones.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows vary, according to their appearance and according to the parts of the body from which they originate.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Their variety is such that there are some with large points, and others with small, and some with barbs, and others smooth.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some with two edges, and others with tongues, and those with fragments.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and those that split in any member, splitting in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	You should focus on the primary member, as in the head, body, liver, heart, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it breaks in any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterwards, appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must then be prepared for the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterwards in various ways;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not fully extracted, do not pull it, but treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces the skull and bone, and satisfaction is felt on top of the skull, is when darkness and blinding and squinting and redness occur in one eye, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and impaired understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps it is without feeling from the nostrils or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the moist wound, white pus resembling a pulsation, and also like a brisk flow of blood;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears, if you hold to the treatment, pull out the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of an arrow when it breaks or moves is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were embedded in hard, not empty, tissue.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the arrow remains silent like the pulse, and there is sudden black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	so you know for certain that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that the pulse never moves is that there is no foam coming from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns pale, and he breathes heavily and stops moving.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow pierces the skin deeply, it is necessary to remove the small bones.
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and it causes great pain and sorrow, and sighs.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and it moves all the shoulder muscles.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow pierces through the stomach, perhaps something from the wound disturbs the indigestible flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces through the belly, and there is no trace of good fate through the intestines, then there is little hope for a cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow pierces the bladder, the patient urinates in fits and starts, strongly feeling pain.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	he knows that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs—as it feels and appears—the fingers, hands, arms, shoulders, aid (possibly referring to a specific medical term or condition), the lower back, knees, feet, and legs, all exhibit various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man at home, an arrow struck him or cut his eye socket.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I attempted it, and pulled from another side, removing the fat of the ear, and it was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I pulled out an arrow that had struck in the fat below the paper, and the arrow was straightened, and only the tip towards the wood could be seen, and it was an arrow of great length with a blue arch, light as a feather without any noise.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The spirit was pure, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian; it was an Arabian arrow with ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I removed the beard, and manipulated it gently as I extracted it, and the Christian was healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And extracted an arrow from a man's home, which had entered his stomach, and thought he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after he has passed thirty days, his condition does not change.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut out the arrow, disassembled it, and removed it, without any adverse events.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man with an arrow in his side or back, and the wound is deep;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and keep the arrow inside him, and do not change his natural state, nor find any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man, to whom an arrow struck his face, and the wound was deep;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and he endured thus, suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many others of similar kind.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And pulled out an arrow from the body of a prince, the king, which had struck him in the neck and was slightly inclined to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely extracted.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat her after she had been ill for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I examined her with great care, but felt nothing.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and she felt a sharp pain and discomfort deep within her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from an arrow's point. I applied a soothing poultice to the swollen lobe, as the swelling had not subsided.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the arrow's head.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the hot iron repeatedly to the wound and thus soothed it, keeping the patient in this way for a long time until he felt the arrow inside his body.
et il le me dist.	and it came out.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied strong, corrosive medicine to the wound with my hands, keeping it closed until it opened, and when I probed it, I felt the point of the arrow sticking in the flesh.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then adjust the opening of the wound with this medicine until the head of the arrow becomes clearly visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and after three months, the wound healed well, and then it reopened, and I had to use pincers, pulling from both sides, but it wouldn't come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I did not stop trying and devising subtle tools until I found the right pair of pincers, as described at the end of this chapter, and as I manipulated it, the wound healed.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the most skilled judges believe that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then restored it, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or, I have told you the quality of extracting arrows, so that you place your treatment on what I do not say, because books cannot encompass everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the most skilled doctors compare very little and only what they see as useful and effective in practice, truly new works, and nine instruments, for the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not leave the members where they are embedded, except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one that comes out from the other side, where it enters into the flesh, is an arrow that never returns again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the flesh around it decays and the way out is clear;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in a bone, it cannot come out, if left like that for no days, and moves each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps, and if it does not jump, it pierces around everywhere with a fine thread, as long as the muscles around are widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in a bone at the top, and goes down to one of the bellies of the brain, and none of the accidents that I have mentioned affect the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If you cannot pull it out, but leave it as long as it remains even after a few days, for if the arrow goes all the way through, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not driven completely into the bone, and does not heal properly, and the patient suffers no ill effect for some time, the skill of extraction must be applied.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be pulled out, then apply herbs around it, as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the limb as long as it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is withdrawn into the limb deeply and cannot be seen, then press it with all your strength.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot open the wound due to its tightness or the arrow's depth, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein to be seen, then leave it as it is until the wound heals.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and extract the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs that hold it in place, remove them from both sides as much as you can, then break or bend the arrowhead's barbs until you can draw it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully, without breaking the arrow, draw it out with greater force.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, so that the limb around it is completely relaxed, then pull it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the course of fever opposes you, then administer as we have said in its chapter about treatment;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and be careful with the incision near nerves and veins, and learn how you can draw out the arrow safely, as soon or as slowly, firmly or gently as possible.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient according to the position in which the arrow entered, for it is the greatest help, and if you cannot do this, then place him as the signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	He knows that the arrow comes from another direction, where it opens something within him, or the skin is swollen in a noticeable way.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	then cut around it, as much as the pliers can grasp, and then extract it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now and then try to extract it again until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrowhead is embedded in the flesh, it drives itself deeper into the flesh.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if it comes out, you must administer pressure, and if you use a sharp instrument, the point of the arrow should enter the flesh alongside the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	then press firmly, and if the arrow is embedded, drive the instrument with its pointed end inside to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you clear all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	and if the arrow comes out in the stomach, or bladder, or side, and it is close to a vital organ, you can press on it;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and you must guard the vein and nerve, then extract it, and then sew up the wound, it is your duty.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it as long as it is clean.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to extract arrows resembles an eagle's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape [for the arrowhead] when it is like a feather is also like the quill of a bird, to push to the tip of the arrow, as this shape is:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of pliers for pushing and pulling, if it is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are 31 veins from which one draws blood, of which there are 16 main ones, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	II beat the muscles that are after the ears, which are called the "soft hairs";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the visible temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the veins that are in the arms of the joints, which are called "aspirations";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is on the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is on the back of the head;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two wedges which are in it;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the upper lip above the mouth, and these veins are called "augerich".
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins of which one commonly speaks are V in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, which is located on the left side of the body, and is commonly called by the people "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle part is called "fast" (or "middle"), composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and the common people call it "vein of the body".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic is found on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", located beneath the skin, and it is the one that opens clearly on the pulse.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the saving vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, and if it rains (i.e., swells);
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and where the foot are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is removed from the ribcage on the left side of the body, and the second is at the ankle on the right side.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "nesse," which is at the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg, there are three veins removed from those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The healing of veins located behind the ears is beneficial for old cataracts and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and regarding the qualities of healing, as I have said, it is important to lift the patient's head and rub the affected area with a rough cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then tie the patient's collar tightly, so that both veins behind the ears, hanging down from the head, become visible.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	place your fingers there, and where you feel the pulse below your thumb, it signifies life.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet, and cut through the vein just above the bone, then gently your hand over the entire vein upstream, and clean and wrap the skin and the vein well it must pass through, and let out the blood as you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and hold it, as long as it is healthy;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The healthy of the two arteries that are in the temples, it is worth to use ancient and dried, and accustomed to the eye, and at the corner of the eyes, hot tears.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of a good healer is such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient tightens his neck, as both veins open widely;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pain deeply in both sides, and then signs with a cross;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then gently place your thumb on the vein at the top of your right index finger, and insert the lance below, and press the vein at the top, and the cup, just as you did with the other two veins, and draw out the blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then loosen the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then form a bandage and leave it until the wound is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken of their connection and extraction, as mentioned at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the vein on the forehead is just as important as the healing of the head in cases of old facial diseases, such as migraine and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is such that the patient twists his neck, until the vein opens.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosseur", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand, or another tool, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then gently release the patient's neck, and tie the vein as long as it remains healthy and free from a wide opening of any flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Nevertheless, it does not suit that the flames are too intense;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and do not set the healthy one crookedly, for the bone is hard, and perhaps break the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The health of the two veins that are in the arms should be treated carefully, and also for conditions such as scabs, redness, and inflammation in the eye, and facial diseases;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their health is such that the patient pulls his collar tightly without twisting any ligaments, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the healthy one, and make it clean through the flame, slightly long and quite wide, for there is no scar.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is too subtle, it may break.
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then apply the flame to the blood, as much as needed, then wrap it in cloth and bind it tightly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The health of the vein near the nose is valuable for colds and sudden sorrows, and facial diseases such as migraines and redness that come to the face, especially when they are old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the health is such that the patient tightens his collar, then pulls his nose to your left hand, and takes the thin flame longwise and inserts it between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well enough, and now the blood will begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not be too hasty in its application, and let the blood flow as needed, then bind it for a night, for it is often quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The holy water of the two eyes is helpful for the narrowing of the eyelid, and at the onset of inflammation, and for many diseases, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and itching.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the water is such that the patient pulls his collar away from both sides, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and if the master is standing over the patient's head, and the patient sits on a seat, then wash the vein with long water, as much as necessary, and treat the wound with bloodletting as appropriate.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then repeat the process on the other vein, loosen the ligature, and gently pull on the veins until the patient is no longer strangled.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until morning so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	from the cleansing of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cleansing of the veins above the lips helps to improve oral health, and it aids in the healing of gum disease, lip splits, and pain and swelling around them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the healing is such that you should have the patient sit before you and pull on his collar as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip and look at both veins, one on the right side of the mouth and the other on the left, and you can recognize them by their black color and the fine black veins around them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	So then, deal with both one after the other, and if you do not know them or are in doubt, take the larger one from each part, and also make cuts from above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The treatment of the veins below the tongue is beneficial after treating the cervical region, and it is useful for narrowing the throat, eye diseases, and mouth ailments.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of the healer is such that the patient should be cut between your hands in the light of the sun, lift up the tongue, and look below each side for a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then make both whole, but do not force them too much, for there are arteries beneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins through which blood flows, which are commonly healed, are treated in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or cutting through them all with a hot iron or a fine olive oil-soaked cloth, which is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and thin according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	It forms a bright red mark, very renowned, and is broad as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins with a sharp blade on those that have visible, thick blood, which contain much blood and pus.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more delicately pointed, and is for cleansing the delicate veins, where there is delicate, yellow-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The holy basil, which is one of these veins, is beneficial for diseases that are beneath the throat, and the collarbone, and the pelvis, and the stomach.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and the physician should treat it carefully, and wash away the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he touches an artery, and blood flows, it must be stopped as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flame must not be squeezed, but cut as if with a blade.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the vein does not open clearly, it is necessary that you extract it and use another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or if you wish to free it from the vein, draw it out of the vein into the arm.
elle apert manifestement;	she opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the flame gently, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you recognize the place of the wound, it is necessary that you extract the arm, touch the place until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the place with a cross, then bind the arm, and cut the vein gently with the flame.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and be sure not to hurt the artery when you see the shoulder swell, for that is the artery.
eschui la donques.	then avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protrude at the top as well as the urine of a child, and the skin is red and thin, know that this is an artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and put your finger deeply, then remove your finger if the skin remains intact, which often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	he lies with his arm relaxed, and lets it be thus, and does not move the patient.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the wound is not immediately healed, it will worsen, and there are no medicines at hand, especially if the artery opens up, as with a deep cut.
et estainche li sans.	and stop the wound from bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fig wood, cut it, and take one half and tie it tightly to the other until morning.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if it remains unstained, that is good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if that does not work, as we have said, with powders that prevent blood from clotting;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the staining is not overly affected by the small size of the wound or the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The surgeon of the vein should draw blood if it aids in treating the wound from its top and bottom, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and the surgeon should be aware that he must wash for the nerve that is exposed, and if he does not cut it precisely, he might damage the nerve, causing swelling and infection, and perhaps it cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any place due to its subtlety, then you must use a surgical instrument to free it.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid the nerve's power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if a vein is between the two bones, cut it from above.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The treatment for headaches involves drawing blood from the head, which helps and relieves the pain.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary for the healer to prick with olive oil or myrrh flame, because it is the safest of all veins, as it does not harm any nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, it is necessary to seek the gentler vein, and do not be alarmed if it hurts the first time, and try again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance, the eyes may swell up in some men, without any pain at first, but it causes no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood depends on your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about healing is that health is not restored merely by treating illness, but by preserving health and avoiding future diseases.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and health should be sought through one of the three veins, that is, the neck, armpit, or groin.
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	these being the neck (cephalique), armpit (faste), and groin (basilique).
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should heal at the beginning of prayers, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should heal on the first day or the third, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healer who is administered for diseases has no determined hour, but whenever it is necessary by day or night, at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one should not heal children until they are twelve years old, nor a woman who has given birth for less than four months up to seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should not consider the old who have passed sixty years as healed.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone wishes to be healed, in any way, it is necessary that he purges the bowels with a light enema, if there is much feces retained, so that the veins do not draw out the excessive and harmful impurities from the main limbs.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	He will not be healed who is excessively soaked in salty meats or too much fat, nor those who are weak from drinking excessive water.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and should be wary of the patient after colic, vomiting, abdominal distension, frequent sexual activity, childbirth, watching and fasting, and anything that depletes strength, whether from weapons or bodily illness.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then gently draw out the humours, if they are thick, through foods, drinks, and remedies, if you have such power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then into the bath, if nothing hinders you, to draw out the blood, and heal the vein from within and around it, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself from work, trouble, luxury, and similar things on that day.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be calm and joyful, and make the healing more effective than that of others, and rub the arm twice or three times, then tighten the ligature gently, for if it is too tight or loose, it will not heal well.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the joint with your hands, until the veins swell and you feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then moisten the wound with a drop of old oil, then place your left-hand finger on the vein below the joint, where you want to heal, so that the vein does not burst and cause harm.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flow like strings when healing, and if they are filled with pus, so that when you apply the flame, it pulls away from the flame, and cannot open the vein, thus one suffers from such a condition.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if they open the vein, if the wound is too narrow, then it is necessary that the healers be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, it is necessary to repeat the process slightly below where it was done, for if the limbs are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen and the patient fears, let it be for one or two days without binding the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	Perhaps there appear abscesses suddenly.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	One should not bathe immediately, then renew the dressing if it seems appropriate.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if it is a small opening, gently pierce the skin and doubt not that it will let out as much blood as you see, so sure are we of the same piercing itself, straight to the flame.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and open it slightly gently, so that the muscles are not inflamed.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	because this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the vein swollen, do not immediately recommence the healing process, and apply a little oil, for it lightens the body of blood, and the sticky substance that the oil leaves is helpful in this situation.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil in every vein you treat to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and it has a soothing and comforting effect when applied to the swollen vein.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if subtly the bone moves and spreads when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there develops a large abscess, which happens often, especially when the vein is not wide enough to be opened at once, act swiftly, and place a moistened sponge with some hot seal on it over the area and keep it there for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood flow from the vein has stopped, and if it remains at the site for several days without any blackening or greening, then it causes no harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, place on anything cool or cold, soaked in a calamine juice, show, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times, abscesses and pustules appear on the sacred flesh of the basilica.
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	then place your hand on it, and if you feel the warmth is too great under the pressure of your hand, this is when such an appearance occurs.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	So be careful not to apply anything of what we have said, for it might cut off the flow without an artery.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but he should make an emollient with dry herbs to harden the joint, then apply another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each one of the pains according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the pain.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the skin is pale, let it continue to turn red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it as thick, leave it until it becomes thin.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for him who is sick and weak, and has the skill to extract blood, that he make a larger wound, and have wider flames.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for the weak, do the opposite, and it is more necessary to heal them quickly and often, and one should heal them by cutting across, not piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this healing method is free from the decay of blood and the disruption of nerves, and it is more effective than healing either long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to him whose body needs salivation, it is necessary to give a little of the juice of pomegranates.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is overheated, he should take cold juice three or four times a day, and if he has a cold complexion, he should first dilute the salivation with a little syrup made from grapes, or honey syrup perfumed with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and nutmeg, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints at the sickbed, after drawing much blood, it is necessary that he inhale a brew of charcoal and subtle fragrant syrup, and use other things as we have mentioned in the section or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to extend his arm and heal it later, as necessary, when it is weakened by much healing, he should pull and release it little by little, according to the amount of its continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to extend his arm after the first healing, and he has strong stiffness, he should heal it seven hours after the first healing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to heal from another side, he should heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For he has excess heat and blood inside the body, which causes fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, and widen the opening as much as possible;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	since you fulfill all the conditions for healing, and place your hand on a pulsating (vein) when it is healthy, death does not come in its place, and this often happens, when healers are negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not advisable when you see the arm dislocated a second time, and blood flows out again, and the opening is closed, to press strongly on it.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If he is weak, he should stretch his arm slowly, for it would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but he should let it heal the second time around;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you should apply the tip of the flame to the frozen vein until it bursts open, then place a small piece of silk over it and gently press.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not squeeze it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it becomes necessary to drain the blood again due to the abscess, either in the same place or in another vein or arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthier in place of the vein in the head because it is composed differently.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of healing is that the patient should immerse their hand in hot water until the veins turn red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then tie it gently, so that the vein opens well, then clean the wound now with a thin and precise movement, not too wide or too long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and make the wound wide enough, and ensure the healing is close to the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be extracted, immerse the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow out in the water until you have enough.
