et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if this does not work, do not push the hand back into the hot water, as it is more harmful than helpful.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the health of this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are neither arteries nor nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The health of the vein in the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand and immerse it in hot water, as long as the vein is inflamed, if that is visible;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and hold the hand across, and if you grasp it firmly from every side, then there is no pain.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not harm the patient too much, for the nerves are entirely exposed and naked of flesh, and then apply the hand to warm water, so that the blood is frozen in the wound, and it cannot escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as best you can, then place oil and silk on the vein to bind it tightly, and so do for each person.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healthy person holds the mouse with their left hand if it has a disease of the eye, and does everything as I have told you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sage of the soul holds sway over all illnesses affecting the body, such as illnesses of the eyes, and retention of flowers (possibly referring to a condition related to plant or petal-like growths), and diseases of the kidneys, feet, and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of his health is such that the patient should immerse themselves in warm water and rub the vein until it breaks, and then bind over the joint with a cloth.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and they will apply much rain (or perhaps pressure) above the foot.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Sanct then make wider or larger cuts, or at the ankle, wherever it is valuable to move.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you make cuts on the foot, be careful with the nails that are underneath, and cut across as well as when piercing.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and so the flames will subside.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the splint cannot be removed, place the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the cuts need to be made for the first time, then repeat the second cut just above a little, because the wounds are salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein's lion is at the ankle's fire, and its healing brings pain to the lower back when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his health is such that if the patient enters the bath, he should pull three times on the ankle, twisting it, because otherwise the vein will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, take the health in every way that you can, and draw through it.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is worth that you hold it, because the veins are safe, and it is much refreshed with many hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not let it heal, if any healthy thread from the wound opens or closes slowly and gently, and takes care of the nails.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and apply pressure against the blood as you see fit, then loosen the bandage, and place a piece of cotton and tighten it.
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	From the medical treatments of the vacuum (sauce/suction).
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Suction cups are made of horns, or iron, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and ventilation is done according to two manners:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this ventilation without piercing is according to two manners:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it is with all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and the ventilation done by piercing and drawing blood is done in twelve parts of the body, so that one part is entirely in sleep at the head.
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are in the neck.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and the others on both sides of the neck.
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction from under the chin.
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction from both shoulders.
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction on the knees.
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the suctions on both arms.
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the leech (suction) cups of both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the leech (suction) cups on both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the leeching does not treat blood, but rather small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and for this reason it weakens no one, as is done with vein-sucking;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not advisable to use it in any condition arising from fullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, due to necessity or illness, it is necessary to release the air, either at the beginning or end of the month, or every day, then it should be done each hour.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are such people who, when they need to release air, have a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if they who experience relief with release have redness in their face, head, neck, and dark circles around the eyes.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, have an inflamed tongue, and bleed.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are such people who think, see blood, and feel pain and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we order vomiting after three hours during the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The healer of the muscle should help with the great pain in the head ...  that comes from these (causes), and it is not appropriate for this to happen after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this treatment should be in the hands of the healer of the head, and it is not appropriate for someone of a cold disposition to use it, or who has catarrh, for it causes them much harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason, it is not advisable that the elderly or those with cold illnesses use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who recovers from it often becomes oblivious, and for this reason, the cup should be placed a little lower down in doubt of its oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The wind or inflammation of the neck is contrary to health from the top and base, and for this reason it causes tightness in the chest, narrowing of the airway, coughing, and congestion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is advisable to press lightly, as if it holds too firmly, it can cause faintness or stomach and body pain.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The inflammation of the ribs in the neck causes pain in the head, eyes, and migraines, constriction, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and is contrary to the health of the sinus from the base.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is necessary that you instruct the healthy person to press his hand gently so as not to damage the artery, and no blood loss occurs.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The inflammation of the jaw is worth addressing for mouth diseases, gum corruption, and similar ailments in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and is located in the healthy areas between the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Breathing through the shoulders is beneficial for illnesses that arise from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The inflammation of the edges (possibly referring to skin folds or areas around veins) is as important to address as three major veins in the arm, because it attracts blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the healthy not to cut too deeply, for the flesh is devoid of strength, and the bones and arteries are easily damaged.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cup (ventouse) placed on the groin is useful for draining blood from deep within and for treating internal diseases. It must be large and made of iron, and it needs to be applied correctly.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and if, by chance, it (the cup) is too thin, it will break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The suction cups on the legs should be opened tightly, for they draw blood from throughout the body, and they are as painful as ancient rain, or pain in the joints, or in the bladder, and they cause trembling.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they affect the second ribs, and the two ankles, but they weaken the body after long use, and cause paralysis in many positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The proper way to apply a suction cup is to first ensure it is empty, then suck gently, and place it firmly. Move it slowly and consistently, without stopping, until you see the red skin become pale and the blood flow cease.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then, apply pressure, and remove the suction cups, taking care in the placement of the bandages, for there are some with deep wounds and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	it is necessary to strike only once, and make large wounds, and deep ones.
et suce legierement.	and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the pain is intense, it is necessary to strike twice.
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to carefully extract the thick blood vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, it may be necessary to cut it a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to extract thin blood little by little, it is enough to do so only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, we should not do it often.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, cutting it will be effective, and completing the process ensures that the veins are suddenly pierced; for those with thick, hard skin, and who have swollen pores, one should apply oil to the suction cup before and after use.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is a matter of a red-colored oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in the form of oil from beetroot, or lily, or chamomile, or any similar plant.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amaranth oil, or balm oil, or hemp oil, or similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one has a strong and wide wound, it is not necessary to put oil on it, but rather after cleansing with rosewater, or cold water, or myrtle water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or any similar liquid.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with much moisture should rise from it using myrtle water, sumac water, and similar substances.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excessive moisture should rise from old wine, or eucalyptus water, or anise or chamomile decoction, or any similar thing.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and they should not use a vacuum immediately before or during a bath, but rather after the bath, one or two hours later.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep after the incision, and it is necessary that he bathe, when he needs to be ventilated and when he has been ventilated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	and be wary of those who have a fever that is choleric, and if the patient lacks heat, it is too acute and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it is necessary that he apply cold things, such as grapes, endive and lettuce in the shade, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat prunes, and juice of chestnuts, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, should drink syrup of honey, and moderate, fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat nothing too much, and small birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day when he feels hungry, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give no one any triacle or nutmeg at any time before or after ventilating, in order to strengthen the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be subtle about it, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The suction cups that are used to heal are those applied to the liver, and the spleen, and podagra, and the belly, and the bowels, and the kidneys, and the hips, for these parts do not tolerate being struck, and they are only used to draw blood from one part to another, as we apply them to the mammary glands when nursing.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity from the member, as we apply suction cups to the belly and bowels to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain when there is an extraction or stone, if by its attractive virtue it draws out the extraction, or leaves the stone in its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus it is done when one places it upon the liver and spleen when there is retention of wind, and these suction cups are emptied to suck only;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and they are never filled with fire together, and never with cold water, as in cases of tears flowing freely, and in such a way one fills the cup with hot water or water mixed with herbs suitable for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cup (ventose) administered by fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it should be two and a half palm widths in length, and on one side there is a small opening around the middle, large enough to push an needle through, and it should be curved gently so that it does not hurt the patient when placed upon the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and tell them to place a stick diagonally of wood or iron, to take hold of a cloth, and according to the diseases and age of those who use it, they will be large or small.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suckers of children are different from those of the old, and thinner than the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must thus place this sucker on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the cloth of wax or linen, and place it across the sucker through the stick that is in the sucker, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the sucker so it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it over the member, and your fingers should be on the opening we have mentioned, so that when you want, the vapour goes there, and we remove the suction cup.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and draw along the line as before, and repeat often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the case of the suction cup, which is applied to treat pleurisy, and any acute condition, it has no opening or gap, and can only be applied when the part is filled with fluid, and placed over the member only then.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Without exception, only members where suction cannot be applied due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar parts, are exempt.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare skin areas, such as the hands or feet, and others similar.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is such that when you find suction cups in fresh water, clean and without putrefaction, if they are taken.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place a hot needle in their armpits until they become accustomed to it, and have no wind or pressure on their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then make them well from veins and leeching, and rub the limb until it turns red, and apply blisters.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they stop bleeding and crying, if it is a place where a leech can be applied, then apply one, for this is much better afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If this is not possible, then lift the leech from its place, wash it well with water, and then dry it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and hold the eyes steady after the surgery until the wounds are healed; if a moist linen cloth in cold water is placed on them, and left there until the wounds are closed.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the wounds multiply, then apply crushed vitriol, or gall, and similar substances until they are completely healed.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you can place half-peeled beans on the joint and leave them until they adhere to the bone; this will now heal.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more skill, then take other wounds.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the veins do not want to be taken, so rub the fresh blood vein with a strong press, or you insert an needle until the vein pops, and then place them back on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will move.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are moving, sprinkle some aloe and powdered silk or ash on them, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	We begin the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear reader, that the strange symptoms that arise from this chapter are not found in any ancient books, nor have they ever been read or written about.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, the knowledge is strange in our land, for I never found any good of it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it, except through the knowledge of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have acquired the knowledge, and through experience, and through the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I have done in these two chapters mentioned before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in this prologue of this book the principles of speech and the chapters where the wise ones apply their understanding, staying on the truth, so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture, dislocation, or twisting occurs in any part of the body, you should quickly tend to the patient from both sides, if nothing stops you, such as weakness of the body, illness, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if it is too tight or too cold,
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and warm things, such as hot towels, and a horse's collar and chest bandage, and do not drink wine, do not eat any fatty foods, and do not stuff yourself with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you are certain of the heat of the abscess or the swelling of the member.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient returns to having a fever after proper treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that we alleviate the patient from foods that cause excessive belching, or have a viscous consistency, such as cooked flour in water, and rice, and peas, and veal, and offal, and fish, and fresh meat, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For excessive belching prevents the bone from healing properly, as it re-opens the fracture more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones broken from old age or fragility cannot be well healed or consolidated according to their nature due to the stiffness of the members, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of young children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is no cure, reset the broken bone with thick fingers that open and join the member together, as much as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not restrict it entirely from its movement, and for this reason, it is necessary to feed on substantial meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manners of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	Because there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another when sharpening, just like the blade of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and the fracture is at a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each kind has its own mechanism, and its specific tool for restoration, according to what the memory comes to it.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the fracture of the bone is recognized because the joint is twisted, and it opens well due to external force, and feels tender under pressure from the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twist or pressure felt, and the patient does not experience much pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can still have twist, crack, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it with the hand, but apply remedies that will come hereafter, and then gently tighten it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture which goes in an arc, and the two parts are disjoined, now it is fitting to put them back together evenly so that an abscess does not form from there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if an abscess forms, it is important to let it heal for a time, until the abscess is calm.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then make it even with the muscle as you can gently and firmly, and know that the restoration of what is whole is lighter than the restoration of what has been broken.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then hold steady, as it is needed afterward.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bones there are broken pieces, if they extend from two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or to your hand if it is a small member, or to the tendons, or to a tendon and to your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the member according to its natural position, so that when the parts of the broken member are out of alignment, you reset them with all instruments at your disposal, and ensure that through your work, the patient does not suffer further injury or pain.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust both joints of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with your hand if it seems not properly aligned to you.
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if you dress it properly and do not tighten it too much, nor press as those who cause deep abscesses and contractions in the member through their own work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is at its limit, gently instruct the patient so they do not move it, neither awake nor asleep, nor by turning or any other manner.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and ensure that the limb is secure so as to feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, except just at the point of treatment, it is necessary to put oneself in a position where he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and ensure that it is set correctly, so that no crookedness comes when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken limb depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that broken members are diverse in size and shape and strength.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For it has small members, as bras, legs, and similar ones.
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	it is necessary to wrap soft and delicate linen around it.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are thick, like the thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	it is necessary to wrap with a wide and firm bandage, for the wide bandage embraces the entire limb, compressing it evenly from all sides so that there is no movement.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then he enters lightly, making three turns or four according to the limb, and tightens your hand slightly on the entire joint, then goes above the fracture and tightens it less, so that the fracture can gradually pull itself apart.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and softens the joint little by little, as you press deeply into the healthy part of the limb, then take another joint and repeat this process from the beginning above the fractured bone.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part at the bottom of the fracture and tighten it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we said in the first section above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place it between the thick cords of linen or cloth, as even as possible, then bind it all from above with bandages, and then put your well-made needles on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	If there is an abscess or swelling, apply a hot soothing compress to it, which reduces the swelling, and leave it like that for several days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then stretch your needles, and they should be of half the thickness of a fine cane cut sharply, or made of wood used for making arrows, or palm fronds, and according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the thread which one puts on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be also as long as necessary for the member, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then tighten the threads on the thread as you did in the first layer, then tie a new thread over it, just as in the first layer on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter it is bound, the less it will move;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the thread is too thick, as I have seen many people make their threads from twisted linen cords, it is a great error, because the thread cannot be even if it is too fine, and it does not suit that there should be less than two threads per space between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is troubled by the seeds of stars (possibly referring to splinters or foreign bodies) after dislocating their joints, he should place soft cloth or other bandages over them to prevent bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by breakage (of bones or tissue) and the heart is broken, I will describe its treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to extract all the stars (bones or splinters) from a member that is broken on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	Because when the members (limbs) are large, it is not suitable to put stitches too close together, only after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your own judgment of the swelling coming down.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and now let us consider the ancient methods of applying plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and take flour that clings to the walls of a mill, mix it with enough egg, and make this preparation, neither too liquid nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of applying plasters to restore fractures in various ways, especially for women and small children, as it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of applying plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take some barley meal, and almonds, and henna, and asafoetida, and gum Arabic, and mix them with water (or perhaps meant to be mixed with oil or another base), as directed by Doctor X.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	mixture of mirror and aloe, as directed by Doctor V.
alechil VIIII З.;	alecin (or a medicinal preparation containing alecin) from Doctor VIIII.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make it into a powder, mixing it with egg albumen.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the patient's skin is hot, use this plaster, as it is of good composition and gently restores broken bones, and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of plastering that is effective for twists:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take vinegar and wolf's dung, mix with X (unknown substance);
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Mix mirror and aloe, add seven (unknown substance);
acaice VI З.;	Use lime six (unknown quantity or substance);
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Bolic armenic X Z., grind it well, and mix with enough fire or water, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method of splinting joints and realigning bones in their sockets, easing the pain that arises, and using a saw to cut the bone, and the fracture.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take another new cloth, moisten it with oil and heat, and place it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cyst splints do not restore, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of splinting that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dry figs, and land pavot leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plastering to restore the broken bone and thus lessen the remaining pain of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take the root of alder, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, each in equal parts.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind, and mix with wine, and warm the affected members by mixing with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of plastering when the abscess hardens during the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take the roots of alder, and flaxseed, and valerian, and melilot, and fennel, and violet and chamomile flowers, each in equal parts.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and crush, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the warmth of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that one should not apply a hot compress to a broken member, but rather a certain type of compress made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be neither too hot nor too cold.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen states that one should apply warm, dry things to a broken member to restore it, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another method of splinting that is effective for both injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	take feathers and goat hair from humans who have been shorn, or pen feathers, and silk, and cut them equally, and crush them, and make plaster and bind it tightly.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then loosen it slightly after, and take care that the patient feels no pain, and that the bone has not moved from its place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if it does not come loose by strong hands.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	and if pain comes to the place, or itching, feeling of restlessness or swelling, then act quickly, dislodge it and remove the splint immediately.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a moist sponge from the sea, and dip it in water, and lift the limb until the itching stops and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then cover it with a dry cloth, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it up until you are certain that the abscess is hot.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and rests the swelling of the affected member, and heals the bone pain, then begins again with subtle heat, and a little plaster, and does not strain it as strongly as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	as subtily as it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is closed, red, painful, and swollen, then you need to apply plaster and bind it again; just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing improves in the member of what we have said, then do not dislocate it until after three, four, five, or seven days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and never leaves it for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals and the joint approaches its normal position on the limb.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then hold it more tightly than first, and thicken its flesh, as I have said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you notice the vein is more engorged than necessary, know that no healing can come from it.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	open the vein with hot water immediately, every time you dislocate it, and let the blood flow a little each day.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this effort, therefore, cut the vein in the limb, and use cautery as the foolish do, attempting to restore the twisted member.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	This is evil, and if it causes great fear, I see no other way but to leave it and do it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of fractures, and various shapes, and the causes are diverse.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and the bone splits completely through to the other side, as if cut with a hatchet or axe.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason, this type of fracture is called "hatchet-like".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or he uses a spear to pierce the bone without causing injury, and this method of fracture is called "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and this is the wound of these two fractures, great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a pounding, or a fracture, or a cut from a stone, or a blow against a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent fracture, which approaches the bone tissue that is beneath or on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound that is closed over the bone is as subtle as a hair, and the crack is small, it is called this fracture "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is caused by a stone or an arrow or something similar, and the bone fragment goes deep inside, and the joints are bent as when a blacksmith bends metal over a forge.
si entre li piere dedens.	if it enters the stone inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	and this is more common in those who have moist bones, such as children's skulls.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it occurs in all these ways of fracture, causing small pieces to be dislocated as if they were.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the ways of breaking through withdrawal from them, and inquiry at close range, and by corrupt flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is perceived when the bone is discovered and rubbed further, opening the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be cautious of accidents with the patient, and if you notice any ill effects such as vomiting, loss of consciousness, extension or bending of the limb, paleness, fever, sudden warmth, redness, or other similar symptoms in various combinations, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any dangerous accidents and hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fever comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon's cycle while it is still fresh.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this happens, if you hurry to remove the bone on the seventh day, when the tissue surrounding the bone is decomposed, then come the complications that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone extends up to the membrane covering the brain, it is necessary that you split the broken part like this:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and you should press the patient's head with pain, and expose the bone in all ways that you can, and on the wound's surface as gently as possible, and if blood comes out when you uncover the bone, or an abscess opens, use what is necessary to help, and fill the area with moistened woolen cloth.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and keep the wound at rest until the abscess is calmed and be sure of the blood flow.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to separate the bone, and this is done according to two ways of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One method is to hold the affected area tightly with your hands, and this is how it looks:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then take another treatment even more powerful than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is to have many different-sized instruments, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed and made of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and gently open it, so as not to damage the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and dense, you must drill around it gently, so as to insert instruments with care, without going too deep that they penetrate beyond the soft part of the bone, and on top of the point should be a margin or curve, which prevents the tip from going through the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and it is necessary to have many, so that each comes to its place according to the expectation of the bone, so you must take care for all parts.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three types of care:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality to pierce around the broken bone is that you apply care to the bone and return to your tasks as long as you know that the bone is pierced.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then apply the care elsewhere a little later, and do so all around, then cut with incisions the space between the fragments of bone, and make it as gently and subtly as possible while still removing the bone with your hand or with any of the tools you have, such as pliers or pincers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and ensure you do not touch the brain or the heart.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone, and treated it, you must then observe the tension that is delayed from the bone to all other instruments resembling a chisel, but it should be more tense and more subtle than any other chisel.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if it does not delay any small bones, or any scales, gently remove them with the instrument.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then dress the wound with bandages and bindings as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another method of treatment is that which Galen says, which is safer.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and speak very loudly, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you expose a part of the bone, either where it is broken open or clearly visible, and when you have exposed this part, place the flat edge of this lens-shaped scalpel beneath it. This is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not deviate from this method in any way, and it is the acute side on the second rib, so that the incision is towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small mallet from above, so that you gently hit the bone all around, and be very careful of the skin that is below.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is detached from the bone, gently pull it, for it comes out with a good sensation, without pain or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not reach down to the flesh, and the bone is only broken on top, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to smooth out these asperities and shave off the scales with a fine rasp, of which you should have various quantities, to soften each part according to the severity and form of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you encounter great difficulties and then even more subtle ones, do not cease from this task until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	For each of the other haircuts or subtle breaks, you must treat according to their specific location.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that is never fully answered for those who have dedicated their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if satisfaction is achieved, it is necessary to apply a linen bandage according to the size of the wound, soaking it in rose oil and placing it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled over twice or thrice, soak it in wine and rosin oil, and place it on top of the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and make it lighter than you can, without straining the wound too much, then apply another bandage on top and do not tighten it excessively so as to only touch the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it thus for a day or two until the abscess is calmed, then loosen it and administer medications such as roots of lis, flour of times, powder of incense, aromatic herbs, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and from these things make a powder, apply it to the wound, and administer worldwide remedies without biting;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and ensure that the wound is always clean, do not leave any uncleanliness, nor allow it to fester, for when it festers and pus forms on the flesh, it causes great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one applies sharp, biting things to it, if it is not held steady, it causes no harm.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if darkness comes not from the medicine applied, then let that virtue take effect; it is necessary to press a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and wrap it in cloth, and apply it to the biting place.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the cure with ways of healing that are necessary, as long as he is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Knowing that the two parts of the upper arm are never broken, either entirely or partially, for they are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and the inner part is cartilage, and does not break, unless it bends or twists severely, then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should apply your little finger or press into the joint, and make the same fracture in your index finger, and hold it firmly until the joint returns to its natural position.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and make it gentle, and ensure that the patient feels no pain through your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the joint and the fingers cannot be moved to reset it, you should put a slightly thick stick at the top of the joint to realign it.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of the second degree, repeat the same procedure, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if this is not possible, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess at the wound's edge has healed, then apply to the head new bandages made of linen thread, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you may bind it from another side if the fracture is present.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and make the bands so thick that they fill the gaps between the teeth.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that no healing occurs when the bandages are not moistened with butter, and they must be changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	I do not think this is correct, but it is necessary that they be moist when preparing egg white and flour powder.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the band, until the bone is hard and the cartilage stiffens.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never should bands or goose pen be applied in place of bands, and if the wound is covered with moisture, and the break persists, and the patient suffers, it will blow among them.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or make sure you see well.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses form in the wound while you are treating it, apply a plaster or wet cotton wool soaked in rose oil or a poultice of dill seed.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess does not drain, apply a poultice from outside with flour of spices and incense powder, confited with egg yolk, then place light bandages on it and do not tie the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the nose is broken and shattered into small pieces, remove it with suitable instruments, then clean the cut and treat it with hot charcoal and other suitable bandages.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the nose, if it is cured with these treatments, and he puts splints, as long as it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the dislocation of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is dislocated and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only slightly out of place, and it is not broken into two pieces, but only displaced inward, then if you gently recognize it, it can be set back in place.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	If the fracture is in the right side, you should insert your index finger into the mouth of the patient with the injury.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is in the left mandible, insert your index finger of your right hand, gently push the fracture back into place, and use the other hand to apply equal pressure.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is severe in two parts, it is necessary that you administer an extension of the second part, as long as it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movement of the teeth causes a fracture, tying them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then apply a plaster to the broken jaw, and place a double cloth over it.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and place the cloth with a large, well-made star or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and fasten it to the teeth as best you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the alignment changes, untie it on the third day and then reset it as it was aligned.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and then apply a plaster on it, with a powder from the mill mixed with enough egg or flour of chickpea, after you have removed the dressing.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and then apply a lighter second plaster, and if the plaster sticks, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it heals.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	often it heals within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess appears, then administer what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a break and wound together, it does not matter if any part of the bone is removed.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if skillfully using suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is tight, stretch it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and it does not delay, close the wound if it is wide, and apply suitable plugs to it, to draw out pus, as long as it is healthy.
de la forcele	from the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The force breaks many times before, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is broken and disjointed in two parts, and there are fragments, and it is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or there is fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the aid that is broken with force.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the others stretch the collar towards the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then make the break even with both hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no bulge or indentation.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend it further, place a round, thick piece of cloth or wool under the shoulder of the patient, as needed.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and gently extend the arm, and grasp the cloth with your hand, ensuring that the break is even as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the dislocation away from the bone because it is stuck completely, then the patient should lie on their side with their shoulder supported, and have a helper press the shoulder downwards until the bone in the dislocation is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then address the fracture with your hands, and if you feel any debris, it is necessary that you cut through it.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and gently try to separate the pieces, and if the bone cannot join together for any reason, then the fracture is at one of the incisions you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but that you apply the strength of this instrument underneath, to ensure satisfaction.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it should resemble a spoon, and is not too sharp, and as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the extent of the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and take note of the joints, as you see them, and let one be wide and the other narrow, just as is the rupture of the wound that you made when treating the bone;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of the hot abscess, if cutting the wound, and if its rupture is small, then you doubt the hot abscess, if applying bandages and poultices according to their quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses appear, then moisten the cloth with rose oil and silk and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The straining of the bone, when it is sensitive to touch and has no incision, is that you place a thin layer of fine-milled powdery plaster and egg white on the bone, then put light bandages over it, and insert a spear under the joint if necessary.
