puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very wide bandage, one palm length wide, then place two layers on top of each other on the stump, and apply the plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the top of the bandage is exposed.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the stick on the fracture, then turn the bandage around the collarbone, and lift the healthy armpit, and lift the painful armpit.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the stick does not move over the broken bone, reward it each day, and when the bands loosen, restrict them.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his side, and place a small pillow under his armpit to raise the dislocated joint;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if you lighten the fracture with the alignment of the shoulder, or tie the arm to the collarbone, and no further harm comes from it for twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then resume the splinting if you see that it is necessary, tighten it and leave it thus until it is healed;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored within 28 days, and to no one sooner.
de la brisure de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It follows that when the shoulder is broken or severely dislocated, it does not move normally, and its position can only be adjusted by touch.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if the apparatus is adjusted according to the shape of the fracture and restored to its natural form in every way possible.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then place a soft, fine-milled powder on the joint, along with light bandages and a double cloth covering.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then place a wide and thin steel (blade) slightly larger than the shoulder, and dislocate the blade in no specific place of the shoulder, using that sharp edge of linen cloth, so that the blade cuts evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then tighten it with a great firm band so that the blade does not move from its place, and examine it every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and whenever it loosens (the band), loosen the strap and place the blade evenly if it is out of its place, and lay the patient on his side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is reduced after 10 to 25 days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when these numbers are reached, if it is dislocated, be careful, for it is not bone that will set itself easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out and is not removed from the inside, it causes inflammation and pain in the abscess, so do as we have said to calm the heat of the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from the break of the worst abscess
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The skin is never broken in the middle, but it can be slightly damaged.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks when subjected to heat.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken at the end, it retracts inside and causes the patient great pain, and there is no strength left, and sometimes it bleeds, and opens up the wound in the broken bone, and feels better.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his side, and puts a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and aligns the ribs with your hands, subtly making it even in all ways that you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then apply plasters and bandages over the tender flesh of the broken bone, wrapping it in a cloth and securing it so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and restore the ligament to its proper position on the back, tightening it gently, and checking the freedom of movement every hour, relaxing it if it becomes tight.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	if it becomes necessary to release it due to corrosion or itching in the flesh, or pain or an abscess that develops at the site, act quickly, release the plaster, and treat the underlying condition appropriately.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reset the splint and hold it tightly until it heals.
de la brisure des costes	from the breakage of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaking of ribs only occurs in the upper regions of the back and at the top, and they do not bend unless they are broken.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and feels the patient well during questioning as is right.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you put it back in place as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, gripping it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the rib fracture is inclining inward, the patient feels great pain, as well as piercing and crying out, because the bone punctures the tissue.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and furthermore with pins, and often and violently filled with blood, it is of great pain and the ancients have put much skill into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And for those who say that it is appropriate to administer foods that cause bloating in the stomach to push the fracture out.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not claim that incisions in hot wounds will not come, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes back, then the patient is healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they say that none of us should use cupping glasses on the skin, as it forms a vacuum, and this seems reasonable.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, there is doubt that the cupping glass does not attract impurities to the skin due to its weak condition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that none of you should cover the joint with moist wool in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to evenly distribute the heat around it, then treat the cure for pleurisy, flesh, and with medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patients feel great pain that they cannot bear through their bones where the cup is pressed, there is doubt in the patient, and it is necessary to cut into the broken rib bone, and it is necessary to put under the instrument to hold the satisfaction.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut the bone, draw gently, and stitch the two edges of the wound together, if it is large, and treat it with poultices, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if abscesses develop, place moistened oil-soaked rags on them and cover with a cloth.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat while the cloth over the abscess is fresh, keeping it in place, resting on the side where it should be, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	From the rupture of the collarbone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	No fracture should occur to the delicate collarbone, and it rarely happens;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also to the painful spine.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover, pay attention if you see their hands becoming soft, swollen, and numb, and they cannot move or stretch them, and if you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Knowing that it is deadly in many ways, and if they are mute and feel well when squeezed and not at all, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and the patient will be cured, if proper treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if a similar thing occurs to the painful spine, you must know if it is whole or not, if you observe if its joints are soft, and if there are any accidents in the hands, and on the back, coughing and vomiting without will.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when you remember it on your belly, such severe coughing and vomiting without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is remembered lying on its back and wants to move, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	He knows that it is deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if he does not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not occur, then the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that if there is a hot abscess, you apply warm rose oil or egg yolk oil to it until it is soothed.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then place a comforting and drying plaster on it, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, as long as he is whole.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	and if any bone becomes detached, it is necessary to cover it with cloth;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then close the two edges of the wound with a stitch if it is large, and apply a dressing to the wound, keeping it clean, as long as it is whole.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the bone fragment is broken, which is called the "fragment of the wound," press your pouchet (possibly a type of bandage or compress) with your left hand and place it equally in your right hand over the wounded area, then apply plaster and a splint if needed.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then hold it tight, and if there is a bone out of place, put it back in order, and heal the wound as long as it is clean.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	from the fracture of the bone in the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	First, if the bone in the neck is broken, and it has, there shouldn't be much reduction at the top.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and stretching it long, and bending it in the opposite direction, brings pain to the patient at the site of the break, and swelling, and inflammation that results from the fracture.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the healing is such that you extend your hand above, as long as you are over the break.
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and such is the fracture and shape of it;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is only at the head, then make all such fractures even, as long as they are in their natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, it inclines inward, then make the patient lie on his stomach until the restoration of this fracture appears.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have made it even, then place a splint above it, and put a stick or rod under it, and tighten the fracture so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and hold the limb against the body, as long as the muscle is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if an abscess forms, it should not be touched until it has calmed down, and then apply what we have said above.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to restoration, holding it as necessary, if there is no adverse event.
et c’est li maniere.	and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	dislocation of the joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The helper is what lies between the shoulder and the head, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two ways:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	do not take a sharp instrument of medium thickness according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	and bind the two parts together, twist them upwards, and place the patient in a reclining position;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then pour the hot liquid over the broken arm until it is completely immersed, and place a wooden splint around it, then twist it upwards towards any heavy object or have the attendant pull it downwards.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then align the fracture so that it is level with both hands together, until the fracture returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is that one should place the patient on his back, and bind his hands to his neck, then command the assistants that one holds what is above the break in the hand, and the other holds below at every joint, and extends each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then tighten it slightly from around the fracture, and on the fracture, and stretch each of the assistants to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the fracture is near the top of the shoulder, it is necessary that you apply a medium-strength ligature under the joint, and another towards the neck, below the fracture.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the fracture is towards the neck, it is necessary to apply a light ligature without effort, as long as the fracture is even on the bone, both on top and towards the neck.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	then make the fracture even, as it should be, and tighten it, if abscesses do not form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess appears, it is not pulled out for seven days, and a moist cloth is placed over it in linseed oil and rose oil until the abscess at the base is calmed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then pull it out, and the manner of pulling is that you place the strap over the dislocation, then raise the arm towards the helper, and place your hand on the shoulder or the breast.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and take the cloth, pull on the helper and the arm, so that the arm is straight up, as long as nothing prevents it or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use a splint, and place on the fracture a broader and stronger splint than others, and leave two spaces between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes beyond the fracture on both sides.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then tighten the splints, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter about the fracture, stronger and less apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the position of the splints and their tightening, as we have said, when you return the broken member to its place, and doubt whether the abscess is hot, leave it bound for up to seven days, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then, each day for three days, observe the wound, that it does not become inflamed or swollen, and let no movement come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accident occurs, then do not release it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and place the dislocated joint in a soft pillow of equal-length wool, and observe each hour during the day or night, to ensure that the shape of the limb is not altered, and the ligaments do not relax.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if it is healed by the virtue of medicine, and given food that we have mentioned above, in such a way that the food is first subtle.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to recover, it will be significant.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	and it is customary that the aid and leg should be healed over forty days in all.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then it should be dislocated and treated with baths and medicines suitable for the joint to be healed.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the contraction is severe and swollen, it may take longer to loosen, sometimes days or even months.
de la brisure du bras	of the dislocation of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fossa," one smaller and the other succeeding to the pouch.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is the one that is opposite, towards the smaller bone.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	should the larger "fossa" break only, or both, then reassemble them together if possible.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the smaller bones break, their restoration and healing is easier.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the bones are broken, if healing is poor, it becomes more painful than when they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bones are broken, it is sufficient to extend them slightly and make them even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is a large, deep wound, then more force must be applied to tighten it.
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extends it on the cushion, placing the palm higher than the others, and the small fingers lower, crossing the patient over itself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any pain.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then extend the healers' hands to the side of their hand, or to the joint, and other ministers to the others above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set it even with the eyes, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture each piece is set in its place, and if there is none that holds the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then doing as we have said above, on both sides of the bone.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the wound rupture, I have spoken of it in the specific chapter;
si pren la cure.	then take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of restoration appear abscesses, I apply a bandage made of rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and I cover it gently, until the abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	Then remove the bandage, and apply the plaster of fine-milled powder with plenty of egg, then place the pins, and let the pin from the break be even stronger, a little broader than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it must have six pins or arms in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	so that the break is in one of the bones, or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and it is held tighter on the fracture than elsewhere, and less as it heals, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the bandages on the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or rough.
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and the thread, from which it is held, should be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after no days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if no ill accident befalls the limb, such as itching which may come upon it, then you should apply hot water to the limb until the itching is soothed.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the member not be squeezed tightly at rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then repeat the exercise, and if the ligaments become slack and the bones lose their alignment, or any similar thing, address it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the tightness prevents any movement in the limb, because it is too tight, then you should loosen it a little and leave it for some days until the stiffness improves, and then tighten it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then he should be released in twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	if troubled, then tie his hands to his chest, and make sure his collarbones are even, and guard against movement and gesture, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is healed in 30 days or 45 days, and by chance in 10 days, according to the combinations and complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the dislocation of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that on the back of the hand and at the joints there are often small breaks, and it brings only pain many times over.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the hand bone is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient cuts across it and holds it straight before him equally.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then he places his hand on the extended board, extending the broken bones of the minister and aligning them equally until they are properly joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and applies a poultice and hot compresses, if abscesses do not form, then he places a piece of salt according to the size of the wound.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and is wrapped in a cloth drape.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is near the stomach of the plant, make a ball of cloth and instruct the patient to press it against the broken place.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then stretch a long drape, and make the heart-shaped cloth as tight as the palm of the hand, and tighten it, as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the edge, then you must place a stick across it and another underneath in the sole, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly all around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the bones.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	If any of us experience a break, and it is the joints, place it evenly, as appropriate;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and tighten with the palm, and if you see that a small, straight cloth raises the break without moving;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the break is in other joints, like in the example or any other, place it evenly and bind it with the healthy finger after;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	you hold them all in place with a tight grip, as much as possible, or you put a splint on it, just like you would;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and placement of hot abscesses, and protect those who come near it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	from the broken hipbone
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	the bones of the foot are often broken, and it is clearly visible when they heal in front and behind;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is when they are bound together above the break and another is placed below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then extends each limb evenly to both sides.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the fracture is through the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the hipbone, one should bind it towards the wrist, and the others below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, then the ligaments around the knee should be relaxed and the extension should be downward.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then aligns the bone with both hands, evenly according to its natural shape, and then applies the splint, binding it firmly in place without causing new damage.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it soothe down, then return to your work and treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The bandage is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	You should wrap around the fracture a bandage hard and tightly doubled in two or three layers, then remove any excess, and turn the leg until the heel reaches the root of the toe, and insert a long thread between the calf and the leg, below the knee joint, and bring the end up over the top.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn to the leg and shin the bandage, then place the splint across it, and put a stick over the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then use the eighth part of a cloth, soft between the leg and shin, to apply an even strain, then begin to tie three turns or four over the splint.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and as you go higher over the splint, strain it less.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then take the two threads that you have woven between the leg and shin, and tie three stitches on top, then return to the other side, under the knee with the thread, until you reach the foot.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and hold it steady, if it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, and it will not become abscessed or swollen or any other thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens that it disconnects, and the swelling comes back as it has many times before, as we have said numerous times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are fragments of bone that grip, it is prudent to extract them if possible;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot extract them, then it is necessary to break the joint and pull forcefully;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and the treatment is as we have said, as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And never should the foot be broken in this way with stars, as is done in the aid or arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	However, this restoration done in this way does not please the sick.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the foot is restored in 7 to 10 days, or perhaps a little less or a little more, depending on the variety of complexes.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the alley of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	You know that in the alley of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, even if it is only a crack or a hole, it affects every wound, and without a wound, and everyone feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is when everything is put back in place as it should be, as long as it can be moved together.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then apply the plaster, and put a round stick, if you need it, and hold it as appropriate, then correct all the positions that we have mentioned in other fractures, such as a hot abscess or any similar thing.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	if each case requires it, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	from the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Knowing that the leg has two bones, of which one is called the "right" and the other is called the "shank";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and it has a similar fracture as the arm, and its restoration is the same as that of the arm, equally difficult; and if both bones are broken together, the leg can turn in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, they return to their original position.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain, and one can see it well.
et torne desoz.	and turn it inside out.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then apply extension, and set it even, and tie the stars equally.
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	But nevertheless, it is necessary that the broken bone be ugly, and there are multiple pieces, so the extension should be less severe and lighter.
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and make it straight according to its strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your task, take two strips of cloth as thick as the leg, extending from one side to the other, and make them quite long from the thigh down to the ankle.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap it in two bands of cloth, both above and below, and tie it tightly in the middle, and with this binding, the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and thus it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and no one should administer any binding around the length of the leg, and if it is of cloth, they place the leg to prevent movement, and properly make this at the fracture where there is an injury.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each part of the leg to see if there is a hot abscess or any other accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if you treat it while it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones of the foot can be fractured and the two small bones, and there is no treatment that applies in all cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if a bone is broken deeply, and you see the bones pressing against each other, causing the patient to lie with great pain on the ground, as if they wanted to move, then place your foot on their leg, holding the bones in their original position, and press until they return to their proper place.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then apply a splint and bandages, place a small, flat board under the belly of the leg with two holes, fasten it to the leg, wrap it tightly with cloth and other materials as needed.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three or four days have passed, if you loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones even, either broken or discolored.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if any of the two bones are broken, restore them as we have said about the bones of the hand.
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then take the broken bone and make it into a splint according to the length of the bone, and make it slightly wider, then place the foot under the board that I have mentioned, and tie it securely.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more broken bones, take a splint for each bone according to its length, wrapped in a cloth, and tie the board under the foot.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and so it is placed on the upper part of the table, with the belly facing down, if it is done well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, when we have spoken.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and attend to each of these accidents as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Regarding the fracture of the bone in the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bones of a woman's natural structure are broken and the swelling increases, then incline her to one side, leaning on her back, and hold her from behind.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the wound with a cloth saturated with honey and also add as much as I can.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then turn the woman around, gently pressing her back, and then pull out the cloth, until it reaches the wound's entrance, and return the bone with the honey.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, remove the cloth, and once she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven days or so.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	if the fracture is healed, and you notice, take a bladder of barley, tie it to the opening with a cane, and pour all the contents into the wound.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the flame until the bladder is filled inside.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	nature will heal the broken ones.
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then fill it with cotton and leave it thus for no days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bones of a man or woman are broken, restore them thus as we have said regarding the hip bone.
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these fractures are not hidden from him who devotes his study and skill to them, and listen to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For fracture indicates various dispositions towards the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	understand then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the staff, when it is broken, take a goose throat and blow the staff;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap rags around it, leave for three days or until healing is complete.
de brisure avec plaie	from fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is important for someone with a fracture and a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone in the shin or shoulder or similar, to be treated immediately, so that the healing process, as we have described, can begin.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but there is still hardness from the bruise, if you have no other remedy, then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour or on the same day that the abscess appears.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscess opens on its own, let it heal undisturbed for a new day or two, until the abscess is calm, and do not touch it even on the third or fourth day, or you would bring about a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible beneath the skin, you must gently place your hands on it, with small extensions.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension does not appear even in your hands, then reset this instrument which is of iron, having seven or eight inches in length, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound.
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this reason, it is necessary to use a mirror so that he moistens three or four times, according to what he needs in each break treatment.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and it should be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend to the pressure on the limb at your discretion, and it is sharp in front and thick in the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called a "palainche", so it is necessary that the curved bone be placed on the visible head of the bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and the bottle should be held once, as it returns, and so that one is even with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, you must hold the head of the bone until the instrument has a firm grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, take a suitable instrument, such as a scalpel or forceps, in your power.
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then take that which is delayed in the bone, of hardness and small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterward, knowing that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If you make it stay in its place, then moisten the cloth with black vinegar, and apply it properly.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not place any wax or other substance on the wound that would prevent air from reaching it, as it will cause putrefaction and decay.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer steriles when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound exposed, and clean the surrounding area, according to the size of the wound, and be careful not to constrict the wound with any fragments.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times they have done this foolishly, and brought upon the patient death or great corruption several times.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and so the bindings should be softer and more gentle than others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is severe or large, and you doubt that a complication will arise, as we have said, and it brings pain instead of healing, if it is not suitable to place anything on it.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap it around, instead of bandages, with hard cloth, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is bowing or sinking, then remove what you have applied to it, and apply a healing dressing for wounds, such as a four-part ointment or similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it remains swollen and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be separated in such a way that the bow of the joint gently moves downwards.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if this persists for a long time, it cannot heal but repeatedly returns to the bowed state, knowing that there are small fragments of bone, so it is necessary that you clean the wound thoroughly and remove all these misplaced fragments causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula forms in its place or any other type of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it according to what is said in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when a bone is broken and opens up on the limb, such as the bone of the shin or the shoulder, or other similar bones of the large limbs, do not pull it, for in many cases it leads to gangrene, but let it be until it rots.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	if, after twenty or thirty days, the wound has healed, then treat it if possible.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if it cannot be treated, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	burns that come from the solder
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often encounter after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near a joint, and the sight of the misaligned limb is a sad thing.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance cannot perform the natural movements of its limbs.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Beware therefore, if this happens to us:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if he administers astringent medicines such as aloe, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, akebia, and similar ones, without pressing any of these things or all together, and conserves them with astringent wine or with abundant egg white or with ash.
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and places them on the wound in compresses, tightens them well, and does not untie them for several days.
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then dislocate it, and begin again with a new one, until the knots are broken.
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you stretch it on a well-made plank;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of the plank is that it removes all swelling from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the knot has become hard as stone, it must be broken, if possible, and the excess removed, exposing the surface.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	You must cut it with no rasping, as long as it is fresh, and treat it while it is clean.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the weak member after treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is healed and the limb remains weak and delicate, it occurs for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	because one is due to it being constrained too tightly and not constrained as it should be;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because it has too many constraints and cannot attain the normal movement of the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	for from many irritations;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or due to too great movements, not staying in its proper time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because it has little blood in its body, it becomes weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat, and make the body firm, until the blood begins to multiply within him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer baths, and give joy and comfort;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then place lead on the affected member, so that the lead attracts great pain, and often raise it with cold water, until the pain subsides in the member.
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The twisted member after health.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the member is twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the member is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function.
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	do not believe the fools who say we must break the member from the very beginning, and many foolish practices have been done in our land.
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this work is blameful, and brings great harm, and sometimes death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	However, if the nodations (swelling) and torture are fresh, they should be treated with hot water or cooked herbs that have soothing properties, such as fennel, roots, melilot, and similar things.
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and apply the soothing plaster, well-prepared as it should be, and take the resin of fennel, and preserve it with gelin fat or sesame oil, and apply the plaster.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	You take fatty substances, crush them finely with collyria and similar medications that ease inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never should the dislocation be rubbed continuously and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow the limb to move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the swelling is inflamed and hardened, like stone, then it needs to be opened with iron, if necessary covering it with cloth, with a delicate incisor lightly.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and apply compression and study the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur from a joint moving out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs due to no apparent cause, it is necessary to attempt to bring the limb back to its normal position immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	Because if treatment is delayed, the swelling can increase, and it may be necessary to apply pressure firmly to the site.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	because it is not necessary to move it with force when it is swollen.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	often causes pain and other discomforts;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	however, when this happens, if it makes the patient healthier, then leave it until the abscess is completely healed.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the affected limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as the cure comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder joint all the way to the foot.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It is first necessary that the jaws be dislocated slightly, and both dislocations are according to two manners:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	when they are slightly separated from their sockets, and softened somewhat;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are entirely dislocated, hanging down towards the chin, and draining saliva from the mouth so that it cannot be held closed, nor can he close his lips, and he drools while speaking.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is minor, it often returns to its proper position through various dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is entirely and completely dislocated, then it must be reset immediately, without delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the physician places his thumb on the patient's head and pulls it slightly with the root of his hand into the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, thus dislocating it by half.
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two hands should be prepared equally.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instructs the patient to soften his jaws and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he should equalize the pressure, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if they return to their place, especially when both jaws are involved, then apply hot water and oil, gently bringing them back together.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	I shall not try to bring it back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back evenly, and the patient's mouth is closed without too much difficulty, apply moistened cloth bandages made of rose oil and wax, then gently bind them with soft cords.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and have the patient sleep on their back, with their legs between two cushions, so that they do not move to the left or right, nor strive for anything more, but gently press meat into them until the pains are gone and the jaws are still.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then massage it gently, and do not try to open the mouth for eating or drinking until the jaw is well-nurtured and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be brought back to their proper position within an hour and are not aligned properly, then fever and severe pain may occur, as well as abdominal distension, and possibly pure bile vomiting.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is destruction;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and often leads to the death of those whom it befalls within seven days.
de la forcelle	De la forcelle" translates directly to "of the
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot stay in place from either side within the continuation of it and is dislocated neither outside nor inside, and it causes great pain.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, extending their arms.
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the joint back into your palm, and it will return.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then apply the plaster and bind it tight, and hold it fast.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the joint that is near the shoulder cannot be dislocated.
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does not move, and if it does not dislocate even once, then put it back in place as we have said.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply the plaster and bind it tight, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and so, itself is brought back to the shoulder joint, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	You know that the shoulder is injured in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one is when it is injured at the part of the shoulder blade towards the back;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the part of the lesser curve;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and by chance, it is injured at the upper part, and this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and do not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and do not dislocate inside for the nerves.
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and often dislocate away from the axis, especially for those who have little strength, as this causes them great pain.
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	for those who have enough strength, the dislocation occurs gently, and it returns gently.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And occasionally, no matter the person, they might experience a bruise or fracture, and an abscess of heat forms in the shoulder, and they think it is dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	It is therefore necessary that you test it, as long as you are certain.
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And dislocation is recognized when it moves towards the joint, and makes a distinction between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their manifest diversity between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find at the top of the shoulder a pit, and by pressing on the joint, the top of the shoulder feels as if it were one.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring their hand back to its normal position, nor make any movement.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated at the top and not hidden away, for you will feel it clearly through touch;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this method of dislocation is not only to be used when it is fresh, or if the patient is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the healer places his hand on the patient's head, then puts his palms underneath the affected area, and pulls the joint upwards with strength towards the joint.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the healer lifts his hand, extending it upwards, then places it underneath.
si venra hastanment.	if illness comes.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if illness does not come as we have said, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and apply it gently and soothingly, such as with an infusion of fennel and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let it be applied.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then the patient should be placed on their back, and a soft cloth of equal thickness should be placed beneath them, neither too loose nor too tight, then place a pillow under their heel and gently lift the head from the shoulder, and pull the hand of the ill person.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and other ministers should tie the patient's head to prevent movement.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	the shoulder now returns, and if it is dislocated, reset it according to this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and make sure that the presence of someone at home is more significant than the patient's illness;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and be straight against the side, and pull the patient's shoulder blade away from the spine, and lift the blade upwards, so that the patient's arm hangs down.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and other assistants take hold of the patient's hand below the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, and any heavy object causes no discomfort, then the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And it is also adjusted in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and place a long stick in the ground, so that the end is also bright like a pestle, and not too thick or too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then the patient is placed on their back, but with soft cloth over them, and the pain should be from a long wound;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then, stretch his hand downward from another direction, forming a new angle, and the joint will return to its place steadily.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return for all the things we have said, make this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take a small piece of cloth from both arms, broad and long enough, that the end can be pushed completely through the wound, according to this shape.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then wrap over the wound with a cloth from above, so that it does not hurt the patient, and then insert it through the wound of the ill person.
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	And stretch one arm over the thigh, holding the shoulder on the thigh, and raise the arm up to the top of the hand; then place the arm on the palm of a wide knife, and extend the hand downwards, leaving the body hanging from the other side.
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint moves back now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is dislocated, in any way, it is necessary that you place under the limb a spear of equal wool, then apply the plaster made from powdered chalk, with incense and eagle's egg, over the entire shoulder area, then stretch the limb away from the body, and secure the bandage on the plaster, and press the hand to the collarbone, so that the hands remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he move slightly, as long as the limb is comfortable, because it will heal more quickly.
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then move more after two or seven days, and move it again.
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is frozen and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is stuck due to moisture or any other cause, it is necessary that you apply heat at three points, as described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and after seven days the dislocation persists, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot raise his arm above his head, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is either compressed, stretched, or softened.
